Salah — Prayer

8 min
The Ruling and Procedure for Sujud al-Sahw
Ruling and procedure for sujud al-sahw with dalil and internal disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that sujud al-sahw is wajib, identify its evidence from the Prophet's practice, and explain the required procedure including the dispute on reciting salat and supplication.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw is wajib, proven by the Prophet's practice, and its full procedure includes two prostrations, tashahhud, and salam, with the chosen view adding salat and supplication.

In the previous lesson, we learned the causes that trigger sujud al-sahw. Now we turn to its specific implementation: how many prostrations, what is recited, and the evidence that establishes this. The Hanafi school holds that sujud al-sahw is wajib (obligatory), not merely sunnah, and its procedure is based on the direct practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Understand that sujud al-sahw consists of two prostrations and that the Hanafi school rules it as wajib (obligatory). The text states 'wa yajib sajdatani' (and two prostrations are obligatory).
Wajib means omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw), but the prayer remains valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence (dalil) is the Prophet's action: he prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness while sitting after salam. This is a hadith ahad (single-transmitter narration).
The text says 'because the Prophet ﷺ prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates wujub (obligation) when there is no evidence to the contrary (qarinah) suggesting recommendation (nadb). Here, no such qarinah exists, so the ruling is wajib.
The category of the dalil: thubut is zanni (since ahad), but dalala is qati (clear meaning).
4
Outline the procedure
After the final salam, one sits, performs two prostrations with the same postures as prayer prostrations, then sits again for tashahhud and salam. The original tashahhud and salam are 'raised' (i.e., replaced by the sujud).
The text mentions 'with tashahhud and salam' because the previous ones are no longer effective.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
There is a difference on whether to recite salat upon the Prophet and supplication (dua) in the sitting after sujud. The 'chosen view' (al-mukhtar) includes them, while some scholars (e.g., Qadi Khan, Zahir al-Din) recommend caution by reciting them in both sittings (before and after sujud).
Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi is quoted as supporting the chosen view. The practical difference is minimal; both views are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب (سجدتان) لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم مسجد سجدتين للسهو، وهو جالس بعد التسليم وعمل به الأكابر من الصحابة والتابعين بتشهد وتسليم لما ذكرنا ويأتي فيه بالصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والدعاء على المختار لترك (واجب) (بتقديم أو تأخير أو زيادة أو نقص لا سنة لأن الصلاة لا توصف بالنقصان على الإطلاق بترك سنة وأما الفرض فيفوت بفواته الأصل لا الوصف) 6 فعلى القول بالرفض تكون القعدة التي قرأ فيها التشهد هي الفرض وعلى القول بعدم تكون واجبة لأداء التشهد، والصحيح أن الصلاة صحيحة، ويجب سجود السهو قوله: (فيفترض إعادته ويجب إعادة التشهد والسلام قوله (ويجب) لا حاجة إليه للاستغناء عنه بكلام المصنف. قوله : (سجدتان) كسجدتين الصلاة يجلس بينهما مفترشاً، ويكبر في الوضع، والرفع، ويأتي فيهما بتسبيح السجود وكل ذلك مسنون، وعن بعضهم يندب أن يقول سبحان من لا ينام، ولا يسهو، وهو لائق بالحال، فيجمع بينه وبين التسبح فلو اقتصر على سجدة واحدة لا يكون آتياً بالواجب، ولا شيء عليه إن كان ساهياً، وإن تعمده يأثم، وفي البحر لو سها في سجود السهو لا يسجد لهذا السهو، وفي المضمرات لو سها في سجود السهو عمل بالتحري ولا يجب عليه سجود السهو لئلا يلزم التسلسل، ولأنه يغتفر في التابع، ما لا يغتفر في المتبوع، وحكي أن محمد بن الحسن قال للكسائي ابن خالته : لم لا تشتغل بالفقه، فقال : من أحكم علماً يهديه إلى سائر العلوم، فقال محمد أنا ألقي عليك شيئاً من مسائل القفه فتخرج لي جوابه من النحو قال : نعم، فقال محمد: ما تقول فيمن سها في سجود السهو فتفكر ساعة، ثم قال : لا سهو عليه، فقال من أي باب من النحو أخرجت هذا الجواب، فقال من باب أن المصغر لا يصغر فتعجب من فطنته .اهـ. قوله وعمل به الأكابر ) أي فلم يكن منسوخاً، والمقصود إقامة الدليل على من قال بغير ذلك. قوله : بتشهد وتسليم هما وأجبان بعد سجود السهود لأن الأولين ارتفعا بالسجود قوله : ( بالصلاة على النبي ( الباء للتعدية. قال فخر الإسلام : انه اختاره عامة أهل النظر من مشايخنا، وهو المختار عندنا وذكر قاضيخان، وظهير الدين أن الأحوط الإتيان بذلك في القعدتين واختاره الطحاوي، وقيل عندهما يصلي في الأولى وعند محمد في الثانية، وفي المفيد قولهما أصح
And it is obligatory (two prostrations) because the Prophet ﷺ prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness while sitting after the salam, and the great among the Companions and Followers acted upon it, with tashahhud and salam according to what we mentioned. And according to the chosen view, he recites the salat upon the Prophet and supplication. For leaving a wajib, whether by advancement, delay, addition, or deficiency—not a sunnah, because prayer is not described as deficient absolutely due to leaving a sunnah. As for the fard, it is lost by losing its essence, not its description...
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage continues the hashiya, now focusing on the specific ruling that sujud al-sahw consists of two prostrations. The proof (dalil) is the Prophet's action: he prostrated two prostrations while sitting after performing salam. The companions and followers practiced this, indicating it is not abrogated. The author then discusses the procedure: after the two prostrations, one sits and performs tashahhud and salam again because the original tashahhud and salam were raised (i.e., replaced) by the sujud. There is a difference of opinion on whether to send blessings on the Prophet and make supplication during the sitting after sujud al-sahw; the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is to do so. Various scholars mention the rulings: if he omits one prostration intentionally, he sins; if forgetful, nothing is required. If one forgets in the sujud al-sahw itself, no additional sujud is needed to avoid infinite regress. The author also relates a story where Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani tests al-Kisa'i with a fiqh question to which al-Kisa'i answers using grammar principles, demonstrating that a forgetfulness in sujud al-sahw does not require another sujud. The passage ends with a discussion on whether to perform tashahhud and salam after the first prostration or the second, with various opinions.

Key Terms
السجدتان (al-sajdatani): The two prostrations of sujud al-sahw.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith during the sitting in prayer.
السلام (al-salam): The closing salutation of the prayer.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred position among Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence for sujud al-sahw consisting of two prostrations?
A) A Quranic verse
B) The Prophet's action
C) Ijma of the companions
D) Qiyas on the prayer prostrations

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib, consists of two prostrations performed after salam, and the chosen Hanafi procedure includes tashahhud, salam, and reciting salat and supplication.

Sujud al-Sahw for Leaving a Wajib: Original vs. Non-Original Acts
Explains that sujud al-sahw is required for leaving a wajib of the original prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between original wajib acts and non-original wajib acts in prayer, and apply the ruling on sujud al-sahw accordingly.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw is required only for leaving an original wajib of the prayer, not for every mistake.

Many students assume that any mistake in prayer triggers sujud al-sahw. However, the Hanafi school draws a careful distinction: only the omission of an original wajib (wajib asli) necessitates sujud al-sahw. Non-original wajib acts - such as the order of recitation, basmalah, or delaying sujud al-tilawah - may not require it, and there is even disagreement within the school. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi refines the general rule and presents the different positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the opening phrase: 'For leaving a wajib.' Note the qualification: 'from the original wajib acts of the prayer.' This immediately restricts the scope.
Original wajib acts are those inherently part of the prayer structure, e.g., tashahhud, salam, reciting al-Fatihah and a surah.
2
Distinguish original vs. non-original
Identify the examples given: 'order of tilawah' and 'basmalah' are non-original. Understand why they are excluded.
The order of recitation (fatihah before surah) is a wajib but not 'asli'; the basmalah is not an original wajib.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on non-original wajib
Note the disagreement: al-Zayla'i says sujud al-sahw is required for delaying sujud al-tilawah; al-Tajnisi says it is not. Determine the basis of each view.
Al-Zayla'i considers delaying sujud al-tilawah as a delay of a wajib from its proper place; al-Tajnisi sees it as non-original and thus not requiring sujud.
4
Apply the rule to specific scenarios
Work through the examples: reciting an ayah from a surah before al-Fatihah, repeating al-Fatihah, leaving the surah and remembering during al-Fatihah. For each, decide whether sujud al-sahw is needed.
The text states that beginning with a surah before al-Fatihah requires sujud al-sahw for delaying the wajib (tartib).
5
Note the mufta bihi
Understand that the relied-upon position in the school is to require sujud al-sahw for leaving an original wajib. For non-original wajib, the more cautious view (followed by al-Zayla'i) is to perform sujud.
The text cites al-Fath and al-Muhit as supporting the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that leaving most of al-Fatihah requires sujud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( لترك واجب) أي من واجبات الصلاة الأصلية فخرج واجب ترتيب التلاوة، واختلف في تأخير . سجود التلاوة عن التلاوة، وجزم في التجنيس بعدم وجوب السهو فيه لأنه ليس بواجب أصلي في الصلاة ولا يجب بترك التسمية على ظاهر المذهب، وجزم الزيلعي بوجوب السهو لها، ويجب بترك آية من الإمام، وبترك أكثر الفاتحة عندهما، وبه جزم في الفتح تبعاً للمحيط، ومن الواجب تقديم الفاتحة على السورة ، وأن لا يؤخر السورة عنها بمقدار أداء ركن فلو بدأ بآية من السورة، ثم تذكر الفاتحة يقرؤها، ويعيد السورة ويسجد للسهو لتأخير الواجب عن محله، ولو كرر الفاتحة، أو بعضها في إحدى الأوليين قبل السورة سجد للسهو، ولو ترك السورة فتذكرها في الفاتحة عند
His saying: 'For leaving a wajib' means from the original wajib acts of the prayer, so the wajib of the order of tilawah is excluded. And there is disagreement regarding delaying sujud al-tilawah from the recitation. He decided in al-Tajnisi that sujud al-sahw is not required for it because it is not an original wajib in the prayer. And it is not required for leaving the basmalah according to the apparent madhhab. Al-Zayla'i decided that sujud al-sahw is required for it. And it is required for leaving an ayah from the imam, and for leaving most of al-Fatihah according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and he decided this in al-Fath following al-Muhit. And it is wajib to precede al-Fatihah over the surah, and not to delay the surah after it by an amount that would constitute performing a rukn. So if he begins with an ayah of the surah, then remembers al-Fatihah, he recites it and repeats the surah and performs sujud al-sahw for delaying the wajib from its place. And if he repeats al-Fatihah or part of it in one of the first two rak'ahs before the surah, he should perform sujud al-sahw. And if he leaves the surah and then remembers it during al-Fatihah...
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage refines the ruling that sujud al-sahw is required for leaving a wajib, specifying that it applies only to the original wajib acts of the prayer (wajibat al-salat al-asliyyah), not to non-original acts like the order of tilawah (recitation) or the basmalah. There is a difference of opinion: some scholars like al-Zayla'i require sujud al-sahw for delaying sujud al-tilawah, while others (like the author of al-Tajnisi) do not. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that sujud al-sahw is required for leaving an ayah from the imam or most of al-Fatihah, as per Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Specific examples are given: if one recites an ayah from a surah before al-Fatihah, he must return to al-Fatihah, then repeat the surah, and perform sujud al-sahw for delaying the wajib. Similarly, if one repeats al-Fatihah before the surah, he performs sujud al-sahw. The passage ends mid-sentence with the case of leaving the surah and remembering it during al-Fatihah, which is incomplete.

Key Terms
واجبات الصلاة الأصلية (wajibat al-salat al-asliyyah): The wajib acts that are inherently part of the prayer structure, such as tashahhud, salam, reciting al-Fatihah and a surah.
ترتيب التلاوة (tartib al-tilawah): The order of recitation, specifically that al-Fatihah must precede the surah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following mistakes would require sujud al-sahw according to most Hanafi authorities?
A) Reciting a surah without basmalah
B) Delaying sujud al-tilawah by one second
C) Reciting an ayah from the surah before al-Fatihah
D) Omitting the qunut in witr

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib only when an original wajib of the prayer is left; non-original wajib like order of tilawah are disputed and require caution.

Ruling on Sajdat al-Sahw for Omitting a Wajib
Explaining the obligation and proof of sajdat al-sahw for omitting a wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-sahw when a wajib is omitted, cite the primary proof from the Prophet's action, and explain the distinction between fard and wajib in this context.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-sahw is wajib for omitting a wajib; it does not invalidate the prayer because a fard cannot be compensated.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses the obligation of prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) when a wajib element of the prayer is left out. The author establishes the ruling with the Prophetic practice and clarifies the crucial Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib. Understanding this distinction is essential to determine whether an error requires repetition of the prayer or simply compensation through prostrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is sajdat al-sahw when a wajib is omitted. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school.
The term 'wajib' here means obligatory but with a lower epistemological certainty than fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him)who performed two prostrations for forgetfulness while sitting after the taslim. This was practiced by the Companions and Successors.
The dalil is a fi'li (action) of the Prophet, supplemented by tacit approval.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent performance and command indicate obligation (wujub). The fact that he did not order a repeat of the prayer shows that the omitted element is not a fard but a wajib.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action in the context of teaching indicates wujub unless proven otherwise.
4
Distinguish fard and wajib
A fard is established by qat'i evidence and its omission invalidates the prayer. A wajib is established by zanni evidence and its omission requires sajdat al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and has practical implications for compensation.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion regarding the first tashahhud: some considered it fard, but the correct view (al-mukhtar) is that it is wajib, so omission requires sajdat al-sahw rather than repetition.
The ikhtilaf is resolved by the principle that the Prophet's prostration for forgetfulness indicates the omitted act is not a fard.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the prayer remains valid and sajdat al-sahw is wajib.
This is the position of the majority of Hanafi scholars and is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب (سجدتان) لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم سجد سجدتين للسهو، وهو جالس بعد التسليم وعمل به الأكابر من الصحابة والتابعين بتشهد وتسليم لما ذكرنا ويأتي فيه بالصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والدعاء على المختار لترك (واجب) بتقديم أو تأخير أو زيادة أو نقص لا سنة لأن الصلاة لا توصف بالنقصان على الإطلاق بترك سنة وأما الفرض فيفوت بفواته الأصل لا الوصف ، فعلى القول بالرفض تكون القعدة التي قرأ فيها التشهد هي الفرض وعلى القول بعدمه تكون واجبة لأداء التشهد، والصحيح أن الصلاة صحيحة، ويجب سجود السهو قوله: (فيفترض إعادته ويجب إعادة التشهد والسلام قوله (ويجب) لا حاجة إليه للاستغناء عنه بكلام المصنف. قوله : (سجدتان) كسجدتين الصلاة يجلس بينهما مفترشاً، ويكبر في الوضع، والرفع، ويأتي فيهما بتسبيح السجود وكل ذلك مسنون، وعن بعضهم يندب أن يقول سبحان من لا ينام، ولا يسهو، وهو لائق بالحال، فيجمع بينه وبين التسبح فلو اقتصر على سجدة واحدة لا يكون آتياً بالواجب، ولا شيء عليه إن كان ساهياً، وإن تعمده يأثم، وفي البحر لو سها في سجود السهو لا يسجد لهذا السهو، وفي المضمرات لو سها في سجود السهو عمل بالتحري ولا يجب عليه سجود السهو لئلا يلزم التسلسل، ولأنه يغتفر في التابع، ما لا يغتفر في المتبوع، وحكي أن محمد بن الحسن قال للكسائي ابن خالته : لم لا تشتغل بالفقه، فقال : من أحكم علماً يهديه إلى سائر العلوم، فقال باب أن المصغر لا يصغر فتعجب من فطنته .اهـ. قوله وعمل به الأكابر ) أي فلم يكن منسوخاً، والمقصود إقامة الدليل على من قال بغير ذلك. قوله : بتشهد وتسليم هما وأجبان بعد سجود السهود لأن الأولين ارتفعا بالسجود قوله : ( بالصلاة على النبي ( الباء للتعدية. قال فخر الإسلام : انه اختاره عامة أهل النظر من مشايخنا، وهو المختار عندنا وذكر قاضيخان، وظهير الدين أن الأحوط الإتيان بذلك في القعدتين واختاره الطحاوي، وقيل عندهما يصلي في الأولى وعند محمد في الثانية، وفي المفيد قولهما أصح قوله : ( لترك واجب) أي من واجبات الصلاة الأصلية فخرج واجب ترتيب التلاوة، واختلف في تأخير . سجود التلاوة عن التلاوة، وجزم في التجنيس بعدم وجوب السهو فيه لأنه ليس بواجب أصلي في الصلاة ولا يجب بترك التسمية على ظاهر المذهب، وجزم الزيلعي بوجوب السهو لها، ويجب بترك آية من الإمام، وبترك أكثر الفاتحة عندهما، وبه جزم في الفتح تبعاً للمحيط، ومن الواجب تقديم الفاتحة على السورة ، وأن لا يؤخر السورة عنها بمقدار أداء ركن فلو بدأ بآية من السورة، ثم تذكر الفاتحة يقرؤها، ويعيد السورة ويسجد للسهو لتأخير الواجب عن محله، ولو كرر الفاتحة، أو بعضها في إحدى الأوليين قبل السورة سجد للسهو، ولو ترك السورة فتذكرها في الركوع، أو بعد الرفع منه قبل السجود فإنه يعود ويقرأ السورة ويعيد الركوع، وعليه السهو لأنه بقراءة السورة وقعت فرضاً فيرتفض الركوع حتى لو لم يعده فسدت صلاته وكذا إذا قرأ السورة وسها عن الفاتحة، ثم تذكر، فإنه يعود ويقرأ الفاتحة ويعيد السورة، ويعيد الركوع وعليه السهو لما قلنا بخلاف ما لو تذكر القنوت في الركوع، فإنه لا يعود، ولا يقنت فيه لفوات محله، ولو عاد وقنت لم يرتفض ركوعه لأن القنوت لا يقع فرضاً، فلا يرتفض به الفرض، ويسجد للسهو على كل حال ليترك الواجب أو تأخيره ولو قرأ آية في الركوع، أو السجود، أو القومة فعليه السهو، ولو قرأ في القعود ان قرأ قبل التشهد في القعدتين فعليه السهو لترك واجب الابتداء بالتشهد أول الجلوس وإن قرأ بعد التشهد فإن كان في الأول فعليه السهو لتأخير الواجب، وهو وصل القيام بالفراغ من التشهد وإن كان في الأخير فلا سهو عليه لعدم ترك واجب لأنه موسع له في الدعاء، والثناء بعده فيه والقراءة تشتمل عليهما، ولو قرأ التشهد مرتين في القعدة الأخيرة، أو تشهد قائماً أو راكعاً، أو ساجداً لا سهو عليه. منية المصلي لكن إن قرأ في قيام الأولى قبل الفاتحة أو في الثانية بعد السورة أو في الأخيرتين مطلقاً لا سهو عليه، وإن قرأ في الأوليين بعد الفاتحة والسورة أو في الثانية قبل الفاتحة، السجود لأنه أخر واجباً وإيضاحه في ابن أمير حاج، ولو ترك التشهد في القعدتين أو بعضه لزمه السجود في ظاهر الرواية لأنه ذكر واحد منظوم فترك بعضه كترك كله، ومنها قنوت الوتر، وتكبيرته فلو تركها وجب السهو على ما رجحه في البحر، ومنها جهر الإمام فيما يجهر فيه، والإسرار في محله مطلقاً، واختلف في القدر الموجب للسهو، والأصح أنه قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين، لأن اليسير من الجهر والإخفاء لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه، وما روي من الآية أحياناً في السرية، فهو لبيان أن القراءة مشروعة فيما يسمع فيه ورده في 6 وجب عليه أنه كان يسمع الفتح بأن القراءة معلومة قبل ذلك لأنه كان يجهر بالقراءة في الصلوات كلها حتى نزل قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تجهر بصلاتك ولا تخافت بها﴾ [الإسراء : ١١٠] فتعين أن ذلك لبيان الجواز أي بیان جواز الجهر بهذا القدر لأن الاحتراز عن الجهر بالكلية متعسر لا سيما عند مبادىء التنفسات ، فإنه غالباً يظهر الصوت .اهـ. قال شرف الأئمة لا خلاف أنه لو جهر بأكثر الفاتحة فيما يخافت ، ثم ذكر يتمها سراً، ولو خافت بأكثرها فيما يجهر قال شمس الأئمة: قياس مسائل الجامع أنه يؤمر بالإعادة، وقد نصوا أن وجوب الإسرار مختص بالقراءة، فلو جهر بالأذكار، والأدعية، ولو تشهدا لا سهو عليه وعلم بما ذكرناه صور التقديم والتأخير، والزيادة والنقص. قوله : (لما (روينا من أنه سجد سجدتين للسهو . قوله : (وإن تكرر ( سواء كان من جنس، أو من جنسين، فلا يجب عليه أكثر من سجدتين بالإجماع، ولا يرد ما لو سجد للسهو، ثم
And two prostrations are obligatory because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness while sitting after the taslim, and the great ones among the Companions and Successors acted upon it with tashahhud and taslim for what we mentioned, and it includes sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and supplication according to the chosen view, due to leaving a wajib by advancement or delay or increase or decrease, not a sunnah because the prayer is not described as deficient absolutely by leaving a sunnah. As for the fard, it is lost by the loss of its essence, not its description. So according to the view of cancelation, the sitting in which he recited the tashahhud is the fard, and according to the view of non-cancelation, it is wajib for performing the tashahhud, and the correct view is that the prayer is valid and prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
The passage begins by stating the obligation (wajib) of two prostrations for forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) when a wajib of the prayer is omitted. The proof is the Prophet's action. The author details that the prostrations are performed sitting after the taslim, with tashahhud and taslim, and include sending blessings and supplication according to the preferred view. The cause is leaving a wajib, whether by advancement, delay, increase, or decrease. The commentary distinguishes between fard (essential) and wajib, explaining that omitting a sunnah does not make the prayer deficient, while omitting a fard invalidates it. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: on the view that the first sitting is cancelled (by standing for the third rak'ah), the sitting with tashahhud is the fard; on the view that it is not cancelled, it is wajib. The correct position is that the prayer is valid but sajdat al-sahw is required. The passage then discusses the details of the prostrations themselves (sitting between them, takbir, tasbih) and an interesting anecdote about Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Kisa'i regarding forgetfulness within forgetfulness. It also covers many scenarios where sajdat al-sahw becomes obligatory, such as mistakes in recitation, order of Surah and Fatiha, forgetting qunut, etc. The general rule is that any intentional or unintentional deviation from a wajib necessitates the two prostrations. The passage concludes that even if forgetfulness occurs multiple times, only two prostrations are required by consensus.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for errors (omission, delay, increase, decrease) in prayer that violate a wajib.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that is established by a zanni evidence; omission requires compensation (sajdat al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting of prayer; also refers to the sitting itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone intentionally omits the first tashahhud (sitting) in a four-rak'ah prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but sajdat al-sahw is required.
C) The prayer is valid and no sajdat al-sahw is required because it is a sunnah.
D) The prayer is invalid and an additional rak'ah is required.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-sahw is wajib for omitting a wajib in prayer, and the prayer remains valid; this is based on the Prophet's action and the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on Sujud al-Sahw (Prostration of Forgetfulness)
Critical refinement on the rules of sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that necessitate sujud al-sahw and apply the Hanafi ruling to scenarios of forgetfulness and intentional omission in prayer.

Core Idea
Forgot a wajib? Sujud al-sahw compensates. Did it intentionally? Repeat the prayer — except for three cases.

In the Hanafi school, sujud al-sahw is a critical mechanism to preserve the validity of prayer when a wajib act is omitted, delayed, added, or advanced due to forgetfulness. This lesson unpacks the rules governing when this prostration is required, when it is not, and how it interacts with intentional errors. Understanding these distinctions prevents the common error of misapplying sujud al-sahw to intentional violations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sujud al-sahw is a wajib act that compensates for forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer. It is not a fard; its omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation if forgotten.
The ruling is based on the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) performing two prostrations for forgetfulness.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the narrated practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) who performed sujud al-sahw after the salutation. This is a hadith ahad, which in Hanafi usul establishes a wajib ruling.
The author references 'ma rawayna' (what we narrated) indicating the reliance on this hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (prostrating after salutation) combined with his statement 'when one of you forgets, let him prostrate two prostrations' indicates that sujud al-sahw is legislated to compensate for forgetfulness. The general command 'let him prostrate' (al-amr) in the hadith implies obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and others; the Hanafi school uses it as proof for wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement on timing: the majority of Hanafi scholars (zahir al-riwaya) hold it is sunnah to perform after salutation, but some say it is wajib after salutation. There is also a difference on whether it is sunnah or wajib in general, but the relied-upon view is sunnah with permissibility before or after salutation.
Al-Hidayah states the difference is one of preference, not validity.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The tarjih is based on the principle that the salutation is obligatory and should precede sujud al-sahw by analogy with other obligatory acts. However, performing sujud al-sahw before salutation is not invalid because compensation can still be achieved.
The author follows the view of al-Hidayah and al-Bahr, prioritizing the zahir al-riwaya.

It is not compensated by anything else (forgetfully) by advancement, delay, increase or decrease, according to what we narrated. And the intentional one deserves only severity by repeating his prayer to compensate its defect. (And if it recurs) by consensus, like leaving al-Fatihah and tranquility in bowing, or after rising from it before prostration: he returns and recites the surah and repeats the bowing, and upon him is the prostration of forgetfulness because by reciting the surah it occurred as an obligatory act so the bowing is nullified; even if he does not repeat it, his prayer is invalidated. Similarly, if he recited the surah and forgot the Fatihah, then remembered, he returns and recites the Fatihah and repeats the surah, and repeats the bowing, and upon him is the prostration of forgetfulness. Unlike if he remembers the qunut in bowing: he does not return and does not perform qunut in it because its place is missed; if he returns and performs qunut, his bowing is not nullified because qunut does not occur as an obligatory act, so the obligatory act is not nullified by it. And he prostrates for forgetfulness in any case due to leaving an obligatory act or delaying it. And if he recites a verse in bowing, prostration, or standing, then upon him is the prostration of forgetfulness. And if he recites in sitting: if he recites before the tashahhud in the two sittings, upon him is the prostration of forgetfulness for leaving the obligatory beginning with tashahhud at the first sitting. And if he recites after the tashahhud: if it is in the first sitting, upon him is the prostration of forgetfulness for delaying the obligatory, which is connecting standing with finishing the tashahhud. And if it is in the last sitting, there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon him because he did not leave an obligatory act, as he has leeway in supplication and praise after it, and recitation includes both. And if he recites the tashahhud twice in the last sitting, or recites tashahhud while standing, bowing, or prostrating, there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon him. (Munyat al-Musalli) But if he recites in the first standing before the Fatihah, or in the second standing after the surah, or in the last two sections unconditionally, there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon him. If he recites in the first two sections after the Fatihah and surah, or in the second section before the Fatihah, he prostrates because he delayed an obligatory act. Its clarification is in Ibn Amir Hajj. And if he leaves the tashahhud in the two sittings or part of it, prostration is necessary upon him in the apparent narration because it is one organized remembrance, so leaving part of it is like leaving all of it. Among them is the qunut of witr and its takbirah: if he leaves them, the prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory according to what was preferred in al-Bahr. Among them is the Imam's loud recitation where he should recite loudly, and silence in its place absolutely. There is a difference of opinion on the amount that necessitates the prostration of forgetfulness. The correct view is the amount that makes the prayer valid in the two cases, because a small amount of loudness and silence cannot be avoided. And what is narrated about reciting a verse sometimes in the silent prayer is to show that recitation is prescribed where it is heard, and it was rejected... He used to recite loudly in all prayers until the verse was revealed: "And do not recite aloud in your prayer nor in a low voice" [al-Isra 17:110]. So it is determined that that is to show permissibility, i.e., the permissibility of reciting aloud to this extent, because avoiding loudness completely is difficult, especially at the beginning of breaths, as sound often appears. End quote. Sharaf al-A'immah said: There is no difference that if he recites most of al-Fatihah aloud where he should be silent, then remembers, he completes it silently. And if he recites most of it silently where he should recite aloud, Shams al-A'immah said: By analogy with the cases of al-Jami', he is commanded to repeat. And they explicitly stated that the obligation of silence is specific to recitation. So if he recites loud with remembrances and supplications, even if they are tashahhud, there is no prostration of forgetfulness upon him. And from what we mentioned, the forms of advancement, delay, increase, and decrease are known. His saying: (According to what we narrated) that he prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness. His saying: (And if it recurs) whether of the same type or different types, he is not required more than two prostrations by consensus, and it is not countered by one who prostrated for forgetfulness, then... in bowing, prostration, and the first sitting, and delaying the standing for the third by the extent of performing a pillar, even if silently. (And if he leaves) the obligatory (intentionally, he sins and must (repeat the prayer) as a severity (to compensate its defect). So it becomes a completion, and the obligation is fulfilled by the first. And it is said: the second becomes the obligation that removes it. And he does not prostrate for (intentional) (forgetfulness) because it is stronger. It is said except in three issues: (leaving the first sitting) intentionally or delaying it, he prostrates from the first rak'ah intentionally until the end of the prayer, and the third: (his thinking intentionally until it occupied him from the extent of a pillar). Fakhr al-Islam al-Badi'i was asked: How is it obligatory due to intention? He said: Prostration of forgetfulness. (And it is sunnah to perform the prostration of forgetfulness) after the salutation in the apparent narration, and it is said: it is obligatory to do it after the salutation. The apparent view is based on what we narrated. And one salutation is sufficient. So said Shaykh al-Islam and the generality of the scholars, and it is more precautionary and better, and it is (to the right) because that is the prostration of excuse... He remembers a prostration of recitation or obligatory prostration, so he prostrates for the omitted one then repeats the prostration of forgetfulness. Thus, the prostration of forgetfulness has recurred in one prayer in reality and ruling, because we say: this is not repetition; rather it is repeated to remove it by returning to the recitation or obligatory prostration to show that his first prostration was not in its place. As in al-Bahr. His saying: (And the repetition of the prayer is obligatory upon him) If he does not repeat it until the time exits, it falls from him with disapproval of prohibition. This is the relied view. His saying: (Because it is stronger) i.e., because intentional is stronger than forgetfulness, and the stronger cannot be compensated by the compensator of the weaker. His saying: (No to three) add to it: if he prays upon the Prophet ﷺ in the first sitting intentionally, and if he leaves the Fatihah intentionally. His saying: (Or) delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah) The better expression of some is: or delaying one of the two prostrations of a rak'ah to after it intentionally. His saying: (That is the prostration of excuse) i.e., the prostration done as an apology for what occurred from him. His saying: (And it is said: it is obligatory to do it after the salutation, so it is not permissible before it because performing it before its time, as in the commentary. His saying: What we narrated that he prostrated after the salutation, which does not necessitate sunnah, but rather may imply obligation. The expression of the commentary: The apparent view is that his action occurred in a place of ijtihad, so it is not ruled invalid because the rationally understood meaning of its legislation, which is compensation, is not negated by its occurrence before the salutation. However, it is against the sunnah according to us based on what we narrated. Al-Hidayah said: The difference is one of preference, and there is no difference in permissibility before and after salutation due to the authenticity of the hadith on both, and it is the apparent narration, and preference is for what we said. The meaning: The salutation is obligatory, so it is given precedence over the prostration of forgetfulness by analogy with other obligatory acts. And because if he forgets the salutation, he can prostrate. So if he doubts whether he prayed three or four, and this occupies him until the end of the salutation, the prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory upon him. If he advances the prostration for leaving another obligatory act, then prostrates for what was mentioned, the prostration is repeated. And if he does not prostrate, a necessary defect remains uncompensated, so it is recommended to delay it after the salutation for this reason. His saying: (And it is more precautionary) means that precaution is more in it. He said in the commentary from al-Khabbaziyyah: The fiqh of it is that the first salutation is tahlil and greeting, and the second is greeting, because the tahlil occurs with the first. Therefore, it is not valid to follow him after the first, and if he laughs aloud after the first, his ablution is not nullified. So it was more precautionary to prostrate before from the aspect of correctness.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the commentary of Maraqi al-Falah, discussing the rulings of Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) in prayer. The author, al-Tahtawi, explains the conditions under which this prostration becomes necessary, the cases where it is not required, and the differences between forgetfulness and intentional omission.

The passage begins by stating that a prayer that is defective due to forgetfulness (by advancement, delay, increase, or decrease) is not compensated by anything other than sujud al-sahw. This is based on the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) performed two prostrations for forgetfulness. For intentional violations, the worshipper sins and must repeat the prayer, but sujud al-sahw is not required because intentionality is stronger and cannot be compensated by a weaker substitute. However, there are three exceptions where even intentional omission requires sujud al-sahw: leaving the first sitting intentionally, delaying a prostration from its proper place, and being so preoccupied by thinking that one omits a pillar.

The text then details various scenarios: if one forgets to recite al-Fatihah and remembers after bowing, he must return, recite al-Fatihah and the surah, repeat the bowing, and perform sujud al-sahw. If he remembers qunut in bowing, he does not return because its place is lost. Reciting verses in bowing, prostration, or standing necessitates sujud al-sahw because it is an addition or delay. Reading before tashahhud in the first sitting also requires it, but not after tashahhud in the last sitting because supplication is allowed there.

Regarding the timing of sujud al-sahw, the preferable view (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is sunnah to perform it after the salutation. Some say it is obligatory after salutation, but the author notes that there is no disagreement on permissibility before or after salutation. The first salutation suffices, and it is more precautionary to perform the prostration before the salutation if one fears missing the compensatory effect.

The passage also addresses the case where a prostration of recitation (tilawah) or obligatory prostration (sahw) is remembered after performing sujud al-sahw: one prostrates for the omitted one and repeats sujud al-sahw, but this is not considered a repetition of sujud al-sahw in the same prayer; rather, it is a correction.

Key Hanafi principles evident: the distinction between wajib (obligatory) and fard (essential) — omitting a wajib requires sujud al-sahw, while omitting a fard invalidates the prayer. The authority weight is from the zahir al-riwaya and later preferred positions of the school.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness-related errors in prayer, such as omission or delay of a wajib act.
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness or unintentional error during prayer that does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation.
واجب (wajib): An act that is required but not at the level of fard; omission does not invalidate prayer but requires sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sujud al-sahw for forgetting to recite the surah after al-Fatihah in the first rak'ah and remembering after bowing?
A) The prayer is invalid; he must repeat it.
B) He must return, recite the surah, repeat bowing, and perform sujud al-sahw.
C) He continues and performs sujud al-sahw at the end without returning.
D) He does nothing because the surah is not wajib.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw compensates for forgetful errors in prayer, but intentional errors require repetition unless falling under the three exceptions; the preferred timing is after salutation, but before is permissible.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Sujud al-Sahw for Deliberate Omission in Prayer
Explains the rule on deliberate wajib omission and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that deliberate omission of a wajib requires repeating the prayer and identify the three exceptions where Sujud al-Sahw is prescribed.

Core Idea
Deliberate omission is stronger than forgetfulness; sujud cannot compensate except in three specific cases.

The Hanafi school distinguishes sharply between forgetful and deliberate omisssion of wajib elements in prayer. The general rule is that deliberate omission cannot be repaired by Sujud al-Sahw; the prayer must be repeated. However, there are three exceptional cases where even deliberate omission is compensated by prostration. This lesson unpacks that rule and its exceptions, grounding you in the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
From the passage, identify the ruling for deliberate omission of a wajib: it requires repeating the prayer (iʿādat al-ṣalāt) and does not permit Sujud al-Sahw.
The text says 'wa wujiba ʿalayhi iʿādat al-ṣalāh' — repetition is wājib.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that deliberate omission (al-ʿamd) is stronger (aqwā) than forgetfulness (al-sahw), and the compensator (jābir) for the weaker cannot fix the stronger. Grasp the principle that the severity of the omission determines the remedy.
This is a core Hanafi usul maxim: al-aqwā lā yanjabiru bi-jābiri al-aḍʿaf.
3
List the three exceptions
From the passage, extract the three cases where deliberate omission does require Sujud al-Sahw: (1) leaving the first sitting (qaʿdah ūlā), (2) delaying a prostration from a rakʿah to a later point, (3) being engrossed in thought until missing the extent of a rukn.
Some add cases like sending ṣalāh on the Prophet in the first sitting or deliberately leaving al-Fātiḥah, but the core three are given.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a person who deliberately omits the first sitting. According to the rule, does he repeat the prayer or perform Sujud al-Sahw? The answer is sujud, because this is one of the exceptions.
The prayer is valid but deficient; sujud compensates.
5
Contrast with forgetful omission
If the same omission occurred forgetfully, Sujud al-Sahw would be the standard remedy. Deliberate omission elevates the requirement to repetition. Understand why the school treats them differently.
This contrast is essential for fatwa: always check intention (ʿamd vs. sahwah).

Regarding bowing, prostration, first sitting, delaying standing for the third [rak'ah] by the extent of performing a pillar, even if motionless (And if he deliberately leaves) the obligatory (he sins and must (repeat the prayer) as a severity upon him (to compensate its deficiency). So it becomes completing, and the obligation falls with the first, and it is said: the second becomes an obligation that drops [the first]. (And he does not prostrate for deliberate (omission due to forgetfulness) because it is stronger; it is said except in three issues: (deliberately leaving the first sitting) or delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah) deliberately to the end of the prayer, and the third (deliberately thinking until it distracted him from the extent of a pillar). Fakhr al-Islam al-Badi'i was asked: how does it become obligatory due to deliberate action? He said: Sujud al-Sahw. (And it is sunnah to perform Sujud al-Sahw) after the salam in the apparent narration, and it is said: it is obligatory to do it after the salam, and the justification of the apparent is what we narrated, and one salam is sufficient, said by Shaykh al-Islam and the generality of the mashayikh, and it is the most guaranteeing of caution and the best, and it is (to his right) because that is the prostration of excuse. If he remembers a tilawa or salbiya sajdah, then he prostrates for the missed one, then repeats Sujud al-Sahw; for Sujud al-Sahw would be repeated in one prayer in reality and in ruling, but we say this is not repetition; rather it is repeated to raise it by returning to the tilawa or salbiya to show that his first prostration was not in its place; thus in al-Bahr. His saying: (and he must repeat the prayer) – if he does not repeat it until the time exits, it drops from him with karaha tahrimiyya; this is the relied-upon. His saying: (because it is stronger) i.e., because deliberate is stronger than forgetfulness, and the stronger cannot be compensated by the compensator of the weaker. His saying: (not) – in three, it is added: if he sends blessings on the Prophet deliberately in the first sitting; also if he deliberately leaves al-Fatiha. His saying: (or delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah) – the expression of some is better where they said: delaying one of two prostrations of a rak'ah to after it deliberately. His saying: (that is the prostration of excuse) i.e., the prostration done to apologize for what occurred from him. His saying: (and it is said it is obligatory to do it after the salam) thus it is not permissible before it because it would be performed before its time; thus in al-Sharh. His saying: (what we narrated) – that he performed prostration after the salam, and this does not necessitate sunnah, rather it may imply obligation. The expression of al-Sharh: the justification of the apparent is that his act occurred in a place of ijtihad, so it is not ruled invalid, for the rational meaning of its legislation, which is compensation, is not negated by its occurrence before salam, but it is contrary to the sunnah according to us because of what we narrated. He said in al-Hidayah: the difference is in priority, and there is no difference in permissibility before and after salam due to the authentic hadith about both, and it is the apparent narration and the preference is for what we said: the meaning is that salam is obligatory, so it takes precedence over Sujud al-Sahw by analogy with other obligatory acts, and because if he forgets the salam, he can prostrate; so if he doubts whether he prayed three or four and this distracted him until the end of salam, Sujud al-Sahw becomes obligatory. So if he advances the sujud for leaving another obligatory act, then prostrates for the mentioned [doubt], the sujud is repeated; and if he does not prostrate, a necessary deficiency remains uncompensated, so it is recommended to delay it after salam for this reason. His saying: (and it is the most guaranteeing of caution) means that caution is greater in it. He said in al-Sharh from al-Khabbaziyya: the fiqh in it is that the first taslim is tahlil and tahiyya, and the second is tahiyya, because the tahlil occurs with the first, and for this, it is not valid to follow him after the first; and if he guffaws after the first, his ablution is not broken; so the more cautious is to prostrate before [salam]. He does not perform Sujud al-Sahw after two taslims because that is like speech (in the most correct view), and it is said its justification is a distinction between the salam of cutting and the salam of forgetfulness, said by Fakhr al-Islam. And in al-Hidayah: he performs two taslims – this is correct. But you have learned that the cautious is after one taslim, and the prohibition of doing it after two taslims. So the most balanced and most correct is that if he prostrates before salam, it is makruh tanzihan, and he does not repeat it, so it is permissible, and no one has said it should be repeated. And if his imam considers it before salam, he follows him, just as he follows him in qunut of Ramadan after ruku'. Sujud al-Sahw is nullified by sunrise after salam in the fajr prayer, and by the exit of time of Jumu'ah and 'Eid due to loss of condition of validity; and likewise it is nullified if he greets just before its reddening, i.e., the change of the sun in 'Asr, to avoid the disliked; and it is nullified by the occurrence of something that prevents building after salam, like deliberate hadath, or an act that contradicts due to loss of condition. (And the follower is bound) by what binds the imam regarding forgetfulness except in three: if we say that he prostrates after salam.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi presents a detailed discussion on Sujud al-Sahw for deliberate omissions and the timing of the prostration. The commentary begins by stating the rule: if one deliberately omits a wajib (obligatory element) in prayer, he sins and must repeat the prayer entirely. This is a severity to compensate the deficiency. The original prayer is valid but deficient, and the repetition is recommended (some consider the second prayer as the actual obligation). The reason deliberate omission is not compensated by Sujud al-Sahw is because deliberateness is stronger than forgetfulness, and a stronger deficiency cannot be remedied by a compensator meant for weaker lapses. The author then notes an exception: there are three cases where deliberate omission does require Sujud al-Sahw: leaving the first sitting, delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah to the end of the prayer, and being so engrossed in thought that one misses the extent of a pillar. Fakhr al-Islam al-Badi'i confirms that in these cases, Sujud al-Sahw becomes wajib. The passage then shifts to the timing of Sujud al-Sahw. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, it is sunnah to perform it after the salam (the final greeting). Some scholars (including Imam Muhammad? Actually it's reported from some) say it is wajib to do it after the salam. The preferred view is that it is sunnah, and one sufficing taslim (to the right) is enough, as stated by Shaykh al-Islam and the majority. This is the most cautious and best practice. The author explains that performing sujud after a single taslim is the established practice. Then, if one remembers a missed tilawah or salbiya (forgetfulness) prostration, he should prostrate for the missed one, and then repeat the Sujud al-Sahw. Though this looks like repetition, it is not; rather it is a new sujud because the previous one was not in its proper place. The text then discusses the difference of opinion on whether Sujud al-Sahw is sunnah or wajib after salam. The evidence for the sunnah view is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated after salam, and this does not necessarily imply obligation. The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah, and performing it before salam is permissible but makruh tanzihan. The text also addresses whether two taslims should be performed. Some scholars, like Khahar Zadah, prohibit performing Sujud al-Sahw after two taslims because the second taslim is like speech. Others hold that two taslims are correct. The most balanced view is that one taslim is the established practice and more cautious. If one's imam considers Sujud al-Sahw before salam, the follower should follow him, just as in qunut of Ramadan after ruku'. Finally, the passage lists factors that cause Sujud al-Sahw to lapse: (1) sunrise after salam in Fajr prayer, (2) exit of time for Jumu'ah or 'Eid prayer (since validity conditions are lost), (3) if one gives salam just before the sun reddens in 'Asr prayer (to avoid karaha), and (4) occurrence of something that prevents building (like deliberate hadath or contradicting action) after salam. The follower is bound by the same rules as the imam regarding forgetfulness, except in three cases (which are mentioned later). This is a critical refinement of the Maraqi al-Falah text, clarifying the nuances of deliberate omission and the preferred timing.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (Sujud al-Sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or omission in prayer. It is wajib for certain omissions and sunnah after salam.
الترك العمد (al-tark al-‘amd): Deliberate omission of a wajib element in prayer. This requires repeating the prayer and is not compensated by Sujud al-Sahw except in specific cases.
السلام (al-salam): The final greeting of prayer, consisting of taslim to the right (and optionally to the left). It is a wajib part of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone deliberately leaves the first sitting (qa'dah ula) in prayer?
A) He must perform Sujud al-Sahw and the prayer is valid.
B) He must repeat the entire prayer and does not perform Sujud al-Sahw.
C) He must perform Sujud al-Sahw before salam.
D) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated without sujud.

Key Takeaway
Deliberate omission of a wajib generally requires repeating the prayer, except for three specific cases where Sujud al-Sahw suffices: leaving the first sitting, delaying a prostration from a rak'ah, and being preoccupied with thought until missing the extent of a rukn.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Timing of Sujud al-Sahw: After Salam vs. Before Salam
Discusses timing of Sujud al-Sahw and dispute on taslim count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position that Sujud al-Sahw is sunnah after salam and identify the practical consequences of performing it before salam.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw after salam is sunnah; before salam is makruh tanzihan but valid.

One of the most debated aspects of Sujud al-Sahw is its timing: should it be performed before or after the salam? The Hanafi school, based on Zahir al-Riwayah, holds that the sunnah is to perform it after salam, while other schools permit or prefer before salam. This lesson explores the evidence, the reasoning, and the practical implications of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
From the passage, note that the clear teaching (zāhir al-riwāyah) is to perform Sujud al-Sahw after the salam. This is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The text says 'wa yusannu al-ityānu bi-sujūd al-sahw baʿda al-salām'.
2
Understand the opposing view
Some scholars (including from other schools) say it is permissible or even recommended before salam. The passage mentions that the difference is in priority, not in essential validity.
Al-Hidayah states: 'al-khilāf fī al-awlawiyyah, lā khilāf fī al-jawāz qabl al-salām wa baʿdah'.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The proof cited is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who prostrated after salam. Additionally, qiyas is used: salam is wajib, so it takes precedence over sunnah sujud, similar to other wajibat.
The qiyas is: 'anna al-salām wājib, fa-yuqaddam ʿalā sujūd al-sahw qiyāsan ʿalā ghayrihi min al-wājibāt'.
4
Note the ruling for performing before salam
If someone performs Sujud al-Sahw before salam, it is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not sinful), and the prostration is valid. He does not need to repeat it.
The text says 'fa-in sajada qabl al-salām kariha tanzīhan wa lā yuʿīduh'.
5
Apply the ruling in congregation
If the imam holds the view that sujud is before salam, the follower should follow him, as in the qunut of Ramadan. This shows that ikhtilaf within the school is accommodated in practice.
The passage says: 'wa in kāna imāmuhu yarāhu qabl al-salām tābaʿah'.

Regarding bowing, prostration, first sitting, delaying standing for the third [rak'ah] by the extent of performing a pillar, even if motionless (And if he deliberately leaves) the obligatory (he sins and must (repeat the prayer) as a severity upon him (to compensate its deficiency). So it becomes completing, and the obligation falls with the first, and it is said: the second becomes an obligation that drops [the first]. (And he does not prostrate for deliberate (omission due to forgetfulness) because it is stronger; it is said except in three issues: (deliberately leaving the first sitting) or delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah) deliberately to the end of the prayer, and the third (deliberately thinking until it distracted him from the extent of a pillar). Fakhr al-Islam al-Badi'i was asked: how does it become obligatory due to deliberate action? He said: Sujud al-Sahw. (And it is sunnah to perform Sujud al-Sahw) after the salam in the apparent narration, and it is said: it is obligatory to do it after the salam, and the justification of the apparent is what we narrated, and one salam is sufficient, said by Shaykh al-Islam and the generality of the mashayikh, and it is the most guaranteeing of caution and the best, and it is (to his right) because that is the prostration of excuse. If he remembers a tilawa or salbiya sajdah, then he prostrates for the missed one, then repeats Sujud al-Sahw; for Sujud al-Sahw would be repeated in one prayer in reality and in ruling, but we say this is not repetition; rather it is repeated to raise it by returning to the tilawa or salbiya to show that his first prostration was not in its place; thus in al-Bahr. His saying: (and he must repeat the prayer) – if he does not repeat it until the time exits, it drops from him with karaha tahrimiyya; this is the relied-upon. His saying: (because it is stronger) i.e., because deliberate is stronger than forgetfulness, and the stronger cannot be compensated by the compensator of the weaker. His saying: (not) – in three, it is added: if he sends blessings on the Prophet deliberately in the first sitting; also if he deliberately leaves al-Fatiha. His saying: (or delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah) – the expression of some is better where they said: delaying one of two prostrations of a rak'ah to after it deliberately. His saying: (that is the prostration of excuse) i.e., the prostration done to apologize for what occurred from him. His saying: (and it is said it is obligatory to do it after the salam) thus it is not permissible before it because it would be performed before its time; thus in al-Sharh. His saying: (what we narrated) – that he performed prostration after the salam, and this does not necessitate sunnah, rather it may imply obligation. The expression of al-Sharh: the justification of the apparent is that his act occurred in a place of ijtihad, so it is not ruled invalid, for the rational meaning of its legislation, which is compensation, is not negated by its occurrence before salam, but it is contrary to the sunnah according to us because of what we narrated. He said in al-Hidayah: the difference is in priority, and there is no difference in permissibility before and after salam due to the authentic hadith about both, and it is the apparent narration and the preference is for what we said: the meaning is that salam is obligatory, so it takes precedence over Sujud al-Sahw by analogy with other obligatory acts, and because if he forgets the salam, he can prostrate; so if he doubts whether he prayed three or four and this distracted him until the end of salam, Sujud al-Sahw becomes obligatory. So if he advances the sujud for leaving another obligatory act, then prostrates for the mentioned [doubt], the sujud is repeated; and if he does not prostrate, a necessary deficiency remains uncompensated, so it is recommended to delay it after salam for this reason. His saying: (and it is the most guaranteeing of caution) means that caution is greater in it. He said in al-Sharh from al-Khabbaziyya: the fiqh in it is that the first taslim is tahlil and tahiyya, and the second is tahiyya, because the tahlil occurs with the first, and for this, it is not valid to follow him after the first; and if he guffaws after the first, his ablution is not broken; so the more cautious is to prostrate before [salam]. He does not perform Sujud al-Sahw after two taslims because that is like speech (in the most correct view), and it is said its justification is a distinction between the salam of cutting and the salam of forgetfulness, said by Fakhr al-Islam. And in al-Hidayah: he performs two taslims – this is correct. But you have learned that the cautious is after one taslim, and the prohibition of doing it after two taslims. So the most balanced and most correct is that if he prostrates before salam, it is makruh tanzihan, and he does not repeat it, so it is permissible, and no one has said it should be repeated. And if his imam considers it before salam, he follows him, just as he follows him in qunut of Ramadan after ruku'. Sujud al-Sahw is nullified by sunrise after salam in the fajr prayer, and by the exit of time of Jumu'ah and 'Eid due to loss of condition of validity; and likewise it is nullified if he greets just before its reddening, i.e., the change of the sun in 'Asr, to avoid the disliked; and it is nullified by the occurrence of something that prevents building after salam, like deliberate hadath, or an act that contradicts due to loss of condition. (And the follower is bound) by what binds the imam regarding forgetfulness except in three: if we say that he prostrates after salam.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi presents a detailed discussion on Sujud al-Sahw for deliberate omissions and the timing of the prostration. The commentary begins by stating the rule: if one deliberately omits a wajib (obligatory element) in prayer, he sins and must repeat the prayer entirely. This is a severity to compensate the deficiency. The original prayer is valid but deficient, and the repetition is recommended (some consider the second prayer as the actual obligation). The reason deliberate omission is not compensated by Sujud al-Sahw is because deliberateness is stronger than forgetfulness, and a stronger deficiency cannot be remedied by a compensator meant for weaker lapses. The author then notes an exception: there are three cases where deliberate omission does require Sujud al-Sahw: leaving the first sitting, delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah to the end of the prayer, and being so engrossed in thought that one misses the extent of a pillar. Fakhr al-Islam al-Badi'i confirms that in these cases, Sujud al-Sahw becomes wajib. The passage then shifts to the timing of Sujud al-Sahw. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, it is sunnah to perform it after the salam (the final greeting). Some scholars (including Imam Muhammad? Actually it's reported from some) say it is wajib to do it after the salam. The preferred view is that it is sunnah, and one sufficing taslim (to the right) is enough, as stated by Shaykh al-Islam and the majority. This is the most cautious and best practice. The author explains that performing sujud after a single taslim is the established practice. Then, if one remembers a missed tilawah or salbiya (forgetfulness) prostration, he should prostrate for the missed one, and then repeat the Sujud al-Sahw. Though this looks like repetition, it is not; rather it is a new sujud because the previous one was not in its proper place. The text then discusses the difference of opinion on whether Sujud al-Sahw is sunnah or wajib after salam. The evidence for the sunnah view is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated after salam, and this does not necessarily imply obligation. The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah, and performing it before salam is permissible but makruh tanzihan. The text also addresses whether two taslims should be performed. Some scholars, like Khahar Zadah, prohibit performing Sujud al-Sahw after two taslims because the second taslim is like speech. Others hold that two taslims are correct. The most balanced view is that one taslim is the established practice and more cautious. If one's imam considers Sujud al-Sahw before salam, the follower should follow him, just as in qunut of Ramadan after ruku'. Finally, the passage lists factors that cause Sujud al-Sahw to lapse: (1) sunrise after salam in Fajr prayer, (2) exit of time for Jumu'ah or 'Eid prayer (since validity conditions are lost), (3) if one gives salam just before the sun reddens in 'Asr prayer (to avoid karaha), and (4) occurrence of something that prevents building (like deliberate hadath or contradicting action) after salam. The follower is bound by the same rules as the imam regarding forgetfulness, except in three cases (which are mentioned later). This is a critical refinement of the Maraqi al-Falah text, clarifying the nuances of deliberate omission and the preferred timing.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (Sujud al-Sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or omission in prayer. It is wajib for certain omissions and sunnah after salam.
السلام (al-salam): The final greeting of prayer, consisting of taslim to the right (and optionally to the left). It is a wajib part of prayer.
الأولوية (al-awlawiyya): Priority; the concept that one action is preferred over another without rendering the other invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person performs Sujud al-Sahw before the salam?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is permissible without any dislike.
C) It is makruh tanzihan but valid.
D) It is wajib to repeat the sujud after salam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Sujud al-Sahw is sunnah after salam; performing it before salam is makruh tanzihan but valid, and the difference with other schools is one of priority, not essential permissibility.

Salah — Prayer

One Salam or Two: The Hanafi Position on Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sujud al-sahw timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi regarding the number of salams after sujud al-sahw and explain the reasoning of al-Tahtawi's tarjih.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw after one salam is the most just and correct Hanafi position.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: should the forgetfulness prostration (sujud al-sahw) be performed after one salam or two? The source passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah surveys conflicting views among Hanafi authorities and resolves them by preferring one salam as the established practice (al-ma'hud). Understanding this ruling clarifies a practical aspect of prayer completion and illustrates how later Hanafi scholars weigh evidence and achieve tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the Hanafi position
The issue is whether sujud al-sahw should be performed after one salam (to the right) or after two salams. The Hanafi mufta bihi is after one salam.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Some Hanafi authorities like Khawharzada prohibited sujud after two salams because the second salam is like speech (kalam), which invalidates the prayer. Others like al-Hidayah said two salams is correct. Fakhr al-Islam distinguished between salam of termination and salam of forgetfulness.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Khawharzada argues that two salams constitute speech, and sujud after speech is invalid because speech is a munafi (invalidator). Al-Hidayah's view that two salams is correct is also noted.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
Al-Tahtawi prefers one salam as the most just (a'dal) and most correct (asahh) position, because it is intermediate between those who say before salam and those who say after two salams, and it is the established practice. The precautionary measure (ahwat) is also after one salam.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, the musalli should perform sujud al-sahw after one salam to the right, not after two salams. This is the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلقاء لأنه مجتهد فيه المعهود، به ويحصل التحليل، فلا حاجة إلى غيره خصوصاً، وقد قال شيخ الإسلام: خواهر زاده لا يأتي بسجود السهو بعد تسليمتين لأن ذلك بمنزلة الكلام (في الأصح)، وقيل وجهه فرقاً بين سلام القطع، وسلام السهو قاله فخر الإسلام وفي الهداية ويأتي بتسليمتين هو الصحيح، ولكن علمت أن الأحوط بعد تسليمة، والمنع من فعله بعد تسليمتين فكان الأعدل الأصح السلام الثاني قوله : ( والأحسن) معطوف على الأضمن ووجه الاحسنية أنه المعهود لا السلام تلقاء الوجه. قوله : (لأن ذلك أي التسليمة الثانية بمنزلة الكلام أي فلا يأتي بالسهو بعده لوجود المنافي قوله ويأتي بتسليمتين هو الصحيح أيده العلامة خسرو بما لا مزيد عليه . قوله : (والمنع) عطف على أن الأحوط أي منع شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده. قوله: (فكان الأعدل الأصح) أي فكان القول بأنه بعد تسليمة واحدة عن يمينه أعدل الأقوال وأصحها أما كونه أعدل فلأنه متوسط بين قولي من قال : إنه قبل التسليم ومن قال انه بعد التسليمتين، وأما كونه أصح فلقوله سابقاً لأنه المعهود
Towards the face because it is a matter of ijtihad, the established practice. By it tahlil is achieved, so there is no need for other than it, especially since Shaykh al-Islam Khawharzada said: 'Do not come with sujud al-sahw after two salams because that is like speech' (in the most sound view). And it was said its reason is a distinction between salam of termination and salam of forgetfulness, said by Fakhr al-Islam. And in al-Hidayah: 'He comes with two salams, that is the correct view.' But I know that the precautionary measure is after one salam, and the prohibition of doing it after two salams, so it was the most just and most correct. Then the author's statement: 'And the better' is coordinated with 'the more guaranteed', and the reason for betterness is that it is the established practice, not the salam to the face. His statement: 'Because that, i.e., the second salam is like speech, i.e., so he does not come with sujud after it due to the presence of what contradicts [the prayer].' His statement: 'He comes with two salams is the correct view' was supported by 'Allamah Khisraw with no further comment. His statement: 'And the prohibition' is coordinated with 'that the precautionary measure', i.e., the prohibition of Shaykh al-Islam Khawharzada. His statement: 'So it was the most just and most correct' means the statement that it is after one salam to his right is the most just of the statements and the most correct. As for being more just, because it is intermediate between the statement of those who say it is before salam and those who say it is after two salams. As for being most correct, because of his previous saying that it is the established practice.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the number of salams after which sujud al-sahw is performed. The base text from Maraqi al-Falah states the established practice is one salam to the face. The commentator al-Tahtawi explains that some scholars, like Khawharzada, prohibit sujud after two salams because two salams would be considered speech, which invalidates the prayer. Fakhr al-Islam distinguished between the salam of termination and the salam of forgetfulness. Al-Hidayah says two salams is correct, but al-Tahtawi notes the precautionary measure (al-ahwat) is one salam, and the prohibition of doing it after two salams makes the middle view the most just and most correct: sujud al-sahw after one salam to the right. The commentary further explains that the more guaranteed (al-adman) is one salam, but the better (al-ahsan) is the established practice, not the salam to the face. The second salam is like speech, so sujud after it is invalid. The hadith 'The imam is a guarantor' is referenced later. The preferred view is after one salam.

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslimah): One delivery of the salam (greeting of peace) to the right or left, part of the prayer conclusion.
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer leading to a prescribed prostration (sujud al-sahw) to compensate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Tahtawi, which is the most correct (asahh) positioning for sujud al-sahw?
A) Before salam
B) After one salam to the right
C) After two salams
D) It is optional

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that sujud al-sahw is performed after one salam to the right, a position deemed most just and most correct by later scholars.
