عدم الموصوف وقال محمد تبطل أصلاً، ووصفاً لأن التحريمة عقدت للفرض قصداً أو لأصل الصلاة ضمناً فإذا بطل الفرض بطل ما في ضمنه، والحاصل أنه إذا رفع رأسه من السجود بطلت صلاته أصلاً، ووصفاً عند محمد، وهو غير المفتى به، وإذا لم يرفع رأسه من السجدة، وسبقه حدث فيها على قول أبي يوسف فسد وصف صلاته فیبنی على أنها نفل، وعلى قول محمد عليه أن يتدارك فرضه لرجوعه إلى القعدة، ولا يبطل لعدم الإتيان بركعة عنده إذ لا تتم عنده إلا بالرفع من السجود ولم يحصل وهو المفتى به هنا فتأمل. قوله: (وهو المختار للفتوى أي يفتى به في عدم بطلان الفرض بمجرد الوضع لإمكان صحة صلاته بعوده إلى العقدة، إذا سبقه الحدث في السجدة، ولا يفي ببطلانه أصلاً، ووصفاً لأن بالرفع . (۱) قوله الشارح صار فرضه إلى قوله عند محمد الذي يقتضيه كلام المحشي أن تكون العبارة هكذا صار فرضه نقلا عندهما وبطلت برفع من السجود عند محمد وليحرر اهـ مصححه.
His statement: 'And if he forgets the last sitting' – meaning all of it or part of it, and what is intended is what was the last of his prayer, whether preceded by a first or not, so it includes two-rak'ah prayers. He said in al-Siraj: This ruling is not specific to forgetfulness; rather, it is also the case if he stands for a fifth rak'ah intentionally, except that in the intentional case he sins and should repeat it as compensation, while in forgetfulness he prostrates. This applies equally to obligatory and supererogatory prayers. His statement: 'as long as he has not prostrated' – to rectify his prayer, and by it the Sunnah is reported: he returned after his standing to the fifth and prostrated for forgetfulness. And if he sat a little and stood, then returned, and completed by the return the extent of tashahhud, it is valid, even if he does something inconsistent with prayer, his prayer is valid because the sitting for the extent of tashahhud is not required all at once. And he prostrates for forgetfulness for delaying the obligation of sitting. If he does not return until he has prostrated for the extra (rak'ah beyond the obligatory), his obligatory prayer becomes nafl upon raising his head from prostration according to Muhammad, and this is the choice for fatwa because the entry into nafl is firmly established before completing the obligation. Abu Yusuf said: by placing (his forehead) with its cause. And the consideration is for the imam. Even if he returns before prostrating and the congregation are unaware until they have prostrated, their prayer is not invalidated. Because when the imam returns, his bowing is nullified, so the bowing of the congregation is also nullified following him, and they have an extra prostration which does not invalidate unless intentional. And by it a puzzle is made: a praying person who left the last sitting and limited the fifth to one prostration, and his obligation is not invalidated, as in al-Durr and others. If the imam prostrates, the prayer of the follower is also invalidated, whether he sat before following his imam in prostration or not, and whether he is a muqim or a latecomer. What is meant by 'as long as he has not prostrated' is after bowing. As for if he prostrates without bowing, he returns because this prostration is not counted, as less than a rak'ah is subject to rejection. His statement: 'to rectify his prayer' is the cause for the effect, which is his return. His statement: 'and by it' the Sunnah is reported, i.e., by returning. His statement: 'he returned etc.' is a substitute for Sunnah. His statement: 'then he returned likewise' means he sat a little, and it is the second return, and after it the third. His statement: 'and he completed by it' i.e., by the last return. His statement: 'and he prostrates for forgetfulness' whether he was closer to standing or closer to sitting, unlike forgetfulness of the first sitting where there is preference on one of two views. His statement: 'the delay of the obligation of sitting' is connected with raising from prostration. His statement: 'for the extra (rak'ah) on the obligation' means for the fifth in four-rak'ah prayers, the fourth in three-rak'ah, and the third in two-rak'ah. His statement: 'his obligation becomes nafl' according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) and does not become invalid in origin. The absence of description does not necessitate the absence of the described. Muhammad said: it becomes invalid in origin and description because the intention (tahrimah) was contracted for the obligation intentionally or for the original prayer implicitly; so if the obligation is invalidated, what is implicit in it is invalidated. The conclusion: if he raises his head from prostration, his prayer becomes invalid in origin and description according to Muhammad, and he is not the one given fatwa. If he does not raise his head from prostration and is preceded by an event (hadath) in it, according to Abu Yusuf the description of his prayer is corrupted, so he builds it as nafl. According to Muhammad, he must compensate for his obligation by returning to the sitting, and it does not become invalid because he has not performed a complete rak'ah in his view, as it is only completed by raising from prostration, which did not occur. This is the view given fatwa here. Consider. His statement: 'and it is the choice for fatwa' means fatwa is given on the non-invalidity of the obligation by mere placement (of the head) due to the possibility of the validity of his prayer by returning to the knot (sitting) if he is preceded by an event during the prostration, and it does not necessitate its invalidity in origin and description because by raising. (Footnote: The commentator's statement 'his obligation becomes nafl' up to his statement 'according to Muhammad' requires, according to the annotator, that the expression be: 'his obligation becomes nafl according to them and becomes invalid by raising from prostration according to Muhammad,' and let it be written. End of correction.)
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when a person forgets the last sitting (qa'dah akheerah) and stands for an extra rak'ah, such as a fifth in a four-rak'ah fard prayer. The text explains that if he returns to sitting before prostrating the fifth prostration (i.e., before completing the extra rak'ah by going into sajdah), his prayer is valid and he must perform sajdah al-sahw for delaying the obligatory sitting. If he prostrates for the extra rak'ah (i.e., completes the fifth rak'ah by going into sujud), then there is a difference between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, upon raising his head from the extra prostration, his original fard prayer transforms into nafl (supererogatory) because the intention for fard cannot continue after the addition of a complete rak'ah. This is the relied-upon view for fatwa. Abu Yusuf holds that the transfer occurs upon placing the forehead for prostration. The practical consequence: if a person inadvertently stands for a fifth rak'ah and prostrates, his prayer becomes nafl according to the mufta bihi view, and he must complete it as nafl and later repeat the fard prayer. If he returns before prostration, his fard prayer remains valid. The passage also discusses the imam's ruling: if the imam returns before prostrating, the followers must also return; their prayer remains valid as long as they do not intentionally add a prostration. If the imam prostrates, the followers' prayer is invalidated. Overall, the key is the distinction between 'before prostration' (allows return and preserves fard) and 'after prostration' (transforms to nafl).

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qa'dah al-akheerah): The final sitting in the prayer, after the last rak'ah, during which the tashahhud and salawat are recited, and then the taslim.
الخامسة (al-khamisah): The fifth rak'ah, which is an extra rak'ah beyond the prescribed number (e.g., in a four-rak'ah fard prayer).
صار فرضه نفلاً (sara farduhu naflan): His obligatory prayer becomes supererogatory (nafl) due to the addition of a complete rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person stands for a fifth rak'ah forgetfully and does not return until after prostrating, what is the status of his prayer according to the mufta bihi view?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and he must perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) The prayer becomes nafl upon raising his head from the prostration.
D) The prayer becomes nafl upon placing his forehead for prostration.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between returning before or after the extra prostration: return before and the prayer is valid with sajdah al-sahw; return after and the obligation transforms to nafl.

When Does a Fard Prayer Become Nafl? The Fifth Rak'ah Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on when fard becomes nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when a fard prayer becomes nafl after an extra rak'ah, and apply the mufta bihi position to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
The completion of a rukn is by leaving it, not by performing it.

This lesson examines a subtle but practically important dispute within the Hanafi school: at what point does a mistakenly performed fifth rak'ah convert a fard prayer into nafl? The answer affects whether the worshipper can salvage the fard prayer if something happens during the extra prostration. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi presents two positions from the Sahibayn and clarifies the mufta bihi view.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling for the fifth rak'ah
Identify the base ruling: someone who mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah must return to sitting and perform sajdah al-sahw. This is the practice upon which the Sunnah is established.
If he sat briefly, then stood again, and then returned and completed sitting for tashahhud, his prayer is valid because the sitting is not required to be continuous.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
The dispute arises when the person does not return until after prostrating the extra rak'ah. Two opinions exist: Imam Muhammad holds that the fard becomes nafl upon raising the head from the extra prostration. Abu Yusuf holds it becomes nafl upon placing the forehead on the ground.
The text states Muhammad's view is 'al-mukhtar lil-fatwa' (the chosen position for fatwa).
3
Analyze the underlying principle
Examine the proof for each view. Muhammad's view relies on the principle that the completion of a rukn (pillar) is by transitioning from it (al-intiqal 'anhu). Abu Yusuf's view considers the sajdah complete upon placing the forehead because the name 'sajdah' applies to that action. The Quranic command 'اركعوا واسجدوا' is interpreted by Muhammad to include the entire sajdah including raising.
The text argues that the completion of the rukn is by leaving it, as evidenced by the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of a preceding hadath.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence appears when a hadath (ablution-breaking event) occurs while the forehead is on the ground during the extra prostration. According to Muhammad, the worshipper can build upon his prayer (return to sitting and continue as fard) because the fard has not yet become nafl. According to Abu Yusuf, it is already nafl, so he cannot return to fard. The text sides with Muhammad's view, which is the mufta bihi.
The difference is not just theoretical; it affects the validity of the prayer in a real situation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لاصلاح صلاته و به وردت السنة عاد بعد قيامه إلى الخامسة وسجد للسهو، ولو قعد يسيراً فقام ، ثم عاد فتم به قدر التشهد صح حتى لو أتى بمناف صحت صلاته إذ لا يشترط القعود قدر التشهد بمرة واحدة (وسجد للسهو التأخيره فرض القعود فإن لم يعد حتى (سجد) للزائدة على الفرض صار فرضه نفلاً برفع رأسه من السجود عند محمد، وهو المختار للفتوى لاستحكام دخوله في النفل قبل اكمال الفرض وقال أبو يوسف بوضع الجبهة لأنه سجود كامل وجه المختار أنّ تمام الركن بالإنتقال عنه وثمرة الخلاف تظهر بسبق الحدث حال الوضع بيني عند محمد لا عند أبي يوسف
For the correction of his prayer, and the Sunnah came with it, he returns after standing for the fifth and performs prostration of forgetfulness. If he sat briefly then stood, then returned and completed the sitting to the extent of the tashahhud, it is valid; even if he did something that invalidates, his prayer is valid because the sitting to the extent of tashahhud is not required to be in one sitting. (And he performs prostration of forgetfulness for delaying the obligatory sitting.) If he does not return until he prostrates the extra one (beyond the obligatory), his obligatory becomes voluntary upon raising his head from prostration according to Muhammad, and this is the chosen position for fatwa due to the firmness of his entry into the voluntary before completing the obligatory. Abu Yusuf said: upon placing the forehead because it is a complete prostration. The preferred view is that the completion of the pillar is by transitioning from it, and the fruit of the difference appears in the case of a preceding event during the placement: he builds upon it according to Muhammad, not according to Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling when a person mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer. The text begins by stating the general rule: if one stands for a fifth, he should return to sitting and perform sajdah al-sahw. If he sat briefly (yasir), then stood again, and then returned and completed the sitting to the extent of tashahhud, the prayer is valid—even if he did something that would normally invalidate, because the required sitting does not have to be continuous. The key dispute arises when he does not return until after prostrating the extra rak'ah. According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the fard prayer becomes nafl (voluntary) upon raising the head from the prostration of the extra rak'ah. This is the mufta bihi (operative position) because he has already entered the nafl before completing the fard. According to Abu Yusuf, it becomes nafl upon placing the forehead on the ground for prostration, because that completes the sajdah. The commentary clarifies that the chosen view is that the pillar (rukn) is completed only by transitioning from it (i.e., raising the head), not by the placement alone. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this difference appears if a hadath (ablution-breaking event) occurs during the placement of the forehead: according to Muhammad, the person can build upon his prayer (return to sitting and continue as fard), but according to Abu Yusuf, he cannot, because the prayer has already become nafl at placement.

Key Terms
القيام إلى الخامسة (al-qiyam ila al-khamisah): Standing up for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer, which is a mistake requiring sajdah al-sahw.
سجد للسهو (sajada lil-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, performed to compensate for an unintentional omission or addition in prayer.
الانتقال عنه (al-intiqal 'anhu): Transitioning from a pillar (rukn) to the next, e.g., raising the head from prostration. The completion of a rukn is marked by leaving it, not by the act itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this text, at what point does the fard prayer become nafl when someone mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah?
A) Immediately upon standing for the fifth.
B) Upon placing the forehead for the extra prostration.
C) Upon raising the head from the extra prostration.
D) Only if one completes the extra rak'ah completely.

Key Takeaway
The completion of a rukn is by leaving it, so the fard remains until the head is raised from the extra prostration according to the mufta bihi view.

Adding Extra Rak'ahs to Make Salah Nafl
Ruling on adding extra rak'ahs to convert a mistakenly lengthened fard prayer into nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding extra rak'ahs to a mistakenly long fard prayer and explain why it becomes permissible due to conflicting disliked aspects (taqaawum).

Core Idea
When two disliked aspects conflict, they neutralize, and the act becomes permissible.

Imagine you are praying Zuhr and mistakenly stand for a fifth rak'ah. What should you do? The Hanafi school provides a clear remedy: you may add a sixth rak'ah to turn the prayer into a nafl. This ruling relies on a fascinating legal principle where two forms of dislike cancel each other out, resulting in permissibility. In this lesson, we will unpack this ruling, its exceptions, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
Recognize that the worshiper has unintentionally performed extra rak'ahs in a fard prayer (e.g., five in Zuhr, three in Fajr).
The extra rak'ah must be unintentional; deliberate addition would invalidate the prayer.
2
State the remedy
If the prayer is one where adding is possible, the worshiper may add another rak'ah to make the total an even number (e.g., add a sixth to make six, add a fourth to make four).
The text explicitly mentions adding a sixth for four-rak'ah prayers and a fourth for Fajr.
3
Note the exception for Maghrib
Maghrib is excluded because adding would make it four rak'ahs (even), but Maghrib must be odd. The text says there is no adding in Maghrib.
For Maghrib, if one prays four, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
4
Explain the reasoning of conflicting dislikes
Two disliked aspects are present: the karahah of offering a solitary nafl (batira') and the karahah of adding for that specific time (e.g., after 'Asr). These two karahahs are equal in strength, so they cancel each other (taqaawum).
The principle is: when two equally undesirable factors conflict, they neutralize, leaving the act permissible (mubah).
5
Determine the final ruling
On the correct view (al-sahih), there is no dislike in adding; it is permissible (mubah) and even recommended (mandub).
The absence of intention to pray nafl at the start is key: 'li-'adam al-qasd hal'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضم سادسة إن شاء لأنه لم يشرع في النفل قصداً ليلزمه إتمامه بل يندب (ولو) في العصر لأن التنفل قبله قصداً لا يكره فبالظن أولى (و) ضم (رابعة في الفجر) وسكت عن المغرب لأنها تصير أربعاً فلا فيها (ولا) كراهة في الضم فيهما أي صلاة الفجر والمغرب لأنه تعارض كراهة التنفل بالبتيراء، وكراهة الضم للوقت فتقاوماً وصار كالمباح ( على الصحيح) لعدم القصد حال
And he may add a sixth if he wishes, because he did not intend to start a nafl, so it is not necessary for him to complete it, rather it is recommended. And (even) in 'Asr, because performing nafl before it intentionally is not disliked, so by doubt it is more appropriate. And he may add a fourth in Fajr. He remained silent about Maghrib because it becomes four, so there is no adding in it. And there is no dislike in adding in these two (i.e., Fajr and Maghrib) because the dislike of performing nafl singly (batira') and the dislike of adding for the time conflicted and balanced each other, so it became permissible (according to the correct view) because there is no intention (of nafl) at the time.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on joining extra rak'ahs when one has mistakenly performed extra rak'ahs in a fard prayer. The context is: after the previous discussion of the fifth rak'ah, if one has prayed five rak'ahs for a four-rak'ah fard (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Isha), he may add a sixth rak'ah to make the entire prayer a nafl (voluntary) of six rak'ahs. He is not obliged to do so; it is recommended. This applies even for 'Asr prayer, because performing nafl after 'Asr deliberately is disliked, but here it is done inadvertently, so it is less problematic. Similarly, for Fajr (two rak'ahs), if one mistakenly prays three, he may add a fourth to make it a nafl of four. For Maghrib (three rak'ahs), if one prays four, he cannot add a fifth because Maghrib is always odd; adding would make it an even number, which is not valid for Maghrib's nature. The text discusses the dislike (karahah) in these additions: normally, performing a nafl alone (batira') is disliked, and also adding to a fard for the specific time (like after 'Asr) has its own dislike. But when these two forms of dislike conflict, they cancel each other out, and the act becomes permissible (mubah) on the correct view. This is because the person did not intend nafl at the time of starting the prayer; it was a mistake.

Key Terms
ضم (damm): Adding an extra rak'ah to make a mistakenly longer fard prayer into a nafl prayer.
البتيراء (al-batira'): A single rak'ah nafl offered alone, which is disliked as it resembles a cut-off action.
تقاوم (taqaawama): Two conflicting disliked aspects cancel each other out, resulting in permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on adding a fourth rak'ah in Fajr prayer when one has mistakenly prayed three?
A) It is obligatory to complete as nafl.
B) It is permissible and recommended (mandub) to add a fourth.
C) It is disliked (makruh) to add a fourth.
D) It is invalid; the prayer must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
When two equally disliked aspects conflict, they neutralize, and the act becomes permissible; thus adding extra rak'ahs to salvage an accidentally long prayer is recommended.

Completing Nafl After Fajr and Following an Imam Who Adds Rak'ahs
Defines rules for nafl continuation at dawn and follower's obligation when imam adds extra rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on completing a nafl prayer when fajr enters, and apply the Hanafi position on the follower's obligation when the imam adds extra rak'ahs.

Core Idea
A nafl begun before fajr is completed as a pair without dislike; a follower's obligation depends on whether the imam returns to sitting.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah addresses two interconnected rulings: first, if one is in the middle of a tahajjud prayer and fajr time enters, he must complete it as a pair (shaf') without dislike; second, a follower who joins an imam who is adding extra rak'ahs (damm) must determine his own obligation based on the imam's actions. The passage also clarifies that sajdah al-sahw is not required for the omission of sitting during the joining, because the deficiency is due to corruption of the nafl, not forgetfulness. The main focus is the follower's scenario, where there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on how many rak'ahs the follower must pray when the imam cuts off the extra rak'ahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The passage begins with one who prays a single rak'ah of tahajjud and then dawn breaks. The ruling is that he completes the prayer as a shaf' (even number) by adding one more rak'ah, and this is not disliked. Note the exception: no sajdah al-sahw is required for leaving the sitting during this joining.
The reasoning: the deficiency ('corruption') is not compensated by prostration because the original nafl is corrupted by the addition, not by forgetfulness.
2
Understand the follower's scenario when imam cuts off
If a follower joins the imam during the joining (damm) and then the imam cuts off the extra rak'ahs, the follower's obligation depends on whether the imam returns to the final sitting. If the imam does not return, the follower must pray six rak'ahs (for a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer). If the imam returns to sitting, the follower prays four rak'ahs.
The reasoning: the follower's ihram was for the obligatory prayer; the imam's cutting off is based on conjecture, so the follower's obligation remains intact.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the follower's rak'ahs
There is a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on how many rak'ahs the follower must pray when the imam cuts off without returning. According to Muhammad, the follower prays six; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (in another narration), the follower prays two. The mufta bihi (fatwa position) is two rak'ahs.
The tarjih authority is al-Tahtawi, who notes that the fatwa is based on the view of the Sahibayn because the imam's exit from the obligatory prayer is firmly established.
4
Apply the ruling on adding extra rak'ahs to nafl
When a person adds an extra rak'ah to his nafl, it is recommended (or obligatory according to some) to add another rak'ah so that the two become a complete nafl. These extra rak'ahs do not substitute for the sunnah of the obligatory prayer. The passage also mentions the follower's obligation according to different views.
This shows the importance of pairing rak'ahs in nafl prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشروع كمن صلى ركعة تهجداً فطلع الفجر يتم شفعاً بلا كراهة (ولا يسجد للسهو) لترك القعود في هذا الضم في الأصح لأنّ النقصان بالفساد لا ينجبر بالسجود، ولو اقتدى به أحد حال الضم، ثم قطع لزمه ست ركعات في التي كانت رباعية لأنه المؤدي بهذه التحريمة وسقوطه عن الإمام للظن، ولم يوجد في حقه بخلاف ما إذا عاد الإمام إلى القعود بعد اقتدائه حيث يلزمه أربع ركعات لأنه لما عاد جعل كأن لم يقم (وإن قعد) الجلوس (الأخير) قدر التشهد (ثم قام) ولو عمداً وقرأ وركع (عاد) للجلوس لأن ما دون الركعة بمحل الرفض (وسلم) فلو سلم قائماً صح وترك السنة لأن السنة التسليم جالساً (من غير إعادة التشهد لعدم بطلانه بالقيام وقال الناطقي : يعيده وإذا مضى على نافلته الزائدة، فالصحيح أن القوم لا يتبعونه لأنه لا اتباع في البدعة، وينتظرونه قعوداً فإن عاد قبل تقييده الزائدة بسجدة اتبعوه في السلام (فإن سجد) سلموا للحال و (لم يبطل فرضه) لوجود الجلوس الأخير (وضم) استحباباً وقيل وجوباً (إليها) أي إلى الزائدة ركعة (أخرى) في المختار لتصير الزائدتان له نافلة) ولا تنوب عن سنة الفرض في الصحيح لأن المواظبة عليها بتحريمة مبتدأة، ولو اقتدى به أحد يصلي ستاً عند محمد لأنه المؤدي بهذه التحريمة وعندهما ركعتين لأنه استحكم خروجه عن الفرض ولا قضاء عليه لو أفسد عن محمد كإمامه، وقضى ركعتين عندهما، وعليه الفتوى لأنّ السقوط يعارض يخص الإمام (وسجد بالبتيراء) تقدم أنه أحد قولين
[The start:] Like one who prayed one rak'ah of tahajjud and then dawn broke: he completes it as a pair without dislike, and he does not perform prostration for forgetfulness for leaving the sitting in this joining, according to the most correct view, because the deficiency due to corruption is not compensated by prostration. If someone followed him at the time of joining and then [the imam] cut off, six rak'ahs become incumbent upon him in what was a four-rak'ah prayer because he is performing by this initiation and its falling from the imam is due to conjecture, and it did not occur in his case—unlike when the imam returns to sitting after his following, where four rak'ahs become incumbent upon him because when he returned, it is as if he did not stand. And if he sits the final sitting [to the extent of] the tashahhud, then stands—even intentionally—and recites and bows, he returns to sitting because what is less than a rak'ah is subject to being discarded, and he gives salams. If he gives salams while standing, it is valid but he leaves the sunnah because the sunnah is to give salams while sitting, without repeating the tashahhud because it is not invalidated by standing. Al-Natiqi said: he repeats it. And when he goes on to his additional supererogatory [rak'ahs], the correct view is that the people do not follow him because there is no following in innovation, and they wait for him while sitting. If he returns before tying the additional [rak'ah] with a prostration, they follow him in the salams. If he prostrates, they give salams immediately, and his obligatory prayer is not invalidated because of the final sitting. And he joins—recommendedly, and it is said obligatorily—to it, i.e., to the additional [rak'ah], another rak'ah according to the chosen view, so that the two additional [rak'ahs] become a supererogatory prayer for him. And it does not substitute for the sunnah of the obligatory [prayer] according to the correct view because performing it consistently is by a separate initiation. And if someone followed him, he prays six according to Muhammad because he is performing by this initiation, and according to [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] two rak'ahs because his exit from the obligatory prayer is firmly established. There is no makeup upon him if he corrupts it according to Muhammad, like his imam, and he makes up two rak'ahs according to them, and the fatwa is upon this because the falling [of obligation] is countered by the specificity of the imam. And he prostrates with 'al-batira' [a type of amputation?]; it was previously mentioned as one of two statements.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya expands on the base text regarding the rules of nafl prayer begun before fajr and the follower's obligation when the imam adds extra rak'ahs. The author begins by stating that if one is in the middle of tahajjud and fajr time enters, he completes his prayer as a shaf' (even number) without it being disliked, and he is not required to perform sajdah al-sahw for omitting the sitting during the joining, because the deficiency caused by the corruption (of the original nafl due to the added rak'ah) cannot be compensated by prostration. The discussion then shifts to a scenario where a follower joins the imam during this joining, and the imam later cuts off the additional rak'ahs. The ruling depends on whether the imam returns to sitting before tying the extra rak'ah with a prostration. If the imam cuts off without returning, the follower must pray a complete six-rak'ah prayer (for a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer), because his ihram was initially for the obligatory prayer and it only fell from the imam due to the uncertainty (zann) of the imam's intention, but this uncertainty does not apply to the follower. If the imam returns to the final sitting (i.e., he abandons the extra rak'ahs), then the follower's obligation reverts to four rak'ahs. The passage then addresses the case of someone who sits for the final tashahhud, then stands up and continues with recitation and bowing: he must return to the sitting because any action less than a full rak'ah is subject to being discarded. He should then give salams while sitting; giving salams while standing is valid but leaves the sunnah. The tashahhud does not need to be repeated because standing did not invalidate it. Al-Natiqi's contrary view is mentioned. When a person adds an extra rak'ah to his nafl, it is recommended (or according to some, obligatory) to add another rak'ah so that the two extra ones form a complete nafl prayer. These extra rak'ahs do not substitute for the sunnah of the obligatory prayer. The passage concludes with a discussion on the follower's obligation when the imam adds extra rak'ahs: according to Muhammad, the follower must pray six rak'ahs; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (in one view?), the follower prays only two rak'ahs, and this is the position of the fatwa.

Key Terms
الضم (al-damm): Joining an extra rak'ah to a nafl prayer to make it a pair.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) that initiates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Six rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) Two rak'ahs
D) Eight rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
A nafl begun before fajr is completed as a pair, and when following an imam who adds extra rak'ahs, the mufta bihi is that the follower prays two rak'ahs if the imam cuts off.

Adding an Extra Rak'ah to Nafl and Its Relation to Sunnah
Ruling on adding a second extra rak'ah and its non-substitution for sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding a second extra rak'ah to a nafl prayer and explain why it does not substitute for the sunnah prayer.

Core Idea
Adding a second extra rak'ah is recommended; it forms a nafl but cannot replace the separate sunnah.

This passage from al-Tahtawi clarifies the legal status of doubling the extra rak'ah during a nafl prayer and addresses whether those two rak'ahs can count as the sunnah mu'akkadah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct prayer practice, as the sunnah requires a separate intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act in question is adding another rak'ah to the already added extra rak'ah during a nafl prayer, making the total two extra rak'ahs.
The base text assumes one has already added one extra rak'ah; now considering a second.
2
Determine the ruling
The passage states it is recommended (mustahabb) according to the chosen view, but some consider it obligatory (wajib).
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; mufta bihi is mustahabb.
3
Understand the purpose
Adding the second rak'ah turns the two extra rak'ahs into a complete nafl prayer, avoiding an odd number.
A nafl should ideally be in pairs (shafa').
4
Analyze the relation to sunnah
These two extra rak'ahs do not substitute for the sunnah prayer (e.g., sunnah of Fajr or Zuhr). The reason is that the sunnah is performed with a separate, independent intention (tahrimah mubtada'ah).
Thus, if someone intended to perform the sunnah by adding these rak'ahs, it would not count.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضم استحباباً وقيل وجوباً (إليها) أي إلى الزائدة ركعة (أخرى) في المختار لتصير الزائدتان له نافلة) ولا تنوب عن سنة الفرض في الصحيح لأن المواظبة عليها بتحريمة مبتدأة
And he joins—recommendedly, and it is said obligatorily—to it, i.e., to the additional [rak'ah], another rak'ah according to the chosen view, so that the two additional [rak'ahs] become a supererogatory prayer for him. And it does not substitute for the sunnah of the obligatory [prayer] according to the correct view because performing it consistently is by a separate initiation.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on adding a second extra rak'ah (damm) to the first extra rak'ah in a nafl prayer. The base text stated that one should add another rak'ah. The commentator notes that this is recommended (istihbab), though some scholars consider it obligatory. The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that it is recommended. The purpose is to make the two extra rak'ahs a complete independent nafl prayer (nāfilah) rather than leaving it as an odd number. However, these two rak'ahs do not substitute for the sunnah mu'akkadah of the obligatory prayer (e.g., the two rak'ahs before Fajr or after Zuhr). The reason is that the sunnah prayer is performed with a separate, specific intention (tahrimah mubtada'ah) and is a distinct act of worship. Therefore, if one intends to perform the sunnah, he should do so separately rather than relying on the extra rak'ahs added during the obligatory prayer.

Key Terms
المواظبة (al-muwāẓabah): Consistent performance; here referring to the sunnah prayer being performed regularly with a separate intention.
تحريمة مبتدأة (taḥrīmah mubtada'ah): A separate initiating takbir (ihram) for a new act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Obligatory
B) Recommended
C) Permissible
D) Disliked

Key Takeaway
Adding a second extra rak'ah to a nafl is recommended, but it cannot serve as the sunnah prayer because each act of worship requires its own intention.

Ruling on Sajdah al-Sahw in Nafl and Building Another Shaf'
Ruling with proof on building after sajdah al-sahw in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on building another shaf' after sajdah al-sahw in nafl prayer and apply the exception for a traveller who intends iqamah.

Core Idea
Building another shaf' after sajdah al-sahw invalidates the sajdah; repeat it unless building is required to correct an obligatory prayer.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on what happens when a person performs sajdah al-sahw in a nafl shaf' and then builds another shaf' upon it. The passage distinguishes between prohibited building and a necessary building for a traveller, clarifying the consequences and the rationale behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is building another shaf' (pair of rak'ahs) after performing sajdah al-sahw in a nafl prayer. The default ruling is that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to do so, as the text says 'لم يبن ... استحباباً' meaning it is recommended not to build.
The ruling is specific to nafl prayers, not obligatory ones.
2
Understand the rationale
Sajdah al-sahw is meant to be the final act of the prayer to correct forgetfulness. Building another shaf' places it in the middle of the prayer, which invalidates the sajdah because it was not performed at the end.
This reasoning is based on the talil (cause) mentioned in the text.
3
Determine the consequence if performed
If one does build, the initiation (tahrimah) of the new shaf' is valid, but the original sajdah al-sahw is invalidated. Therefore, he must repeat the sajdah al-sahw at the end of the newly built shaf'.
The text says 'صح التحريمة وأعاد سجود السهو'.
4
Recognize the exception
A traveller who intends iqamah (to stay) after performing sajdah al-sahw in his nafl must build another shaf' to correct his obligatory prayer (because his intention changes the nafl to obligatory). In this case, building is necessary, and he still repeats the sajdah.
This exception is specific to the traveller scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسجد للسهو لتأخير سلامه (ولو سجد للسهو في شفع التطوع لم يبن شفعاً آخر عليه استحباباً) لأن البناء يبطل سجوده للسهو بلا ضرورة لوقوعه في وسط الصلاة (فإن بني) صح التحريمة وأعاد سجود السهو في المختار) وهو الأصح لبطلان الأول بما طرأ من البناء، وقيدنا بالتطوع لأن المسافر إذا نوى الإقامة بعد سجوده للسهو يبني تصحيحاً لفرضه، ويعيد سجود السهو لبطلان ذاك بالبناء
And he prostrated for forgetfulness due to delaying his salams. And if he prostrated for forgetfulness in a shaf' of supererogatory prayer, he should not build another shaf' upon it, as a recommendation, because building invalidates his prostration for forgetfulness without necessity due to its occurrence in the middle of the prayer. If he builds, the initiation is valid and he repeats the prostration for forgetfulness according to the chosen view, and it is the most correct, because the first [prostration] is invalidated by what occurred of building. And we restricted it to supererogatory because if a traveller intends iqamah after his prostration for forgetfulness, he builds to correct his obligatory prayer, and he repeats the prostration for forgetfulness because that one is invalidated by the building.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage addresses sajdah al-sahw in supererogatory (nafl) prayers. The base text states that if one performs sajdah al-sahw in a shaf' (pair of rak'ahs) of tatawwu', he should not build another shaf' upon it, meaning he should not begin a new pair immediately after the sajdah. The reason is that sajdah al-sahw is meant to be the final act of the prayer, and performing further prayer after it would place the sajdah in the middle of the prayer, which is invalid. However, if one does build, the new initiation (tahrimah) is valid, but he must repeat the sajdah al-sahw at the end of this new prayer because the first sajdah was invalidated by the subsequent building. The commentator notes an exception: a traveller who intends to stay (iqamah) after performing sajdah al-sahw in his nafl must build (continue) to correct his obligatory prayer, and he repeats the sajdah. This is because the building here is necessary to salvage the obligatory prayer, and the first sajdah is invalidated by the new intention.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): An even number of rak'ahs, specifically a pair in supererogatory prayer.
البناء (al-binā’): Continuing the prayer by adding another shaf' after sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing; the sajdah is valid and the prayer is complete
B) Repeat the sajdah al-sahw at the end of the new shaf'
C) Cancel the entire prayer and start over
D) Perform an additional sajdah for each rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Building another shaf' after sajdah al-sahw in nafl invalidates the sajdah, which must be repeated; an exception occurs when the building is necessary to correct an obligatory prayer, as in the case of a traveller intending iqamah.

Following an Imam with Sajdah al-Sahw
Ruling on following an imam with sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid following of an imam who gave salams but has sajdah al-sahw, and explain the legal rationale using the concept of mawqūf.

Core Idea
Following an imam who gave salams but must perform sajdah al-sahw is valid only if the imam performs the sajdah.

You are praying behind an imam who, after giving salams, realizes he forgot a prostration. He then performs sajdah al-sahw. Is your prayer valid? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling: your prayer is valid if the imam performs the sajdah, because his exit from prayer was suspended (mawqūf). Understanding this ruling requires grasping the concept of suspension and how it affects the follower's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario: an imam has sajdah al-sahw upon him (i.e., he omitted or added something requiring correction). He gives salams, so outwardly his prayer has ended. A follower begins praying behind him.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling: the follower's prayer is valid if the imam subsequently performs the sajdah al-sahw. If he does not, the follower's prayer is invalid.
3
Understand the legal concept: mawqūf (suspended)
The imam's exit from prayer was 'suspended' (mawqūf). This means his prayer is not fully concluded until he performs the required sajdah. When he does the sajdah, he re-enters the sanctity of prayer, making his original salams effective retroactively.
This concept is unique to Hanafi fiqh regarding sajdah al-sahw.
4
Apply the ruling to the follower
The follower's prayer is built on the imam's. Since the imam's prayer is still valid (pending the sajdah), the follower's following is valid on condition that the sajdah is performed. The follower should follow the imam in the sajdah and does not need to repeat it at the end of his own prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سلم من عليه سجود سهو فاقتدى به غيره صح إن سجد) الساهي للسهو لعوده لحرمة الصلاة لأن خروجه كان موقوفاً ويتابعه المقتدي في السجود، ولا يعيده في آخر صلاته وإن وقع في خلالها لأنه آخر صلاته حكماً وحقيقة لإمامه كما تقدم ( وإلا ) أي ، وإن لم يسجد الساهي (فلا يصح الإقتداء به لتبين خروجه من الصلاة
And if one who has a prostration for forgetfulness gives salams, and another follows him, it is valid if the forgetful one prostrates for forgetfulness because he returns to the sanctity of prayer; his exit was suspended, and the follower follows him in the prostration, and does not repeat it at the end of his own prayer even if it occurs in the middle, because it is the end of his prayer virtually and actually for his imam, as previously mentioned. Otherwise, i.e., if the forgetful one does not prostrate, then following him is not valid because it becomes clear that he has exited the prayer.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a person who has sajdah al-sahw upon him (i.e., he forgot something in prayer and must perform sajdah al-sahw). If such a person gives salams (thinking his prayer is complete) and then another person starts to follow him as an imam, the following is valid only if the imam subsequently performs the sajdah al-sahw. The reason is that the imam's exit from prayer was suspended; by performing the sajdah, he re-enters the sanctity of prayer, and the follower's prayer is built on that. The follower should follow the imam in the sajdah and does not need to repeat it at the end of his own prayer, because for the imam this sajdah is the actual end of his prayer. However, if the imam does not perform the sajdah, then it becomes clear that he had already exited the prayer, so the follower's prayer was invalid from the start.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawqūf): Suspended; the imam's exit from prayer is pending until he performs the necessary corrective action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the follower performs sajdah al-sahw on his own
B) If the imam performs the sajdah al-sahw
C) If the follower repeats the entire prayer
D) It is never valid

Key Takeaway
Following an imam who gave salams but has sajdah al-sahw is valid only if the imam performs the sajdah; the concept of mawqūf makes this possible.

Cause of Sajdah al-Sahw in Nafl: Dispute Between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on the cause of sajdah al-sahw in the case of damm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the views of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Abu Bakr ibn Abi Said on the cause of sajdah al-sahw in the damm case, and explain why Muhammad's view is considered the musahhih.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, the cause of sajdah al-sahw when transitioning from fard to nafl is a deficiency in the obligatory prayer (Muhammad's view), not in the nafl.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi debate on the legal cause ('illa) that necessitates sajdah al-sahw when an imam adds extra rak'ahs after completing the fard. While all agree that sajdah is wajib, they differ on whether the deficiency lies in the fard, the nafl, or the ihram itself. Understanding this dispute refines our appreciation of how Hanafi jurists analyze causes within prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the qiyas baseline
Recognize that qiyas would dictate no sajdah because the forgetfulness occurred in the original fard prayer, not in the new nafl prayer.
Qiyas would separate the two prayers.
2
State the istihsan override
All Hanafi imams agree that sajdah is required by istihsan, despite qiyas, to compensate for the deficiency.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.
3
Distinguish the three causes
Abu Yusuf: deficiency in the nafl (entered incorrectly). Muhammad: deficiency in the fard (left wajib salam). Abu Bakr: deficiency in the ihram itself.
Each imam locates the deficiency differently.
4
Understand the tarjih
The author declares Muhammad's view as the musahhih (corrector), meaning it is the relied-upon position in Zahir al-Riwayah.
Muhammad's view becomes the mufta bihi.
5
Note al-Maturidi's preferred view
Al-Maturidi considers Abu Bakr's combined view the most correct, but the Zahir al-Riwayah remains with Muhammad.
This shows nuance within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالمصحح قول محمد قوله : ( وسجد للسهو) راجع للمسألتين جميعاً، أما الأولى وهي ما إذا عاد، وسلم قبل أن يسجد فظاهر لما ذكره المؤلف، وأما الثانية، وهي ما إذا لم يعد حتى سجد، فالقياس أن لا يسجد لأنه في صلاة غير التي سها فيها، ومن سها في صلاة لا يسجد في الأخرى وفي الاستحسان يسجد وسببه نقصان تمكن في النفل بالدخول فيه على غير الوجه الواجب إذ الواجب فيه أن يكون بتحريمة مبتدأة وهذه للفرض وقد انقطعت بالانتقال، إلى النفل، ومراعاة حدود النفل على المباشر واجبة، وإن لم يكن النفل واجباً، وهذا عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد سببه نقصان تمكن في الفرض بترك واجب السلام، ولا نقصان في النقل لأنه بنى على التحريمة الأولى وهي لم تنقطع لأنها اشتملت على الأصل والوصف، وبالانتقال إلى النفل ينقطع الوصف للمنافاة بين وصفي الفرض، والنقل دون الأصل، فبقي الإحرام في حق الأصل على ما كان وذهب أبو بكر بن أبي سعيد إلى أن سبب هذا السجود نقصان تمكن في الإحرام فحينئذ يكون لكل من الفرض والنفل حظ من النقص، والجبر، ونص الشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي على أنه الأصح
So the corrector is the statement of Muhammad. His statement: 'And he prostrates for forgetfulness' refers to both issues. As for the first—when he returned and gave salams before prostrating—it is apparent from what the author mentioned. As for the second—when he did not return until he prostrated—the analogy is that he should not prostrate because he is in a prayer other than the one in which he forgot, and one who forgets in a prayer does not prostrate in another. But according to istihsan, he prostrates, and its cause is a deficiency that occurred in the supererogatory prayer by entering into it in a manner not obligatory, since the obligatory in it is that it be by a separate initiation, and this [initiation] was for the obligatory prayer and was interrupted by the transition to the supererogatory. Observing the limits of the supererogatory is obligatory upon the performer, even if the supererogatory itself is not obligatory. This is according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, its cause is a deficiency that occurred in the obligatory prayer by leaving the obligatory salam, and there is no deficiency in the supererogatory because he built upon the first initiation which was not severed because it comprised both the essence and the description. By transitioning to the supererogatory, the description is severed due to the incompatibility between the descriptions of obligatory and supererogatory, while the essence remains. So the ihram remained in respect of the essence as it was. Abu Bakr ibn Abi Said held that the cause of this prostration is a deficiency in the ihram itself, so each of the obligatory and supererogatory has a share of the deficiency and its compensation. Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi declared this to be the most correct.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the cause of sajdah al-sahw in the scenario where a person adds extra rak'ahs to his prayer (damm). The author clarifies that the correct position (musahhih) is that of Muhammad (Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani). The discussion centers on two cases: (1) when the imam returns to the final sitting and gives salams before prostrating, and (2) when he does not return but prostrates directly. In the second case, qiyas would dictate that no sajdah is needed because the forgetfulness occurred in the original prayer, not in the new nafl prayer. However, istihsan requires sajdah. Abu Yusuf explains that the cause is a deficiency in the nafl because it was entered upon with a changed intention. Muhammad argues that the cause is a deficiency in the obligatory prayer due to missing the obligatory salam, and the nafl is not deficient because it was built on the original ihram which remains intact in essence. Abu Bakr ibn Abi Said synthesizes both, attributing the deficiency to the ihram itself. Al-Maturidi considers this combined view the most correct.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) in this case.
المصحح (al-muṣaḥḥiḥ): The one who corrects or the correct view; here referring to Muhammad's position as the sound one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to which Hanafi imam is the cause of sajdah al-sahw in the case of damm a deficiency in the obligatory prayer (fard)?
A) Abu Yusuf
B) Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Abu Bakr ibn Abi Said
D) Abu Mansur al-Maturidi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school unanimously obligates sajdah al-sahw in the damm case by istihsan, but the cause is attributed to the fard according to the relied-upon view of Muhammad.

Building Additional Rak'ahs After Sujud al-Sahw in Nafl Prayer
Ruling on building nafl after sujud and intra-Hanafi dispute on cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building nafl rak'ahs after Sujud al-Sahw and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on its cause.

Core Idea
Building after sujud in nafl invalidates the first sujud; it must be repeated.

Sujud al-Sahw is performed at the end of prayer. But what if a person performing nafl prostrates for forgetfulness, then decides to add more rak'ahs? The Hanafi scholars discuss the validity and the need to repeat the sujud. This lesson examines the ruling and the subtle difference between Imams Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is building (adding a new pair of rak'ahs) after performing Sujud al-Sahw in a nafl prayer. The ruling is that it is discouraged (makruh) to build, but if done, the tahrima is valid and the sujud must be repeated.
The ruling is specific to nafl; fard has different rules.
2
Understand the invalidation of first sujud
Why does building invalidate the first sujud? Because the sujud is placed in the middle of the prayer, which is not its proper place. The first sujud becomes nullified by the additional rak'ahs.
Building after sujud means the prayer continues, so the sujud was premature.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree that the sujud must be repeated, but they differ on the sabab (cause). Abu Yusuf: the deficiency is in the nafl due to improper entry. Muhammad: the deficiency is in the fard due to leaving the wajib salam.
Abu Hanifa's position is not explicitly stated; the dispute is between the Sahibayn.
4
Apply the chosen view (mufta bihi)
The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that repeating the sujud is obligatory (wajib). This is based on caution: the first sujud is invalid, so a new sujud is needed.
The tarjih authority is al-Tahtawi, who calls it al-asah (most correct).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لبقاء للسهو) لتأخير سلامه (ولو سجد للسهو في شفع التطوع لم يبن شفعاً آخر عليه استحباباً) لأن البناء يبطل سجوده للسهو بلا ضرورة لوقوعه في وسط الصلاة (فإن بني) صح التحريمة وأعاد سجود السهو في المختار) وهو الأصح لبطلان الأول بما طرأ من البناء، وقيدنا بالتطوع لأن المسافر إذا نوى الإقامة بعد سجوده للسهو يبني تصحيحاً لفرضه، ويعيد سجود السهو لبطلان ذاك بالبناء
[The sujud is] for the delay of his salam. (And if he prostrates for forgetfulness in a nafl pair, he should not build another pair upon it, as a recommendation) because building invalidates his sujud without necessity, as it occurs in the middle of the prayer. (If he builds) the tahrima is valid and he repeats the sujud in the chosen view, which is the most correct, because the first is invalidated by the building that occurred. And we restricted it to nafl because a traveller who intends to stay after his sujud builds to correct his fard and repeats the sujud for forgetfulness due to the invalidation of that [sujud] by building.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that one should not build (add a new pair of rak'ahs) after performing Sujud al-Sahw in a nafl prayer; doing so is only recommended against (istihbaban). The sharh explains why: building places the sujud in the middle of prayer, which is not its proper place. However, if one does build, the tahrima (opening takbir) remains valid, and he must repeat the Sujud al-Sahw at the end because the initial sujud is nullified by the intervening building. This ruling is specific to nafl; in fard, building is not allowed. The exception is a traveller who, after sujud in nafl, intends to stay (thus converting his prayer to fard); he must build to save his fard and then repeat the sujud. The commentary then notes an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf holds the cause of sujud in this case is a deficiency in the nafl due to improper entry (since the nafl should have been started with a new tahrima), while Muhammad holds the cause is a deficiency in the fard due to leaving the obligatory salam. The preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that the sujud must be repeated upon building.

Key Terms
البناء (al-bina'): Adding additional rak'ahs (a new pair) onto the existing prayer without a new takbir tahrima.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The initial takbir that enters one into the state of prayer (ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) He must repeat the Sujud al-Sahw at the end.
C) He must perform a new takbir tahrima and restart.
D) No action is needed; the sujud is valid.

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, building additional rak'ahs after Sujud al-Sahw invalidates the first sujud, making it obligatory to repeat the sujud at the end.

Following an Imam Who Owes Sujud al-Sahw
Ruling on iqtida behind an imam who has not yet performed sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar regarding the validity of following an imam who omitted Sujud al-Sahw, and state the practical consequence (thamarah) of this intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
The follower's prayer hinges on whether the imam's exit from prayer was suspended or immediate.

When an imam forgets and owes Sujud al-Sahw, his salam does not necessarily end the prayer. This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the follower's prayer if the imam fails to perform that sujud. You will learn the two views, the underlying legal concept of 'suspended exit', and the practical difference that matters for your own prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the specific problem? A person (follower) prays behind an imam who gave salam but did not perform the obligatory Sujud al-Sahw. Is the follower's prayer valid?
The issue arises from the imam's forgetfulness after salam.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the follower's prayer is invalid. Muhammad and Zufar hold it is valid. Note both positions clearly.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Trace the underlying principle
The concept of 'khuruj mawquf' (suspended exit). According to Muhammad/Zufar, the imam's exit from prayer is suspended until after he performs the sujud; thus his salam does not actually end the prayer. Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf disagree, holding that exit occurs at salam unless the imam returns for sujud.
This principle determines the status of the imam's prayer after salam.
4
Apply the thamarah
The practical consequence (thamarah): if the imam omits sujud, the follower's prayer is valid according to Muhammad/Zufar, but invalid according to Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf. Also, loudly laughing in prayer invalidates wudu only according to Muhammad/Zufar.
The thamarah is the real-world ruling that changes.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text presents Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view first and states 'contrary to Muhammad and Zufar', implying it is the relied-upon position. Thus in fatwa, the follower's prayer is invalid if the imam does not perform sujud.
The mufta bihi is the position of the two shaykhs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سلم من عليه سجود سهو فاقتدى به غيره صح إن سجد الساهي للسهو لعوده لحرمة الصلاة لأن خروجه كان موقوفاً ويتابعه المقتدي في السجود، ولا يعيده في آخر صلاته وإن وقع في خلالها لأنه آخر صلاته حكماً وحقيقة لإمامه كما تقدم، وإلا بأن لم يسجد الساهي فلا يصح الإقتداء به لتبين خروجه من الصلاة حين سلم عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى خلافاً لمحمد وزفر وثمرته بصحة اقتدائه عندهما لا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وفي انتقاض الطهارة بقهقهته
And if one upon whom there is Sujud al-Sahw gives salam, and another person follows him, it is valid if the forgetful one prostrates for forgetfulness, because he returns to the sanctity of prayer, as his exit was suspended. And the follower follows him in the sujud, and does not repeat it at the end of his own prayer, even if it occurs in the middle, because it is the end of his prayer both in ruling and reality for his imam, as previously explained. Otherwise, if the forgetful one does not prostrate, then following him is not valid, because it becomes clear that he exited from prayer at the time of salam according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar. The fruit of the difference is the validity of following him according to them (Muhammad and Zufar), not according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and similarly regarding the invalidation of ablution by loud laughter.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute about following an imam who has given salam but still owes Sujud al-Sahw. The matn states that if the imam does perform the sujud, the follower's prayer is valid because the imam's exit from prayer was suspended; he returns to the state of prayer, and the follower joins him in the sujud. The follower does not need to repeat the sujud later. If the imam does not perform the sujud, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the follower's prayer is invalid because it becomes clear that the imam had actually exited from prayer at the time of salam. However, Muhammad and Zufar hold that the follower's prayer is valid regardless, because the imam's salam is not a true exit until after the sujud. The practical difference (thamarh) is that if the imam omits sujud, the follower's prayer is valid according to Muhammad and Zufar but invalid according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Additionally, there is a related difference regarding whether loud laughter invalidates wudu: according to Muhammad and Zufar it does, while according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it does not.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer.
الخروج الموقوف (al-khuruj al-mawquf): A suspended exit from prayer; the imam is considered in prayer until he performs the obligatory sujud.
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter in prayer that invalidates purity and prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The follower's prayer is valid because the imam's exit was suspended.
B) The follower's prayer is invalid because the imam's exit is confirmed.
C) The follower must perform Sujud al-Sahw on his own.
D) The follower's prayer is valid only if he also forgets.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following an imam who owes sujud depends on whether he performs it; the majority Hanafi view requires the sujud for the follower's prayer to be valid.

Sujud al-Sahw for Intentional Salam: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling on Sujud al-Sahw for intentional salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Sujud al-Sahw is wajib after an intentional salam, and identify the two actions (turning from qibla or speaking) that negate the need for sujud.

Core Idea
Intentional salam alone does not break prayer; sujud is wajib unless followed by turning or speaking.

Imagine you are in prayer and inadvertently say the salam with the intention to end the prayer. Does your prayer become invalid? The Hanafi school teaches that mere intention does not break the prayer, and since the salam itself is a form of dhikr, the prayer remains valid but requires Sujud al-Sahw. However, if you turn away from the qibla or speak immediately after, those actions invalidate the prayer altogether, making sujud unnecessary. This lesson unpacks this nuanced ruling and the proofs behind it.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its default ruling
Identify that the act is intentional salam during prayer with the intention to cut off. The default ruling is that Sujud al-Sahw is wajib, unless an exemption applies.
The ruling is 'wajib' not fard because it arises from a forgetful act that can be compensated.
2
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The text gives a rational proof: 'mere intention to change the prescribed act does not invalidate it' and 'the salam is dhikr, so sujud is due due to the remaining sanctity of prayer.' Understand that the prayer's inviolability (tahrimah) persists until an overt invalidating action occurs.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the principles of prayer.
3
Identify the exceptions
The text states that if the person turns away from the qibla or speaks, these actions invalidate the tahrimah, so no sujud is required. Note the disagreement (qil) that turning alone does not harm if he does not leave the mosque or speak.
The mufta bihi is that turning away does break the prayer, as it is an external action.
4
Apply the ruling to a related case
Consider the case of someone who owes a sajdah (prostration for recitation or fard) and gives salam while remembering the obligation. His salam is invalid and he remains in prayer. This illustrates the principle that an extra salam without proper cause does not exit the prayer.
The details of derivations are in longer works.
5
Distinguish wahm and zann
The text ends with a brief definition: wahm is when error is more probable, zann is when correctness is more probable. Understand that these are epistemological terms used in usul al-fiqh, not directly needed for this ruling.
This is an aside for clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسجد للسهو وجوباً وإن سلم عامداً مريداً للقطع لأن مجرد نية تغيير المشروع لا تبطله ولا تعتبر مع سلام غير مستحق وهو ذكر فيسجد للسهو لبقاء حرمة الصلاة ما لم يتحول عن القبلة، أو يتكلم لإبطالهما التحريمة وقيل : التحول لا يضره ما لم يخرج من المسجد أو يتكلم وسلام من عليه سجدة صلبية أو فرض متذكراً مبطل لوجوده في حقيقة الصلاة وتفريعاته مبسوطة في الأصل توهم الوهم رجحان جهة الخطأ والظن رجحان جهة الصلاة له
And he prostrates for forgetfulness as an obligation, even if he intentionally gave salam intending to cut off, because mere intention to change the prescribed act does not invalidate it, and it is not considered along with a salam that is not deserved, and it is dhikr, so he prostrates for forgetfulness due to the remaining sanctity of prayer, unless he turns away from the qibla or speaks, because these invalidate the tahrima. And it is said that turning does not harm him as long as he does not leave the mosque or speak. And the salam of one upon whom there is a bodily prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) or a fard prostration, while remembering it, invalidates his existence in the reality of prayer. Its derivations are detailed in the original. And wahm is the preponderance of the side of error, and zann is the preponderance of the side of correctness for him.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage contains multiple rulings on Sujud al-Sahw. First, it is wajib to perform Sujud al-Sahw if one says salam intentionally with the intention to end the prayer. The proof given is that mere intention to change the prescribed act does not invalidate it, and the salam (being dhikr) does not break the prayer unless accompanied by an action that nullifies the tahrima. The prayer's sanctity remains, so sujud is wajib. However, if he turns away from the qibla or speaks (with intention to leave), these actions invalidate the tahrima, so sujud is not due. There is a differing view (qil) that turning away does not harm as long as he does not leave the mosque or speak. Next, the text covers the case of one who owes a sajdah salbiyyah (prostration for a verse of prostration) or a fard prostration (rain? unsure) and gives salam while remembering his obligation: his salam is invalid and his prayer is still considered in progress. The details are in longer works. Finally, a brief definition: wahm is the greater likelihood of error, zann is the greater likelihood of correctness.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness; wajib in Hanafi school.
نية القطع (niyyat al-qat'): Intention to end the prayer; alone does not invalidate.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The inviolable state of prayer; actions like turning from qibla or speaking break it.
الوهم (al-wahm): A state of uncertainty where error is more probable.
الظن (al-zann): Preponderant belief (ghalabat al-zann) that something is correct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) In all cases of intentional salam.
C) Only if he does not turn away from the qibla or speak.
D) Only if he remembers his obligation after salam.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib after an intentional salam if the person does not turn away from the qibla or speak, as those actions would break the prayer and negate the need for sujud.

Completing Prayer After Forgetful Salām and Sajdah al-Sahw
Ruling on completing prayer after forgetful salām and prostration of forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that forgetful salām does not invalidate prayer, and state the conditions for completing the prayer and performing sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
A forgetful salām does not end the prayer; completion and sajdah al-sahw are obligatory before any nullifying action.

Many students mistakenly believe that any premature salām immediately invalidates the prayer. However, the Hanafī school, relying on the hadith of Dhū al-Yadayn, holds that the prayer's inviolability (ḥurmah) remains until a proven nullifier (munāfī) occurs. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and the critical condition that preserves the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a person who prays a four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah obligatory prayer (including witr) but makes salām prematurely after only two rak'ahs (or forgets a prostration).
Only obligatory prayers are covered; supererogatory prayers have a different ruling.
2
State the ruling
If the person remembers before doing any nullifying action (munāfī), he must complete the missed rak'ahs or prostration, then perform sajdah al-sahw.
The ruling is wājib (obligatory) because the prayer remains valid but deficient.
3
Understand the proof
The hadith of Dhū al-Yadayn shows the Prophet (peace be upon him) completing his prayer after forgetful salām; the Hanafīs derive wujūb from his command to prostrate.
The evidence is from āḥād sunnah (zannī al-thubūt and zannī al-dalālah), hence the ruling is wājib, not farḍ.
4
Note the exception
The ruling differs when one makes salām due to a mistaken assumption (e.g., thinking he is a traveler). In that case, the prayer is invalid because the intention changes.
This exception is mentioned in the passage as 'unlike salām on the assumption that he is a traveller'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصل (رباعية فريضة أو ثلاثية) ولو وتراً إنه أتمها فسلم ثم علم قبل إتيانه بمناف أنه صلى ركعتين أو علم أنه ترك سجدة صلبية أو تلاوية أتمها بفعل ما تركه وسجد للسهو لبقاء حرمة الصلاة بخلاف السلام على ظن أنه مسافر أو نحوه كما تقدم
A person prays a four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah obligatory prayer - even if it is witr - that he completed it and made salām, then he knows before coming with a nullifier that he prayed two rak'ahs, or knows that he left an essential prostration or a recital prostration; he completes it by doing what he left, and prostrates for forgetfulness due to the remaining inviolability of the prayer, unlike salām on the assumption that he is a traveller or similar, as has preceded.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage states a key ruling regarding forgetfulness in prayer. The lesson type is a ruling with proof. The author, in his hashīyah, clarifies the position of the Hanafī school. The ruling: If a person performs an obligatory prayer of four or three rak'ahs (including witr) and mistakenly completes it with salām after two rak'ahs (or forgets a prostrate element), but then remembers before doing anything that explicitly invalidates prayer (like speaking or leaving the mosque), he should not consider his prayer broken. Instead, he completes the remaining rak'ahs or the missed prostration, and then performs the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). The reason is that the inviolability (ḥurmah) of the prayer remains until a proven nullifier occurs. This is based on the well-know hadith of Dhū al-Yadayn, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) completed his prayer after forgetful salām. The condition 'before doing a nullifier' is crucial: if he had spoken or turned away from the qiblah intentionally, his prayer would be invalid, and he would start over. The Hanafī school distinguishes this from the case where one deliberately gives salām intending to end the prayer – that salām is invalid and requires sajdah al-sahw. The exception mentioned ('unlike salām on the assumption that he is a traveller') refers to a situation where one mistaken about being a traveller and shortens the prayer; that case has its own rule discussed elsewhere.

Key Terms
مناف (munāfī): An action that nullifies the prayer, such as speaking, eating, or turning away from qiblah intentionally.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness that does not invalidate the prayer.
حرمة الصلاة (ḥurmat al-ṣalāh): The inviolability of the prayer, which means the prayer remains legally intact until a clear nullifier occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person prays Zuhr (four rak'ahs) but mistakenly gives salam after two rak'ahs and then remembers before speaking or leaving, what must he do?
A) Repeat the entire prayer from the beginning
B) Complete the remaining two rak'ahs and perform sajdah al-sahw
C) Do nothing because the salam already ended the prayer
D) Only perform sajdah al-sahw without completing rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The prayer's inviolability remains until a nullifier occurs; premature salam due to forgetfulness does not break the prayer, and completion with sajdah al-sahw is obligatory.

Salam Based on Illusion of Completion vs Intentional Salam
Ruling on salam after assuming completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between salam based on wahm (illusion of completion) and intentional salam with knowledge, and apply the Hanafi ruling on completing the prayer with sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
Salam based on illusion of completion does not nullify prayer; intentional salam with knowledge does.

When a person prays and mistakenly thinks they have completed the required rak'ahs, saying salam, then realizes the mistake—what happens to the prayer? The classical Hanafi position, rooted in the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him), distinguishes between genuine forgetfulness (tawahhum) and intentional action. This lesson will unpack that distinction, its legal consequences, and the underlying proof from the hadith of Dhu al-Yadain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first part of the passage: one prays a four-rak'ah fard (or three, including witr), assumes completion, says salam, then discovers missing rak'ahs or a prostration. The ruling: complete the missed part and perform sujud al-sahw.
This is the core scenario—salam based on wahm (illusion of completion).
2
Classify the salam as tawahhum vs intentional
The passage distinguishes between salam done with the belief that the prayer is complete (wahm) and salam done with knowledge that the prayer is incomplete. The former does not nullify; the latter does. Study the definitions of wahm (stronger inclination towards error) and zann (stronger inclination towards correctness) provided by the commentator.
Wahm is the key concept here—it explains why the salam is excused.
3
Apply the exception for misidentified prayer types
The passage lists scenarios where one misidentifies the prayer (e.g., thinking Zuhr is Jumu'ah, or a new Muslim thinking four rak'ahs are two). In these cases, the salam is considered intentional because the person knows the number of rak'ahs performed, so the prayer is nullified.
Note the contrast: misidentification of the type, not the count, leads to nullification.
4
Examine the dalil (proof)
The passage cites the hadith of Dhu al-Yadain, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed sujud al-sahw after salam due to forgetfulness. This demonstrates that the salam did not nullify the prayer, and the missing rak'ahs were completed with additional sujud.
The hadith is transmitted as ahad (individual) but is accepted due to being in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The commentator mentions a weak opinion that intentional salam does not nullify unless one intends to address a human. The relied-upon view is that any intentional salam (knowing the prayer is incomplete) nullifies the prayer. The commentator declares the weak opinion as da'if.
This dispute is resolved by the weight of the evidence and later Hanafi consensus.

(Passage from the hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah: The text says: 'One who prays a four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah obligatory prayer, even witr, and completes it, then says salam, then knows before doing anything contradictory, that he prayed two rak'ahs, or knows that he left an obligatory or tilawah prostration, then he completes it by doing what he left, and performs sujud al-sahw because the sanctity of the prayer remains, unlike one who says salam thinking he is a traveler or similar. Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah deals with a specific case of forgetfulness in prayer: a person prays a four-rak'ah fard or witr, thinks he has completed it, says salam, and then realizes he only prayed two rak'ahs or missed a prostration. The ruling is that he should complete the missed part and perform sujud al-sahw, because the prayer is still intact (the salam did not nullify it since it was based on a misunderstanding). This is distinguished from cases where one says salam knowing exactly what he did (intentional salam) which does nullify. The commentator then delves into the terminology of wahn and zann, clarifying that wahn is the stronger inclination towards error, while zann is the stronger inclination towards correctness. The hadith of Dhu al-Yadain (the long-armed companion) is cited as evidence: the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed sujud al-sahw in such a situation. The commentator also discusses the issue of turning away from the qibla and leaving the mosque, which in some cases necessitates returning. Finally, the passage addresses scenarios where one assumes the prayer type incorrectly (e.g., thinking Zuhr is Jumu'ah, or a new Muslim thinking four rak'ahs are two). In those cases, the salam is intentional (because he knows he prayed a certain number but mislabels it), so the prayer is nullified. This is contrasted with the first case where the salam was based on an illusion of completion.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm): The stronger inclination towards error (رجحان جهة الخطأ) as per the author; the weaker side in a matter of doubt.
الظن (al-zann): The stronger inclination towards correctness (رجحان جهة الصواب); the preponderant side of a non-certain belief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
