When Prolonged Thought in Prayer Requires Sujud al-Sahw
Clarifies when prolonged thought triggers sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which prolonged thought (tafakkur) during prayer necessitates sujud al-sahw, and apply the measure of a rukn (three tasbihat) to determine obligation.

Core Idea
Only thought lasting longer than a tashahhud plus one rukn (≈3 tasbihat) triggers sujud al-sahw.

Uncertainty about a missed prayer action can lead to prolonged thought. This lesson, from the Hanafi commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, clarifies exactly how long the thought must be to make sujud al-sahw obligatory. The key is a precise threshold: the time of reciting the tashahhud plus performing one rukn, estimated at three tasbihat. Shorter thoughts are excused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
The passage describes a person who is certain they missed an action, but remains in thought without saying salam until they become certain.
The doubt is about a specific missed action, not about the number of rak'ahs in general.
2
Measure the duration of thought
Determine if the thought lasted longer than the time needed to recite the tashahhud plus perform one rukn.
The tashahhud can be the first or final; the rukn is estimated at three tasbihat.
3
Apply the ruling
If thought exceeded that threshold, sujud al-sahw is wajib because a wajib (standing for third rak'ah or salam) was delayed. Otherwise, no sujud.
Also: if the person engaged in recitation or tasbih during doubt, no sujud is needed even if thought was prolonged.
4
Note the refinement
The commentator (al-Tahtawi) refines the base text by explaining the measure of a rukn and the exception for recitation/tasbih.
This clarifies the earlier ambiguous phrasing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وإن طال تفكره) لتيقن المتروك (ولم يسلم حتى استيقن المتروك (إن كان) زمن التفكر زائداً عن التشهد قدر أداء ركن وجب عليه سجود السهو لتأخيره واجب القيام للثالثة ( وإلا ) أي إن لم يكن تفكره قدر أداء ركن (لا) يسجد لكونه عفواً. (1) قوله (قوله كان ظن أن الظهر (جمعة هكذا في الأصل المطبوع ولا وجود لذلك في الشرح كما ترى فالأولي ما في نسخة أخرى ونصه (قوله أو نحوه) كأن ظن أن الظهر جمعة أو كان قريب عهد الخ تأمل اه مصححه قوله : زائداً عن (التشهد أي الأول أو الثاني سواء كان بعد الفراغ من الصلاة والأدعية أو قبلهما قوله: (وجب عليه سجود السهو) إذا شغله التفكر عن أداء واجب بقدر ركن، أو شغله عن الوضوء بعد سبق الحدث لشكه أنه صلى ثلاثاً أو أربعاً يجب السهو، وإلا فلا كذا في الشرح، ولم يبينوا قدر الركن وعلى قياس ما تقدم أن يعتبر سنته، وهو مقدر بثلاث تسبيحات ثم أن محل وجوب سجود السهو إذا لم يشتغل حالة الشك بقراءة، ولا تسبيح أما إذا اشتغل بهما، فلا سهو عليه، وظاهر إطلاقهم عدم الوجوب عند الإشتغال بما ذكر، ولو كان غير محل لهما ويحرر قوله : (لتأخيره واجب القيام) الأولى زيادة، أو لتأخير واجب السلام قوله لكونه عفواً) لأن التحرز عن الركن مثله فيه حرج، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
(If his thought is prolonged) due to certainty of the missed action (and he did not say salam until he was certain of the missed action) (if) the time of thought exceeds the tashahhud by the measure of performing a rukn, then sujud al-sahw is obligatory upon him for delaying the wajib of standing for the third rak'ah (otherwise) i.e., if his thought is not of the measure of performing a rukn, then he does not perform sujud al-sahw because it is excused. (1) [Footnote: The text says '...' and the copyist corrects]. The commentator says: 'zā'idan 'an al-tashahhud' refers to the first or second tashahhud, whether after finishing the prayer and supplications or before. The phrase 'wajaba 'alayhi sujūd al-sahw' means if the thought distracted him from performing a wajib to the extent of a rukn, or distracted him from wudu after an event occurred due to doubt whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs, then sujud al-sahw is obligatory; otherwise no. In the sharh, they did not specify the measure of a rukn, but by analogy with what preceded, it is considered its norm, estimated at three tasbihat. The place of obligation is when he does not occupy himself during the state of doubt with recitation or tasbih; if he does occupy himself with them, then no sujud is upon him. Their apparent absolute statement indicates non-obligation when occupied with what was mentioned, even if it is not the proper place for them. The phrase 'for delaying the wajib of standing' could also be 'for delaying the wajib of salam'. The phrase 'because it is excused' means that guarding against a rukn is difficult.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific situation: a person is uncertain about a missed part of the prayer and remains in thought (tafakkur) without saying salam until he becomes certain. The key point is the duration of this thought. If the thought lasts longer than the time it takes to recite the tashahhud plus the time to perform one rukn (approximately three tasbihat), then he must perform sujud al-sahw because he has delayed a wajib (either standing for the third rak'ah or the final salam). If the thought was short (less than that), no sujud is required because such a delay is excusable. The commentator explains that the measure of a rukn is estimated at three tasbihat. Additionally, if during the doubt he engages in recitation or tasbih, then no sujud is needed, even if that engagement is not normally appropriate at that point, because the default is that there is no sujud unless the thought distracts from a wajib for a significant time.

Key Terms
التفكر (al-tafakkur): Reflection or contemplation during prayer about whether one has missed an action.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (at-tahiyyat) during sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, under which condition does performing sujud al-sahw become obligatory due to prolonged thought?

B) Only if the thought lasts longer than the time of tashahhud plus the measure of one rukn (about three tasbihat).
C) Only if the person had a certain doubt (shakk) about the number of rak'ahs.
D) Only if the person recites tasbih during the thought.

Key Takeaway
Prolonged thought during prayer only requires sujud al-sahw if it exceeds the tashahhud plus one rukn (≈3 tasbihat) and the person does not engage in recitation or tasbih.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Prolonged Reflection During Prayer
Ruling on when prolonged reflection necessitates sajw al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which sajw al-sahw becomes wajib due to prolonged reflection in prayer and apply it to a scenario.

Core Idea
Prolonged reflection in prayer necessitates sajw al-sahw only if it delays a rukn.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding sajw al-sahw caused by prolonged reflection. The key is the duration of the reflection relative to the performance of a rukn. This ruling clarifies a common situation where a worshipper delays the completion of prayer while trying to recall an omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage discusses prolonged reflection after tashahhud while the worshipper is certain of an omitted element. The ruling is that sajw al-sahw may become wajib or not based on duration.
2
Extract the condition for wajib
The condition is that the reflection time exceeds the tashahhud by the duration of performing one rukn (e.g., ruku' or sujud). If the reflection is shorter, no sajw is required.
The condition is explicitly stated: 'إن كان زمن التفكر زائداً عن التشهد قدر أداء ركن'
3
Understand the reason for sajw
Sajw al-sahw is required because the delay postpones a wajib element—either the standing for the third rak'ah (if the omission was a rak'ah) or the salam itself. The commentator notes the wording 'لتأخيره واجب القيام' is explanatory.
Delay of any wajib triggers sajw, provided the delay equals at least one rukn.
4
Determine the opposite case
If the reflection is shorter than one rukn, the passage states 'لا يسجد لكونه عفواً'—no sajw because the delay is excused (ma'fu).
The legal principle here is that minor delays are overlooked in prayer.

Source Text

(And if his reflection is prolonged) due to certainty of what was omitted (and he does not say salam until he becomes certain of what was omitted, (if) the time of reflection exceeds the tashahhud by the duration of performing a rukn, then sajw al-sahw is obligatory upon him for delaying the obligatory action of standing for the third (rak'ah). Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on prolonged reflection in prayer. If a person is certain that he omitted an obligatory element (like a rak'ah or sujūd) and remains reflecting without saying salām until he becomes certain, then if the time of reflection exceeded the tashahhud by the length of performing one rukn (e.g., rukūʿ), sajw al-sahw becomes obligatory due to delaying the obligatory standing for the third rakʿah. If the reflection was shorter than a rukn, no sajw is required as it is excused. The commentator clarifies that the phrase 'for delaying the obligatory action of standing' is additional; the wajib delayed could also be the obligatory salam.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajw al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or delay in prayer.
التفكر (al-tafakkur): Prolonged reflection on whether an element of prayer was omitted.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith in the sitting posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Reflection that causes missing a wajib

Key Takeaway
Prolonged reflection in prayer triggers sajw al-sahw only when it delays a rukn, not for shorter pauses.

Prophetic Forgetfulness: Hanafi Defense of Sahw
Defense of the possibility of forgetfulness in prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on prophetic forgetfulness (sahw) and evaluate the counter-argument that prophets are immune from all forgetfulness.

Core Idea
Prophets can forget in non-revelation matters; their sahw is not ghafla but absorption in Allah.

This passage defends the possibility of forgetfulness (sahw) in prophets, specifically addressing the incident where the Prophet forgot a rak'ah in prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between forgetfulness in conveying revelation (impossible) and forgetfulness in other acts (possible and occurred). The objection that sahw implies heedlessness (ghafla) is refuted by explaining prophetic sahw as a result of deep spiritual absorption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main issue
What is the disputed question? The possibility of forgetfulness (sahw) occurring in prophets.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi position is that prophets can forget in non-revelation matters. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet's sahw in prayer and the silent approval of the companions, forming ijmāʿ.
3
Present the opposing view
A group argues that prophets cannot forget because forgetfulness is heedlessness (ghafla), and prophets are maʿṣūm (protected) from that.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response makes a distinction: infallibility is only in conveying revelation (protected by miracle); in other matters, sahw is permissible. The Prophet's sahw was due to spiritual absorption, not negligence.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: whether the Prophet's actions in a state of sahw are considered normative (like deliberate actions) or require compensation. Hanafis hold they are normative but compensation (sajdah al-sahw) was prescribed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو الذي الصلاة ذلك، ولم ينكر عليه أحد فصار إجماعاً منهم ، ومعنى قوله له في الحديث: لم أنس، ولم تقصر أي لم يكن شيء من ذلك في ظني، بل ظن أني أكملت الصلاة أربعاً، قال : ناسياً ومن لم أفعل كذا، وكان قد فعل فهو غير كاذب، وفي السيد عن شرح المشارق في الحديث ما يدل على جواز السهو على الأنبياء، وقالت طائفة : لا يجوز لأنه غفلة وهم منزهون عنها، والجواب أن السهو ممتنع عليهم في الإخبار عن الله تعالى بالأحكام وغيرها لأنه قامت عليه المعجزة، وفيما ليس سبيله البلاغ يجوز وسهو نبينا كان لمقام شغله عن بالله، وفي هذا المعنى قيل: يا سائلي عن رسول الله كيف سها والسهو من كل قلب غافل لاهي قد غاب عن كل شيء سره فسها عما سوي الله فــالــتــعــظــيـــم
He is the one who prayed that prayer, and no one objected to him, so it became consensus among them. The meaning of his statement to him in the hadith: 'I did not forget nor shorten' means that none of that occurred in my notion, rather I thought I had completed the prayer as four. He said: 'Forgetfully he did not do such and such, and he had done it, so he is not lying.' In al-Sayyid, from Sharh al-Mashariq, there is indication in the hadith of the permissibility of forgetfulness for prophets. A group said: It is not permissible because it is heedlessness, and they are innocent of it. The answer: Forgetfulness is prevented from them in matters of reporting from Allah regarding rulings and other matters because a miracle supports them, but in what is not the path of conveying, it is permissible. And the forgetfulness of our Prophet was due to a station that occupied him from his mind. In this meaning it was said: 'O you who ask about the Messenger of Allah, how did he forget? And forgetfulness comes from every heedless, distracted heart. He was absent from everything except His secret, so he forgot other than Allah, so this is (a form of) exaltation.'
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a dispute regarding the possibility of forgetfulness (sahw) in prophets. The author cites the hadith where the Prophet forgot a rakʿah, and no companion objected, establishing consensus (ijmāʿ) that prophetic sahw is possible. The meaning of the Prophet's words 'I did not forget' is interpreted as 'I had no notion of forgetting in my mind,' not a literal denial. The author then presents the objection from a group (some scholars) that prophets cannot forget because forgetfulness is heedlessness (ghafla), which prophets are free from. The Hanafi response is that forgetfulness is impossible for prophets in matters of conveying revelation (because of miracles), but permissible in matters not related to conveying. The Prophet's forgetfulness was due to his deep absorption in divine consciousness, as expressed in the poetic line, which is actually an act of exaltation.

Key Terms
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness, especially in acts of worship like prayer.
الغفلة (al-ghafla): Heedlessness, inattention; considered incompatible with prophethood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why do prophets not forget in matters of conveying revelation?
A) Because they are always attentive
B) Because miracles support them in that
C) Because they never make mistakes
D) Because revelation is a burden

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness only in conveying revelation; in other matters, sahw is possible and occurred, without implying heedlessness.

Definition and Conditions of Doubt in Prayer
Defining doubt and its ruling, with three intra-Hanafi opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shakk (doubt) and its conditions for invalidating prayer, and distinguish the three intra-Hanafi opinions regarding the 'first doubt' requirement.

Core Idea
Doubt invalidates prayer only when first-time or non-habitual, not when frequent.

This chapter defines a specific type of doubt that can invalidate prayer. The Hanafi scholars disagree on the precise condition—whether it must be the first doubt ever, the first in this prayer, or simply non-habitual. Understanding these nuances clarifies when a worshipper must restart their prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of shakk
Shakk is defined linguistically as lack of certainty, and technicallly as equality of two possibilities. The chapter uses the linguistic meaning to include cases where certainty is absent.
This broader definition covers more scenarios than the strict technical definition.
2
Extract the conditions for invalidation
The passage states three conditions: (1) doubt about the number of rak'ahs (e.g., between two and three), (2) doubt occurs before completing the prayer, and (3) the doubt is either the first time ever (majority) or non-habitual (al-Sarakhsi).
Condition (3) is disputed among Hanafis.
3
Map the three Hanafi opinions
Majority (akthar al-mashāyikh): first doubt ever in one's prayer life after puberty. Fakhr al-Islam / Ibn al-Fadl: first doubt in this particular prayer. Imam al-Sarakhsi: doubt is not a habit (i.e., forgetfulness is not characteristic of the person).
These are all within the Hanafi school; each has practical implications.
4
Apply the practical consequence
Consider someone who doubts for the first time, restarts, and then years later forgets again. According to al-Sarakhsi, he must restart again because habit was not established. According to the majority, he does not restart because the first doubt already occurred.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: when a second doubt occurs after a long gap.

Chapter on doubt in prayer and purity. Prayer is invalidated by doubt, which is equality of the two matters (in the number of its rak'ahs) between three and two, if that doubt occurs before completion of it, and also it (i.e., the doubt) is the first doubt to occur to him, after his reaching puberty in a prayer. This is the saying of most mashāyikh. Fakhr al-Islam said: the first doubt to occur in this particular prayer, and Ibn al-Fadl chose it. Imam al-Sarakhsi held that its meaning is that forgetfulness is not his habit; it is not intended that he did not fall into it; so his ruling is the ruling of one who experiences doubt for the first time. Therefore he said: (or) if the doubt is not habitual for him, then it invalidates (the prayer) due to his statement: 'If one of you doubts in his prayer how many he has prayed, let him start the prayer anew.' And this has been interpreted as when it is the first doubt that occurs to him because what is meant here is not the customary meaning of equality of the two opposites, but rather the linguistic meaning, which is the absence of certainty (as in al-Qahustani) because the chapter is devoted to what is more general, and it does not contradict his later statement 'and it is equality of the two sides' because that is in the case of invalidation, and the intended meaning of doubt in both is its reality. His saying: (in the number of its rak'ahs) is to exclude doubt in other matters, such as one who prays one rak'ah of zuhr, then doubts in the second that it is 'asr, then doubts in the third that it is nafl, then doubts in the fourth that it is zuhr. They said: it is zuhr and no heed is paid to the doubt. In al-Fatawa: If one doubts the takbirat al-ihram, repeats the takbir and the thana', then remembers, then sajw al-sahw is upon him, and the second is not a new opening nor a termination of the first. The apparent restriction in his saying 'then remembers' indicates that if he does not remember that he had said takbir first, there is no sajw upon him. His saying: (after his reaching puberty) does not specify the ruling for the doubt of a minor; do the mentioned scenarios apply? Apparently yes, but it needs verification. His saying: (in this prayer) i.e., the specific prayer. So if one doubts in zuhr, for example, he starts anew. Then if he begins and doubts in it again, he does not repeat, and the subsequent ruling applies. His saying: (Imam al-Sarakhsi went...) The practical consequence appears in someone who doubts in a prayer for the first time and starts anew, then after years he becomes forgetful: according to al-Sarakhsi, he starts anew because doubt was not his habit and only occurred once before, and the habit is only established by repetition twice or more because it is derived from that. Similarly, according to Ibn al-Fadl, because it is the first forgetfulness for him in that prayer. According to most mashāyikh, he does not start anew. His saying: (his ruling) i.e., the ruling of one for whom doubt is not habitual. His saying: 'therefore he said' i.e., because the ruling is the same in what was mentioned. His saying: (or if doubt is not habitual for him) in it he combined two contradictory statements, so one does not know which he relied upon. His saying: (let him start the prayer anew) 'starting anew' can only be conceived by leaving the first prayer, and that is by saying salam, or speaking, or another action contradictory to prayer, and it is better to say salam while sitting because it is a legally permissible covenant (tahlīl). Mere intention is invalid because it does not remove him from prayer (as stated by al-Sayyid quoting al-Zayla'i). His saying: (and it has been interpreted) i.e., the 'starting anew' (as referring to the hadith). His saying: (due to the narration we will mention).
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a chapter on doubt (shakk) in prayer and purity. It defines the shakk that invalidates prayer: it must be a genuine doubt between two numbers (e.g., 3 or 4 rak'ahs) occurring before completion, and it must be the first time the person experiences such doubt or it is not habitual for him. The passage presents multiple opinions among Hanafi scholars. The majority (akthar al-mashāyikh) require that it be the first doubt ever in his prayer life while being adult. Fakhr al-Islam and Ibn al-Fadl specify it as the first doubt in that particular prayer. Imam al-Sarakhsi defines it as when forgetfulness is not his habit. The practical difference: if someone doubts for the first time and restarts, then years later forgets again, according to al-Sarakhsi he must restart because the habit was not established, while the majority say he does not restart. The passage also discusses what constitutes starting anew (istiqbāl): exiting the first prayer by salām or an act contrary to prayer. Mere intention is insufficient. The hadith 'if one doubts, let him start anew' is interpreted as referring to the first occurrence.

Key Terms
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt defined linguistically as lack of certainty, equal probability of two matters.
الاستقبال (al-istiqbāl): Starting the prayer anew by exiting the first prayer with salam or talk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The doubt must be about any aspect of the prayer, and it must be the first doubt in that particular prayer.
C) The doubt must be non-habitual, meaning the person is not generally forgetful.
D) The doubt must be about the intention of the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Doubt invalidates prayer only when it is the first ever occurrence or non-habitual; habitual doubt is disregarded.

The Ruling on Doubt (Shakk) in Prayer: Invalidation and Its Conditions
Explains the ruling on doubt in prayer, its conditions, and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on doubt in prayer, identify the conditions that trigger invalidation, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the meaning of 'first time'.

Core Idea
Doubt invalidates prayer only if first-time or non-habitual; frequent doubt is handled by taharri.

Doubt (shakk) during prayer—when you cannot recall the number of rak'ahs—can invalidate your prayer, but not always. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between first-time doubt, which renders the prayer void, and habitual doubt, which is relieved through seeking preponderant conjecture (taharri). This lesson unpacks the precise conditions, the textual evidence from the hadith, and the internal scholarly differences that shape the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Define shakk and identify its locus
Understand that shakk is equal likelihood of two possibilities, e.g., whether you prayed 3 or 4 rak'ahs. The text specifies it concerns the number of rak'ahs in prayer.
Shakk is not doubt about other aspects like qira'ah or sujud.
2
State the ruling and its conditions
The ruling is that such doubt invalidates the prayer if two conditions are met: (1) the doubt occurs before completing the prayer, and (2) it is the first time such doubt has ever occurred (or is not habitual). Identify the two conditions in the text.
The first condition 'before completion' is before salam or sitting for tashahhud.
3
Locate the dalil and analyze its wajh al-dalalah
The proof is the hadith: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer how many he has prayed, let him start the prayer anew.' The imperative 'falyastaqbil' indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul. However, it is interpreted restrictively due to other evidence.
The condition 'first time' is derived from the other narration about taharri.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Most mashayikh (including Abu Hanifa) hold that 'first time' means the first time ever in any prayer. Fakhr al-Islam said it means first time in this specific prayer. Al-Sarakhsi said it means forgetfulness is not his habit. Understand the difference in consequence.
The majority view (first time ever) is the mufta bihi.
5
Apply the ruling to specific scenarios
The text then covers: doubt after salam (no effect unless certainty of omission), reports from trustworthy individuals (one vs. two), imam vs. followers, and frequent doubt (taharri prescribed). Walk through each to see how conditions change the outcome.
For frequent doubt, the ruling shifts to taharri to avoid hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
فصل في الشك
في الصلاة والطهارة تبطل الصلاة بالشك وهو تساوي الأمرين (في عدد ركعاتها) ثلاث وثنتين (إذا كان ذلك الشك قبل إكمالها و كان أيضاً (هو) أي الشك أول ما عرض له في الشك) بعد بلوغه في صلاة ما، وهذا قول أكثر المشايخ، وقال فخر الإسلام أول ما عرض له في هذه الصلاة، واختاره ابن الفضل وذهب الإمام السرخسي إلى أن معناه أنّ السهو ليس عادة له، وليس المراد أنه لم يسقط فحكمه حكم من ابتدأه الشك فلذا قال : (أو) كان الشك غير عادة له فتبطل به لقوله : إذا شك أحدكم في صلاته أنه كم صلى فليستقبل الصلاة وقد حمل على ما إذا كان أول شك عرض له لما سنذكره من الرواية الأخرى ولقدرته على إسقاط ما عليه بيقين كما لو شك أنه صلى، أو لم يصل، والوقت باق يلزمه أن يصلي (فلو شك بعد سلامه أو قعوده قدر التشهد قبل السلام في عدد الركعات (لا يعتبر) شكه فلا شيء عليه حملاً لحاله على الصلاح (إلا إن) كان قد تيقن بالترك) فيأتي بما تركه ولو أخبره عدل بعد السلام أنه نقص ركعة، وعند المصلي أنه أتم لا يلتفت إلى أخباره وإن أخبره عدلان لا يعتبر شكه، وعليه الأخذ بقولهما، ولو اختلف الإمام والمؤتمون إن كان على يقين لا يأخذ بقولهم، وإلا أخذ به، وإن كان معه بعضهم أخذ بقوله ( وإن كثر الشك تحرى و (عمل) أي أخذ (بغالب ظنه) قوله : (فليستقبل الصلاة) الاستقبال لا يتصور إلا بالخروج عن الأولى، وذلك بالسلام، أو الكلام، أو عمل آخر ينافي الصلاة والسلام قاعداً أولى لأنه عهد محللاً شرعاً، ومجرد النية يلغو لأنه لم يخرج به من الصلاة سيد عن الزيلعي قوله : ( وقد حمل أي الاستقبال قوله: (لما سنذكره من الرواية الأخرى) وهي إذا شك أحدكم فليتحر الصواب فليتم عليه . قوله : (ولقدرته) عطف على لقوله. قوله : (كما لو شك الخ) وكما لو تيقن ترك الصلاة من يوم وليلة وشك في تعيينها قضى صلاة يوم وليلة ليخرج عن العهدة بيقين كذا في الفتح. قوله: (فلو شك بعد سلامه الخ) محترز قوله إذا كان قبل إكمالها أي قبل إتمام أركانها كما يدل عليه ما هنا قوله : على الصلاح) وهو إتمام الصلاة. قوله: (لا يلتفت إلى إخباره) لأن يقينه لا يزول بيقين غيره خصوصاً ولم يكن قول هذا الغير ملزماً بخلاف ما إذا كان نصاب الشهادة فعليه أن يعمل بما أخيرا لأن قولهما ملزم في كثير من الإحكام . قوله : (وإن كان معه بعضهم أخذ بقوله هذا مفروض فيما لو اختلف القوم، والإمام مع أحد الفريقين، فإن يعتبر جانب الإمام، ولو كان الذي معه واحداً، وفي الشرح لو اختلف الإمام والمؤتمون فقالوا ثلاثاً، وقال أربعاً إن كان على يقين لا يأخذ بقولهم، وإلا أخذ، وإن اختلف القوم والإمام مع فريق أخذ بقوله : ولو كان معه واحد ولو استيقن واحد بالتمام وآخر بالنقص، وشك الإمام والقوم لا إعادة على أحد إلا على متيقن النقض لأن يقينه لا يبطل بيقين غيره، ولو كان الإمام استيقن أنه صلى ثلاثاً كان عليه أن يعيد بالقوم، ولا إعادة على متيقن التمام لها قلنا : أما لو استيقن واحد بالنقصان، ولم يستيقن أحد بالتمام، بل هم واقفون، فإن كان ذلك في الوقت أعادوها احتياطاً لعدم المعارضة بخلاف ما قبلها، وإن لم يعيدوا لا شيء عليهم إلا إذا استيقن عدلان بالنقص، وأخبرا بذلك اهـ من الفتح والزاد وقاضيخان . قوله: (وإن كثر الشك تحرى وذلك بأن وقع له مرتين قبل هذه عند السرخسي، ومرة واحدة قبل هذا عند الأكثر، أو في تلك الصلاة عند البزدوي والفضل قال في الشرح والتحري طلب الأحرى، وهو ما يكون أكبر رأيه عليه، وعبروا عنه تارة بالظن، وتارة بغالب الظن اهـ . قوله : (أي أخذ بغالب ظنه أي الذي حصل له بعد وقوع الشك له فلا یرد أن الموضوع في الشك لا فيمن غلب ظنه، وإنما أخذ بغالب الظن للزوم الحرج بالإعادة كل مرة لا سيما إن كان موسوساً، فلا تجب عليه دفعاً للحرج، فتعين التحري عليه، فلو لم يأخذ بأكبر رأيه بأن غلب على ظنه أنها الرابعة فأتمها وقعد وضم إليها أخرى، وقعد احتياطاً فهو مسيء.
The book of prayer. Section on doubt. In prayer and purification, prayer is invalidated by doubt, which is the equal likelihood of two matters (in the number of its rak'ahs) three and two, when that doubt occurs before completing the prayer and also it (i.e. doubt) is the first time it occurs to him (in doubt) after reaching puberty in a prayer. This is the saying of most mashayikh. Fakhr al-Islam said: the first time it occurs to him in this very prayer, and Ibn al-Fadl chose that. Imam al-Sarakhsi held that its meaning is that forgetfulness (sahu) is not his habit, and the intent is not that he has not omitted anything; so his ruling is the ruling of one whom doubt has initially befallen. Therefore he said: (or) doubt is not habitual for him, so it invalidates due to his statement: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer how many he has prayed, let him start the prayer anew.' And this has been interpreted as when it is the first doubt that occurred to him because of the other narration we will mention, and because he is able to remove what is upon him with certainty, just as if he doubts whether he prayed or not while time remains, he must pray. (If he doubts after his salam or his sitting the amount of tashahhud before the salam in the number of rak'ahs, his doubt is not considered, so nothing is upon him, based on assuming his state to be correct, unless he is certain of having omitted something, then he performs what he omitted. Even if a trustworthy person informs him after salam that he missed a rak'ah while the worshipper believes he completed, he does not heed his report. If two trustworthy persons inform him, his doubt is not considered, and he must act on their statement. If the imam and followers differ: if he is certain, he does not take their statement; otherwise he takes it. If some followers are with him, he takes his statement. And if doubt becomes frequent, he performs taharri and acts on his preponderant conjecture.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the ruling of doubt (shakk) in prayer. The text defines shakk as the equal likelihood of two possibilities (e.g., whether one prayed three or four rak'ahs). The primary ruling is that such doubt invalidates the prayer if it occurs before completing the prayer and if it is the first time such doubt has occurred to the person (according to most scholars), or if it is not habitual for him (according to Imam al-Sarakhsi). The proof is the hadith: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer how many he has prayed, let him start the prayer anew.' The Hanafi commentators interpret this hadith as applying specifically to the case of first-time doubt. The passage then discusses various scenarios: doubt after completing the prayer (no consideration unless certainty of omission), reports from trustworthy individuals (one is not heeded if the worshipper is certain; two are heeded), disagreement between imam and followers (the imam's certainty prevails; if not, he follows the majority), and frequent doubt (taharri is prescribed to avoid hardship). The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is based on the principle of removing hardship, especially for waswasi (those prone to whispers).

Key Terms
الشك (al-shakk): Linguistically: uncertainty; technically here: equal likelihood of two possibilities (e.g., three or four rak'ahs).
التحري (al-taharri): Seeking the more likely correct action based on preponderant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann).
أول ما عرض له (awwal ma 'arada lahu): The first time doubt ever occurs to the person in his life (according to most mashayikh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, when does doubt in the number of rak'ahs invalidate the prayer?
A) When the doubt occurs after the salam
B) When the doubt is the first time it has ever occurred to the worshipper
C) When the worshipper is certain of having omitted a rak'ah
D) When two trustworthy persons inform the worshipper of the doubt

Key Takeaway
Doubt in prayer invalidates only if it is first-time (or non-habitual) and occurs before completion; habitual doubt is relieved by taharri.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Doubt in the Number of Rak'ahs in Prayer
Explains rulings on doubt in rak'ah count: when ignored, when taharri, when building on minimum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for doubt (shakk) in the number of rak'ahs: identify when doubt is ignored, when taharri is required, and when building on the minimum is mandatory.

Core Idea
Doubt after completion is ignored; habitual doubt requires taharri; if uncertain, build on the minimum.

This lesson covers the detailed Hanafi jurisprudence on doubt concerning the number of rak'ahs during prayer. Understanding these rules is essential for every muṣallī and for those who give fatwa on prayer-related issues. The key principle is that doubt is ignored after the prayer is completed (after salām or final sitting), but if doubt is habitual, the worshipper must perform taharri (seeking the preponderant opinion). If preponderance cannot be reached, he must build on the minimum (al-aqall).

Guided Path
1
Distinguish doubt before vs. after completion
Identify whether the doubt occurs before or after the final sitting (qadr al-tashahhud) or salām. Doubt after completion is legally ignored; doubt before requires action.
The text begins with ruling on doubt after salām or sitting to the extent of tashahhud.
2
Handle reports from others
If a single just person reports a deficiency, but the worshipper is certain of completion, the report is not accepted. Two just persons make their report binding.
Also covers imam–congregation disagreement: imam's certainty prevails; if not certain, he follows the congregation.
3
Apply taharri for frequent doubt
If doubt occurs habitually (e.g., at least twice before), perform taharri (seek preponderant opinion). Act according to ghalib al-zann.
Main proof: hadith 'When one of you doubts, let him seek the correct opinion and complete upon it.'
4
Build on the minimum when no preponderance
If after taharri no opinion preponderates, base the prayer on the smallest possible number and perform additional rak'ahs and sittings to cover all possibilities.
Example: doubting 2nd or 3rd in a 4-rak'ah prayer → assume 2nd, sit, then complete as if each extra rak'ah could be the last.
5
Reconcile the three hadith
The three narrations on doubt are reconciled: first (ignore doubt) = occasional doubt; second (taharri) = frequent doubt with opinion; third (build on least) = habitual doubt without opinion.
This method of jam' (reconciliation) is preferred to tarjīḥ when possible.

We will mention it from the other narration. And because of his ability to remove what is upon him with certainty, just as if he doubts whether he prayed or not, and the time remains, he must pray. (If he doubts after his salam or his sitting to the extent of the tashahhud before the salam regarding the number of rak'ahs, (it is not considered) his doubt, so nothing is upon him, as his state is assumed to be sound. (Except if) he was certain of omission, then he performs what he omitted. Even if one just person informs him after the salam that he missed a rak'ah, while the prayer thinks he completed, he does not heed his report. But if two just persons inform him, his doubt is not considered, and he must act on their statement. And if the imam and followers disagree: if he is certain, he does not act on their statement; otherwise he acts. And if some of them are with him, he acts on his own statement. (And if doubt becomes frequent, he performs taharri, and (acts) i.e., takes (by his preponderant opinion). The other narration is: When one of you doubts, let him seek the correct (opinion) and complete upon it. His statement: (because of his ability) is coordinate with his statement. His statement: (just as if he doubts etc.) And just as if he is certain he missed a prayer from a day and night and doubts its specific time, he prays a day and night's worth to exit the responsibility with certainty, as in al-Fath. His statement: (If he doubts after his salam etc.) is the exception to his statement 'if before its completion' i.e., before completing its pillars, as indicated here. His statement: (on soundness) i.e., completion of prayer. His statement: (he does not heed his report) because his certainty is not removed by another's certainty, especially since this other's statement is not binding, unlike when it meets the number for testimony, then he must act on what they reported because their statement is binding in many rulings. His statement: (And if some of them are with him, he acts on his statement) This is posited for when the people differ and the imam is with one of the two groups; then the side of the imam is considered, even if only one is with him. In al-Sharh: If the imam and followers differ, they say three, and he says four: if he is certain, he does not act on their statement; otherwise he acts. And if the people differ and the imam is with a group, he acts on his statement even if only one is with him. If one is certain of completion and another of deficiency, while the imam and followers doubt, no repetition is required except for the one certain of deficiency, because his certainty is not invalidated by another's certainty. And if the imam is certain that he prayed three, he must repeat with the people, and no repetition for those certain of completion. We say: If one is certain of deficiency and no one is certain of completion, but they are uncertain, then if it is within the time, they repeat it as a precaution due to no opposing certainty, unlike before it. If they do not repeat, nothing is upon them unless two just persons are certain of deficiency and report that. End from al-Fath, al-Zad, and Qadikhan. His statement: (And if doubt becomes frequent, he performs taharri) That is, if it occurs to him twice before this, according to al-Sarakhsi; once before this, according to most; or in that prayer itself, according to al-Bazdawi and al-Fadl. He said in al-Sharh: Taharri is seeking the better (al-ahra), which is the greatest of his opinion. They sometimes express it as zann, sometimes as ghalib al-zann. His statement: (i.e., takes by his preponderant opinion) i.e., which occurs to him after the doubt. So it cannot be objected that the subject is doubt, not one whose opinion is preponderant. He only takes by preponderant opinion because of the difficulty of repeating every time, especially if he is obsessive; it is not obligatory to avoid difficulty, so taharri is determined for him. So if he does not act by his greatest opinion, as when his preponderant opinion is that it is the fourth, so he completes, sits, adds another, and sits out of caution, he is sinning. Due to the Prophet's saying: 'When one of you doubts let him seek the correct opinion and complete upon it.' And it is interpreted as when doubt is frequent, due to the previous narration. (If no preponderant opinion occurs to him, he takes the minimum.) Due to his saying: 'When one of you forgets in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed one or two, let him build on one. If he does not know whether he prayed two or three, let him build on two. If he does not know whether he prayed three or four, let him build on three and perform two prostrations before salam,' meaning for forgetfulness. So when all three narrations that we narrated in the three issues were established with them, they adopted the method of reconciliation by interpreting each one in a way that supports it, as in Fath al-Qadir. (He sits) and performs tashahhud (after every rak'ah he thinks is the last of his prayer) so that he does not become a forsaker of the obligatory sitting, with a means leading him to certainty of not leaving it. And likewise for every sitting he thinks is obligatory, he performs it. Ease. His statement: (let him seek the correct opinion) i.e., according to him. And his statement: 'complete upon it' is interpreted as when his taharri leads to the minimum. And it is possible that the meaning is that he completes it even with what remains of it, like tashahhud and salam. His statement: (If no preponderant opinion occurs to him) i.e., nothing becomes preponderant after seeking, as in al-Kafi, or he has no opinion, as in al-Hidaya. His statement: (he takes the minimum) So if he doubts in a four-rak'ah prayer whether it is the first or second, and he builds on the minimum, he makes it the first. Then he sits because it could be the second, where sitting would be obligatory. Then he stands and prays another rak'ah and sits because we have made it, in ruling, the second. Then he stands and prays another rak'ah and sits because it could be the fourth. Then he stands and prays another and sits because we have made it, in ruling, the fourth, and sitting on the third and fourth is obligatory. Likewise, if he doubts whether it is the second or third and no preponderance occurs, he sits immediately because it could be the second. Then he stands and prays another rak'ah and sits because it could be the fourth. Then he stands and prays another rak'ah and sits because we have made it, in ruling, the fourth. And similarly for two- and three-rak'ah prayers, as in al-Dhakhira, and its completion in the lengthy works. His statement: (And he performs two prostrations before salam) with firmness. It has preceded that prostration for forgetfulness before and after salam is established by his statement and action. His statement: (So when it was established) is a clause preceding its result, or condition and answer, so 'lammā' is emphasized. His statement: (they adopted the method of reconciliation) because reconciling evidences whenever possible is not abandoned. So they interpreted each one differently, reconciling them by considering the appropriateness of each in its particular interpretation. So they interpreted the first as when doubt is not habitual due to lack of difficulty; the second as when doubt is frequent and he has an opinion, due to the difficulty of repeating every time, and it contains the command to perform taharri; the third as when doubt is his habit and his taharri does not lead to anything, so it contains the command to discard doubt and build on the minimum. His statement: (by interpreting each one) depicts the method of reconciliation. His statement: (he thinks is the last of his prayer) includes that the subject is one with no preponderant opinion. So if he said, as the author of al-Tanwir said: 'and he sits in every place he imagines is a place of sitting' it would be better. And in al-Sayyid: if he said 'he thinks it is a place of sitting so that he does not become a forsaker of the obligatory or wajib sitting', he would dispense with his statement 'after... and likewise every sitting he thinks is wajib'. The author, like the author of al-Kanz and al-Hidaya, neglected speech on sajda al-sahw, which is not proper. All of them.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) from al-Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, dealing with the rulings of doubt (shakk) in the number of rak'ahs during prayer. The author explains multiple scenarios based on the Hanafi madhhab.

First, if doubt occurs after completing the prayer (i.e., after salam or after the sitting of the final tashahhud before salam), the doubt is not considered. The prayer is deemed valid, and no action is required, because we assume the worshipper's state was sound (hamlan ‘ala al-salah). The exception is if the person is certain that they omitted something; then they must perform the omitted part.

If a single just person ('adl) informs the imam after salam that he missed a rak'ah, but the imam believes he completed, the imam does not accept the report. However, if two just persons (nassab al-shahada) inform him, the imam must act on their report because their testimony is binding in many legal rulings.

When the imam and the congregation disagree about the number of rak'ahs, the imam's certainty prevails; if he is not certain, he accepts the congregation's statement. If the congregation is divided and the imam is with one group, he follows his own view.

If doubt becomes frequent (kathura al-shakk) — defined by some as occurring twice, by others as once — the worshipper must perform taharri, i.e., seek the preponderant opinion (ghalib al-zann). This is because repeating the prayer every time would cause hardship (haraj), especially for an obsessive doubter (muswas). The proof is the hadith: "When one of you doubts, let him seek the correct opinion and complete upon it." This hadith is interpreted to apply to frequent doubt, reconciling it with other hadith.

If no preponderant opinion occurs to the person even after seeking, then he must build on the minimum (al-aqall). For example, in a four-rak'ah prayer, if he doubts whether it is the first or second, he treats it as the first and then sits after each subsequent rak'ah to cover all possibilities. This is based on the hadith: "If one of you forgets and does not know if he prayed one or two, let him build on one..." and so on.

The commentator then discusses the reconciliation of the three hadith on this topic: one hadith commands ignoring doubt and building on the least; the second commands taharri; the third commands building on the minimum. The scholars reconciled them by applying each to a different scenario: the first (ignore) when doubt is not habitual; the second (taharri) when doubt is frequent and a preponderant opinion exists; the third (build on minimum) when doubt is habitual and no preponderance occurs.

Finally, the commentator criticizes the author of Maraqi al-Falah for neglecting to discuss sajda al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) in this context, which he considers a deficiency.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Uncertainty between two possibilities (e.g., number of rak'ahs) without preponderance.
تحري (taharri): To seek the preponderant opinion (ghalib al-zann) when in doubt, by reflecting on what is most likely.
غالب الظن (ghalib al-zann): Preponderant belief that one outcome is more likely, formed after reflection (taharri).
الأقل (al-aqall): The minimum number (e.g., of rak'ahs) when no preponderant opinion exists, to ensure the prayer is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person in a four-rak'ah prayer doubts whether he is in the second or third rak'ah and has no preponderant opinion. According to the Hanafi school, what should he do?
A) Assume it is the third and continue without sitting.
B) Assume it is the second, sit for tashahhud, then complete by adding two more rak'ahs with sittings.
C) Repeat the prayer from the beginning.
D) Ask another person to confirm.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a structured response to doubt in rak'ahs: doubt after completion is ignored; frequent doubt requires taharri; if no preponderance, build on the minimum, all based on sound hadith reconciliation.

Resolving Doubt in Prayer: Tahari and Building on the Least
Proof and reconciliation of hadiths on shakk in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for resolving doubt in the number of rak'ahs in prayer, apply the method of tahari and building on the least, and identify the correct placement of sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
When doubt occurs, seek the correct opinion; if none prevails, build on the least and perform sujud al-sahw before salam.

Doubt about the number of rak'ahs is a common occurrence in prayer, and the Hanafi school provides clear guidance based on prophetic hadith. This lesson examines the two main hadiths on the subject and how the Hanafi jurists reconciled three different narrations to derive a comprehensive ruling. You will learn the conditions for using tahari (seeking the correct opinion) versus building on the least (al-bina' 'ala al-aqall), and the obligation of sujud al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two hadiths and their apparent conflict
Read the two hadiths cited in the passage: one commands tahari, the other commands building on the least. Note that they seem to give different instructions for the same situation.
The conflict is resolved by reconciling the narrations, not by preferring one over the other.
2
Understand the reconciliation method
The Hanafi scholars applied each hadith to a specific scenario: first narration when doubt is not habitual, second when doubt is frequent and the person has an opinion, third when doubt is habitual and no opinion forms.
Reconciliation (al-jam') is preferred over tarjih when possible.
3
Apply the rule: tahari vs. building on the least
If you have a preponderant opinion (ghalabat al-zann), follow it and complete the prayer accordingly. If no opinion prevails, build on the smallest number and perform sujud al-sahw before salam.
Sujud al-sahw in this case is wajib.
4
Practice the detailed steps for a four-rak'ah prayer
Work through the example in the commentary: doubting between first/second or second/third. Note the pattern of sitting after each rak'ah that could be the last, then continuing, and finally performing sujud al-sahw.
This ensures no obligatory sitting is missed.

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi deals with the ruling on doubt (shakk) in prayer regarding the number of rak'ahs. It begins by citing two hadiths: the first commands seeking the correct opinion (tahari) and completing the prayer based on that; the second, when no opinion prevails, commands building on the least number (akhdh bil-aqall) and performing two prostrations before the salam (sujud al-sahw). The commentary explains that the scholars reconciled the three different narrations (one for tahari, one for building on the least, and one for dismissing doubt) by applying each to a specific scenario: first narration when doubt is not habitual, second when it is frequent and the person has an opinion, third when doubt is habitual and no opinion forms. The practical application is then detailed: if one doubts in a four-rak'ah prayer between the first and second, and builds on the least (first), he must sit after every rak'ah that could be the last, performing tashahhud, and then continue, eventually performing sujud al-sahw. The commentator emphasizes that sujud al-sahw is wajib and criticizes earlier authors for neglecting this topic.

Key Terms
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt about the number of rak'ahs performed in prayer.
التحري (al-tahari): The act of exerting effort to determine the correct number of rak'ahs based on preponderant opinion.
البناء على الأقل (al-bina' 'ala al-aqall): Building the prayer on the smaller number of rak'ahs when no opinion prevails, and then performing sujud al-sahw.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed before (or after) the salam to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling explained in this passage, if a person doubts whether they prayed two or three rak'ahs and has no preponderant opinion, what should they do?
A) Build on two and perform sujud al-sahw before salam.
B) Build on three and not perform sujud al-sahw.
C) Repeat the entire prayer.
D) Build on the higher number (three) and perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on doubt in prayer is to seek the correct opinion when possible; otherwise, build on the least and perform sujud al-sahw before salam.

Prostration of Recitation: Definition, Conditions, and Ruling
Definition, conditions, and ruling of prostration of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sujūd al-tilāwah, list its conditions and pillar, explain why it is wājib (not farḍ), and compare the intra-Hanafī views on its timing.

Core Idea
Sujūd al-tilāwah is wājib, not farḍ, because its proof is speculative (ẓannī).

This lesson unpacks the first part of the chapter on Sujūd al-Tilāwah from Marāqī al-Falāḥ. It defines the prostration, lists its conditions (shurūṭ) and pillar (rukn), explains its cause (recitation), and clarifies why the Hanafī school rules it as wājib rather than farḍ. Additionally, we explore an intra-madhhab disagreement about whether non-prayer prostration must be performed immediately or can be delayed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Determine what sujūd al-tilāwah is: a prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific Quranic verse. Note that the title adds the ruling to its cause (idāfah).
The cause is tilāwah; for the listener, hearing is a condition.
2
Determine the ruling and its epistemological weight
The text states it is wājib. Understand why: the Quranic verses command prostration, but the indication is ẓannī, so it does not reach the level of farḍ.
Wājib means omission incurs sin but is not as severe as farḍ.
3
List the conditions and pillar
Extract the shurūṭ: purity (from ḥadath and khabath), facing qibla, covering ‘awrah; no tayammum without excuse. The rukn is placing the forehead on the ground.
Conditions resemble those of prayer except takbīr and intention, which are not required.
4
Analyze the timing dispute
Note the ikhtilāf: Imām Muḥammad and one narration from Abū Ḥanīfa allow delay (ʿalā al-tarākhī); Abū Yūsuf and another narration require immediacy for non-prayer prostration.
The chosen view (al-mukhtār) is the delay view.
5
Apply the muftā bihī position
For fatwa, the operative ruling is that non-prayer prostration may be delayed, but delaying without excuse is makrūh tanzīhan (lightly disliked).
The practical consequence: if delayed without reason, it is not sinful but disliked.

وما في بالشرح أولي حيث قال: لأن آيات السجود على ثلاثة أقسام، قسم فيه الأمر الصريح، وقسم تضمن استنكاف الكفرة حيث أمروا به، وقسم فيه حكاية امتثال الأنبياء به، وكل من الامتثال ،والاقتداء، ومخالفة الكفرة واجب إلا أن يدل دليل على عدم لزومه، لكن دلالتها فيه ظنية، فكان الثابت الوجوب لا الفرض اهـ قوله : (على التراخي عند محمد ورواية عن الإمام وهو المختار، وعند أبي يوسف وهو رواية عن
Chapter of the Prostration of Recitation: The addition of the ruling to its cause is the principle in derivation because [the addition] is for specification. And the strongest of its aspects is the specification of the effect by the cause because it occurs by it. Its conditions: purity from minor and major impurity, and from filth; and tayammum is not permissible for it without excuse; facing the qibla; covering the private parts. Its pillar: placing the forehead on the ground. Its description: obligation immediately in prayer, and with delay if it is non-prayer. Its ruling: the falling of the obligation in the world and attainment of reward in the hereafter. Then he began to explain the cause, so he said: 'Its cause is recitation for the reciter by agreement, and for the listener in the correct view, and hearing is a condition for the action of recitation concerning him; so the deaf person who recites and does not hear, the prostration is obligatory upon him. And it, i.e., the prostration of recitation, is obligatory because it is either an explicit command concerning it, or it implies the disdain of the disbelievers from it, or obedience of the prophets, and each of them is obligatory. It is with delay according to Muhammad and a narration from the Imam, and that is the chosen view, and according to Abu Yusuf and a narration from the Imam.'... His saying: 'it is the original' – the pronoun is mentioned with reference to the predicate. His saying: 'and the strongest of its aspects' i.e., aspects of specification, and its aspects are ownership, entitlement, for example. His saying: 'because it occurs' – this cause appears in the cause-effect but it is stronger because of its effect unlike the cause; so if he had said 'and from the strongest of its aspects' etc., it would be better. His saying: 'and its conditions etc.' – if he had said as al-Sayyid said: 'and its conditions are the conditions of prayer except the takbirat al-ihram and intention and specification', it would be more concise and comprehensive. His saying: 'and filth' i.e., the preventing impurity. His saying: 'and facing the qibla' i.e., in the state of choice, and towards capability in case of inability. His saying: 'its pillar is placing the forehead on the ground' – if he had said as al-Sayyid and others: 'its pillars are placing the forehead on the ground, or bowing, or what stands in their place from gestures for the sick person, or the reciter on a riding animal', it would be better. And its apparent meaning: if he delays it to a second rak'ah, he commits a sin. He said in the Sharh: 'If he delays it until the recitation becomes long, it becomes a make-up and he sins.' Then he said: 'Likewise, delaying the prayer-related [prostration] from the time of recitation is prohibitively disliked.' His saying: 'with delay if it is non-prayer but delaying it is lightly disliked as will come soon.' His saying: 'in the correct view' – and it is said that hearing is the cause concerning the listener. His saying: 'the prostration is obligatory upon him' – it is appropriate to add: and it is not obligatory upon him by the recitation of another, even if he sees someone prostrating. His saying: 'because it is the prostration of recitation' – this is with an omission of a genitive construction: i.e., the evidence of the prostration of recitation. His saying: 'the disdain of the disbelievers from it' i.e., from prostration. His saying: 'or obedience' is coordinated with 'disdain'. His saying: 'and each of them' i.e., of the command, i.e., of obeying it, and the disbelievers i.e., opposing them, and of the obedience of the prophets i.e., following them, is obligatory. And it is not hidden that the expression is awkward, and what is in the Sharh is better, where he said: 'Indeed the verses of prostration are of three types: a type containing an explicit command, a type implying the disdain of the disbelievers where they were commanded [to prostrate], and a type containing a narrative of the obedience of the prophets with it, and each of obedience, following, and opposing the disbelievers is obligatory unless evidence indicates its non-necessity. But their indication is speculative, so what is established is [the level of] wujūb, not farḍ.' His saying: 'with delay according to Muhammad and a narration from the Imam, and that is the chosen view, and according to Abu Yusuf and a narration from the Imam.'
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Sujūd al-Tilāwah (Prostration of Recitation). The author first explains the title: it is an idāfa (construct phrase) where the ruling (sujūd) is added to its cause (tilāwah), which is the strongest form of specification. The conditions (shurūṭ) are: purity from ḥadath and khabath, facing qibla, covering the ‘awrah, and no tayammum without excuse. The pillar (rukn) is placing the forehead on the ground; the commentator notes that including bowing or gestures for the sick would be more comprehensive. The description: it is wajib immediately if performed within prayer, and can be delayed if outside prayer. Its ruling: dropping the obligation in this world and gaining reward in the hereafter. The cause is recitation (tilāwah) for the reciter by consensus, and for the listener according to the correct view (ṣaḥīḥ). Hearing is a condition for the listener, so a deaf person who recites must still prostrate. The prostration is wujūb (obligatory) because the verses of prostration either contain an explicit command, imply disdain of disbelievers (who refused to prostrate), or relate the prophets’ obedience. The commentator clarifies that these indications are ẓannī (speculative), so the level is wujūb, not farḍ. There is a dispute about the timing: Imām Muḥammad and one narration from Abū Ḥanīfa hold that it is permissible to delay (ʿalā al-tarākhī) when outside prayer, which is the chosen view (al-mukhtār); Abū Yūsuf and another narration hold it is immediate. The commentary discusses better phrasing, additional pillars, and the ruling of delay (makrūh tanzīhan if delayed without reason, and makrūh taḥrīman if the prayer-related prostration is delayed).

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (āyah al-sajdah) in the Quran.
التلاوة (al-tilāwah): The act of reciting the Quran, specifically the verses containing prostration commands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī school, what is the ruling regarding a person who recites an āyah of prostration but delays the sujūd until after the prayer?
A) The prostration is invalid and cannot be made up.
B) He must perform the prostration immediately; delay is not allowed.
C) He may delay if it is outside prayer, but it is disliked (makrūh) if done without excuse.
D) The prostration is not obligatory for the reciter; only for the listener.

Key Takeaway
Sujūd al-tilāwah is a wājib act with conditions similar to prayer, and its timing may be delayed outside prayer according to the preferred Hanafī view.

Sujud al-Tilawah: Ruling, Conditions, and Timing Dispute
Explains cause, conditions, pillar, ruling, and timing of sujud al-tilawah with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (wajib), identify the conditions and pillar, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of sujud al-tilawah.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib, not fard, and outside prayer it is with delay (taraakhi), though postponement is disliked.

Sujud al-tilawah is a prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific Quranic verses. This lesson clarifies its cause, conditions, pillar, and the Hanafi position that it is wajib. We also examine the key intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Muhammad (delay) and Imam Abu Yusuf (immediate), and why the delay position is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? State its hukm level (wajib) and why it is not fard.
2
List the conditions and pillar
What are the necessary conditions (shurut) and the single pillar (rukn)? Why do they resemble prayer conditions?
3
Locate the dalil
What proof does the text cite for wujub? How do the Quranic verses indicate obligation (explicit command or implication)?
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Who holds the immediate view, and who holds the delayed view? What is the chosen view (al-mukhtar)?
5
Apply the practical consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf: when is delay sinful vs merely disliked?

Source Text

Its aspects: the attribution of the effect to the cause because it occurs by it. Its conditions are purification from hadath and khabath, and tayammum is not permissible without excuse, facing the qiblah, covering the 'awrah. Its pillar is placing the forehead on the ground. Its description: it is obligatory immediately in prayer, and with delay if it is non-prayer. Its ruling: the falling away of obligation in this world and attaining reward in the hereafter. Then he began to explain the cause: 'Its cause is recitation for the reciter by agreement, and for the listener in the correct view, and hearing is a condition for the application of recitation in his case; so the deaf person, if he recites and does not hear, the sajdah is obligatory upon him.' (It) i.e. sujud al-tilawah (is wajib) because either there is an explicit command for it, or it implies the arrogance of the disbelievers from it, or the compliance of the prophets, and each of these is wajib. (It is with delay) according to Muhammad and a narration from Imam, and it is the chosen view; and according to Abu Yusuf and a narration from Imam, it is obligatory immediately if it had not become obligatory by his recitation (in prayer) because it became a part of the prayer, not performed outside, so it is obligatory immediately in it, and other than it is obligatory with time extent. But its delay is disliked after the time of recitation in the most correct view, if it is not a disliked time, because with long time he may forget it, so its delay is disliked (tanzihan). Sujud is obligatory upon one who recites a verse, being obligated for prayer, and is not a follower, in other than ruku', sujud, and tashahhud, due to prevention from recitation therein. Even if he recites it in Persian, by agreement, whether he understood or not, because it is Qur'an from one aspect. Reading the letter of prostration with a word before or after from its verse obligates it.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement of the earlier Sharh on sujud al-tilawah. The text first outlines the main rulings: the cause (sabab) of sujud al-tilawah is the act of recitation (tilawah) for the reciter, and for the listener it is hearing according to the correct view. The conditions (shurut) are the same as for prayer: purification from hadath and khabath, facing qiblah, and covering the 'awrah. The rukn (pillar) is placing the forehead on the ground. The hukm (ruling) is that it is wajib (obligatory), not fard, because the evidence is based on probable interpretation (zanni). The timing: in prayer it must be immediate (fawr) because it becomes part of the prayer and cannot be performed outside; outside prayer it is with delay (taraakhi). The author then explains the proof: the verses of sajdah either contain explicit commands, or imply the arrogance of the disbelievers (who refused to prostrate), or describe the prophets' compliance, and all these necessitate wujub. The author also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad and a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa hold it is with delay (the chosen position), while Imam Abu Yusuf and another narration from Abu Hanifa hold it is immediate. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is delay. Finally, the text covers additional details: the dislike of delaying without heavy dislike (tanzihan), conditions for the reciter (must be praying, not a follower, not in ruku' etc.), recitation in Persian, and the requirement to read the full verse or at least the prostration letter with a word before or after. The discussion continues with further commentary on these points.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed when reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a prostration marker.
على الفور (ala al-fawr): Immediately, without delay.
على التراخي (ala al-tarakhi): With delay, i.e., can be performed later within a permissible timeframe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon reciting or hearing the verse
B) With delay (taraakhi), though delay without excuse is disliked
C) Only during prayer, never outside
D) It is not obligatory outside prayer

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib, and outside prayer it is performed with delay (taraakhi), though postponement without excuse is disliked.

Obligation of Immediate Sajdah and Dislike of Delay
Critical refinement on the immediacy of sajdah al-tilawah in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of sajdah al-tilawah in prayer, distinguish between fawri and muwassa' obligation, and explain why delay is makruh tanzihan per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Delaying sajdah al-tilawah in prayer is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it must be performed immediately—delay risks forgetfulness and violates the wajib.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah when recited during prayer. While outside prayer the sajdah can be delayed (muwassa'), within prayer it becomes subject to immediate obligation (fawran) because it integrates into the prayer's structure. Al-Tahtawi refines this by addressing an intra-madhhab dispute about whether the delay is only tanzihi or even tahrimi, and clarifies the most correct view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sajdah al-tilawah in prayer is wajib immediately. Understand that it becomes an integral part of the prayer, so it cannot be postponed outside the prayer.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni (non-mutawatir hadith).
2
Locate the dalil (reason)
The reason given is 'because it has become a part of prayer, not performed outside it.' This is a talil (causal explanation) that establishes immediacy.
Outside prayer, the sajdah is muwassa' (broad in time) because there is no such integration.
3
Distinguish between fawri and muwassa'
In prayer: fawri (immediate). Outside prayer: muwassa' (broad). The text emphasizes that delaying in prayer is makruh.
The distinction is based on the sajdah's connection to the prayer act.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars (e.g., in Hashiyat al-Durar) hold that the sajdah in prayer is muwassa' within the prayer, meaning it can be delayed until the end. Al-Tahtawi rejects this, citing the majority view (al-asahh) that delay is makruh.
The dispute revolves around whether the sajdah is part of the prayer's integrity.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Al-Tahtawi follows the most correct view that delay is makruh tanzihan, and warns that contrary views contradict the clear text (nas). The relied-upon position for fatwa is immediate performance.
If delay leads to forgetting the sajdah, it becomes a make-up (qada') and incurs sin, possibly making the delay makruh tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمام يجب على الفور إن لم تكن وجبت بتلاوته (في الصلاة) لأنها صارت جزأ من الصلاة لا يقضى خارجها فتجب فورية فيها، وغيرها تجب موسعاً (و) لكن (كره تأخيره) السجود عن وقت التلاوة في الأصح إذا لم يكن مكروهاً لأنه بطول الزمان قد ينساها فيكره تأخيرها (تنزيهاً
قوله : (في (الصلاة) أي حالة القيام لأنه لو تلاها في ركوع أو سجود ود أو تشهد أو في القومة لا يلزمه سجود لأنه محجور عن القراءة في هذه الأماكن وتصرف المحجور لا حكم له قوله: (فتجب فورية فيها حتى لو أطال التلاوة تصير قضاء، ويأثم فيكره تحريماً تأخير الصلاتية عن وقت القراءة أفاده في الشرح، وهذا ينافي ما أبداه في حاشية الدرر من قوله : ويجوز أن يقال تجب الصلاتية موسعاً بالنسبة لمحلها، كما لو تلاها في أول صلاته، وسجدها في آخرها اهـ وينافي ما ذكره السيد عنه أن تأخير الصلاتية مكروه تنزيهاً، وفي الدر، ويقضيها ما دام في حرمة الصلاة، ولو بعد السلام اهـ، وما ذكره المصنف في حاشية الدرر بحيث لا يعارض النص.
The imam must perform [sajdah] immediately if it had not become obligatory by his recitation (in prayer) because it has become a part of prayer, not performed outside it, so it must be done immediately in it. Other than that is performed broadly. However, delaying the sajdah from the time of recitation is disliked in the most correct view if it is not [a time of] dislike, because over a long time he may forget it, so delaying it is disliked (as a tanzih dislike). His statement: (in prayer) means the state of standing, because if he recited it in bowing, prostration, or tashahhud, or in the standing after bowing, no sajdah is required of him because he is prohibited from recitation in these places, and the action of one prohibited has no ruling. His statement: (so it is obligatory immediately in it) so that if he prolongs the recitation, it becomes a make-up, and he sins, so delaying the prayer sajdah from the time of recitation is prohibitively disliked, as mentioned in the Sharh. This contradicts what was presented in Hashiyat al-Durar from his statement: It may be said that the prayer sajdah is broadly obligatory with respect to its place, as if he recited at the beginning of his prayer and performed sajdah at the end of it. And it contradicts what al-Sayyid mentioned from him that delaying the prayer sajdah is only disliked as a tanzih. And in al-Durr: He performs it as long as he is within the sanctity of the prayer, even after the salam. And what the author mentioned in Hashiyat al-Durar does not contradict the text.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by al-Tahtawi on the ruling of sajdah al-tilawah performed during prayer. The base text (Maraqi al-Falah) states that when the imam recites a verse of sajdah during prayer, the sajdah becomes wajib immediately (fawran) because it has become an integral part of the prayer and cannot be performed outside it. For sajdah outside prayer, it is wajib in a broad sense (muwassa'). The text then mentions that delaying the sajdah from the time of recitation is makruh (disliked) in the most correct view, as long as the time is not itself a disliked time (like after Fajr or 'Asr), because prolonged delay may lead to forgetting. The hashia clarifies that the obligation of immediacy applies specifically when the recitation occurs in a permissible place for recitation (i.e., standing in prayer). If recited in ruku', sujud, or tashahhud, no sajdah is required. The hashia then addresses a dispute: some sources (like Hashiyat al-Durar) suggest that the sajdah in prayer is muwassa' (broad in time) and can be delayed within the prayer, but al-Tahtawi points out that this contradicts the majority view that delay is makruh tanzihi (tanzihen) or even tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) if it causes a make-up. The relied-upon position is that immediacy is wajib and delay is makruh tanzihan, following the most correct view.

Key Terms
فورية (fawriyyah): Immediate obligation: the sajdah must be performed as soon as the verse is recited, without delay.
موسعاً (muwassa'an): Broad obligation: the sajdah may be performed at any later time within a valid window, not immediately.
مكروه تنزيهاً (makrūh tanzīhan): Disliked but not sinful: delaying the sajdah is discouraged, but does not incur sin unless the delay causes forgetting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for performing sajdah al-tilawah when the verse is recited in prayer?
A) It can be delayed until after prayer.
B) It must be performed immediately and delay is disliked.
C) It is not required if the recitation is long.
D) It is only recommended, not wajib.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah during prayer must be performed immediately (fawran); delaying it is makruh tanzihan according to the most correct Hanafi view.
