Sajdah al-Tilawah: Conditions and the Persian Recitation Dispute
Conditions for obligation of sajdah on reciter and listener including Persian recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for sajdah al-tilawah on the reciter and listener, and apply the Hanafi mufta bihi position regarding Persian recitation.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib on the reciter even in Persian; on the listener it depends on understanding when the recitation is non-Arabic.

Sajdah al-tilawah is an act of worship tied to Quranic recitation, but its obligation depends on who is reciting and who is listening. This lesson unpacks the conditions from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi, clarifying when sajdah becomes wajib for the reciter and listener, with a special focus on recitation in Persian (non-Arabic). An intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions is resolved here, establishing the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Scope
State that sajdah al-tilawah is wajib. Distinguish between the ruling for the reciter and the ruling for the listener. Note that the text restricts the reciter to those who are mukallaf, in prayer, not a follower (muqtadi), and not in ruku', sujud, or tashahhud.
The reciter's own sajdah is wajib upon recitation; the follower's sajdah follows the imam.
2
List the Conditions for the Reciter
From the passage, recite the conditions: must be mukallaf (legally responsible), must be in prayer (not a follower), and must not be in a position where recitation is prohibited. Also, the reciter must not be asleep. This applies whether reciting in Arabic or Persian.
Consensus exists that Persian recitation obligates sajdah on the reciter regardless of understanding.
3
List the Conditions for the Listener
For the listener, if the recitation is in Arabic, sajdah is wajib by consensus whether he understands or not. If in Persian, there is disagreement: the mufta bihi is that it is wajib only if the listener understands the meaning.
The listener's obligation is based on hearing the verse in a way that constitutes tilawah.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Identify the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa held sajdah wajib even without understanding for Persian; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held it wajib only if understood. Note that Abu Hanifa is reported to have retracted to their view.
This dispute is recorded in al-Jawharah, and the hashia relies on the companions' view.
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi
Conclude that the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the companions' view: a listener of Persian recitation must perform sajdah only if he understands the meaning. If he does not understand, sajdah is not wajib (though doing it as a precaution is recommended).
Tarjih authority: al-Jawharah and al-Tahtawi rely on Abu Hanifa's retraction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب السجود على من تلا (آية مكلفاً بالصلاة وليس مقتدياً في غير ركوع، وسجود، وتشهد للحجر فيها عن القراءة (ولو) تلاها (بالفارسية) اتفاقاً فهم، أو لم يفهم لكونها قرآناً من وجه
قوله : (وليس مقتدياً) أي، ولا نائماً. قوله : (ولو تلاها بالفارسية) المراد بها غير العربية فتجب على السامع إذا أخبر بها . قوله : (فهم أو لم يفهم) قال في الجوهرة: أما في حق السامع فإن كانت القراءة بالعربية وجب على السامع فهم، أو لم يفهم إجماعاً، وإن كانت بالفارسية لزم السامع أيضاً، وإن لم يفهم عند الإمام وعندهما لا يلزم إلا إذا فهم، وروي رجوعه إليهما وعليه الاعتماد .اهـ. قوله : لكونها قرآناً من وجه) أي نظراً للمعنى دون وجه نظراً للنظم فباعتبار المعنى توجب السجدة، وباعتبار النظم لا توجبها، فتجب احتياطاً أفاده السيد
And sajdah is obligatory upon one who recites a verse [of sajdah] while being obligated (mukallaf) in prayer and not a follower, and not in bowing, prostration, or tashahhud due to prohibition of recitation there. Even if he recites it in Persian, [it is] agreed [upon] whether he understands or not because it is Quran from one perspective. His statement: (and not a follower) i.e., and not sleeping. His statement: (even if he recites it in Persian) what is meant is non-Arabic, so it is obligatory upon the listener if he is informed by it. His statement: (understood or not) said in al-Jawharah: As for the listener, if the recitation is in Arabic, it is obligatory upon the listener whether he understands or not by consensus. If it is in Persian, it is also necessary for the listener, even if he does not understand according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]; but according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], it is not necessary unless he understands. And it is narrated that he [Abu Hanifa] retracted to their view, and upon it is reliance. His statement: (because it is Quran from one perspective) i.e., considering the meaning, not the wording; so in consideration of meaning, it obligates the sajdah, and in consideration of wording, it does not; so it is obligatory as a precaution, as mentioned by al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage refines the conditions for sajdah al-tilawah. The base text states that sajdah is wajib on a reciter who is mukallaf (legally responsible), is in prayer, is not following an imam, and is not in a position where recitation is prohibited (ruku', sujud, tashahhud). The hashia adds that the reciter must not be asleep. The text then discusses recitation in Persian (non-Arabic): there is consensus that if recited in Persian, the reciter's own sajdah is wajib whether he understands the meaning or not, because as Quran it has two aspects—meaning and wording. For the listener, if the recitation is in Arabic, sajdah is wajib on him by consensus whether he understands or not. If the recitation is in Persian, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that sajdah is wajib on the listener even if he does not understand, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is wajib only if he understands. The hashia reports that Abu Hanifa retracted to their view, and the relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is that of the companions: the listener is obliged only if he understands the Persian recitation. This shows the final fatwa is based on the companions' view.

Key Terms
مقتدياً (muqtadiyan): A follower in prayer (ma'mum); a follower is not obliged to perform sajdah al-tilawah independently; he follows the imam.
بالفارسية (bil-fārisiyyah): In Persian; here it means any non-Arabic translation or equivalent recitation of the Quranic verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi), when is sajdah al-tilawah wajib on a listener who hears a verse of sajdah recited in Persian?
A) Always, because it is Quran from one perspective.
B) Only if the listener understands the meaning.
C) Only if the reciter is also praying.
D) Never, because it is not Quran if in Persian.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sajdah al-tilawah on a listener of a non-Arabic recitation depends on his comprehension of the meaning, per the mufta bihi Hanafi view.

Extent of Recitation Required and Number of Sajdah Verses
Debate on how much of a sajdah verse must be recited and listing of the fourteen verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimal recitation that obligates sajdah al-tilawah and identify the fourteen sajdah verses, including the dispute on al-Hajj.

Core Idea
Reciting just the word of sajdah with one word before or after suffices to obligate sajdah al-tilawah.

This lesson examines two interrelated aspects of sajdah al-tilawah: (1) how much of a sajdah verse must be recited to make the sajdah wajib, and (2) which verses of the Quran contain sajdah al-tilawah, with a particular dispute on surah al-Hajj. By understanding these, you will be able to correctly apply the rulings when reciting or listening to the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting a verse of sajdah (or part thereof). The ruling is wajib, meaning the sajdah al-tilawah becomes obligatory upon recitation (or hearing).
The obligation is on both the reciter and the hearer under specific conditions.
2
Determine the minimal recitation required
The base text states that reciting the word of sajdah (harf al-sajdah) with one word before or after it from the same verse obligates the sajdah, just like reciting the full verse. An alternative view requires reciting most of the verse.
The preferred (sahih) view in the Hanafi school is the first, as stated in the base text.
3
List the fourteen sajdah verses
The text enumerates seven surahs with their sajdah verses: al-A'raf (7:206), al-Ra'd (13:15), al-Nahl (16:49), al-Isra' (17:107-109), Maryam (19:58), al-Hajj (22:18), and al-Furqan (25:60). The remaining seven are not listed here but are known from other sources.
The total count of fourteen is agreed upon, but the location within surah al-Hajj is disputed.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on minimal recitation
Within the Hanafi school, there is a narration from Imam Muhammad that reciting most of the verse is required. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the word of sajdah with one word before or after suffices.
This highlights the process of tarjih within the madhhab.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute on al-Hajj
The Shafi'i school holds that surah al-Hajj contains two sajdah al-tilawah verses (22:18 and 22:77). The Hanafi school, based on reports from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar, maintains that only the first (22:18) is a sajdah of recitation; the second is a sajdah of prayer (ruknu).
The practical difference is that Hanafis perform one sajdah when reciting or hearing surah al-Hajj, while Shafi'is perform two.

(وقراءة حرف السجدة مع كلمة قبله أو بعده من آيتها) توجب السجود (كالآية) المقروءة بتمامها في الصحيح، وقيل: لا يجب إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة، وفي مختصر البحر لو قرأ واسجد ومكث ولم يقرأ واقترب يلزمه كلمة السجود، أو بعدها، أو متوسطة، وهو رواية عن محمد واختاره الزيلعي وتبعه في الدر. قوله : (وفي مختصر البحر الخ قد علمت أن هذا أحد أقوال، ولا تجب بكتابة، ولا نظر من غير تلفظ لأنه لم يقرأ ولم يسمع وكذا التهجي فلا تجب عليه، ولا على من سمعه لأنه تعداد الحروف، وليس بقراءة ولذا لا يجزى عن القراءة في الصلاة، ولكن لا به الصلاة لأن تلك الحروف موجودة في القرآن كذا في البحر، وفي الخانية رجل يسمع آية السجدة من قوم من كل واحد منهم حرفاً ليس عليه أن يسجد لأنه لم يسمعها من تال قاله في الدر: فأفاد أن اتحاد التالي شرط .اهـ. قال بعض الفضلاء ويحتمل أن يكون معناه أن ذلك ليس بتلاوة اهـ، ويلزم من عدم التلاوة وعدم التالي ففيه اطلاق اللازم على الملزوم قوله: (أربع عشرة آية) بفتح الشين على الأصل، وعن تميم كسرها مع المؤنث، وتسكينها أفصح، لغة الحجاز. قوله في الأعراف) علم للسورة حكاه سيبويه وحذف الجزء شائع بلا قرنها بالركوع . قوله :
(And reciting the word of sajdah with a word before it or after it from its verse) obligates the sajdah like the complete verse recited in full in the correct view. And it is said: it is not obligatory unless he recites most of the verse of sajdah. In Mukhtasar al-Bahr: If he recited 'wa-sjud' and paused and did not recite 'waqtarib', the sajdah is required. And its verses are fourteen verses: So sajdah is obligatory in al-A'raf at His statement: 'Indeed those who are with your Lord...' [7:206] and in al-Ra'd: 'And to Allah prostrates whoever is in the heavens...' [13:15] and in al-Nahl: 'And to Allah prostrates whatever is in the heavens...' [16:49] and in al-Isra': 'Those who were given knowledge before it...' [17:107-109] and in Maryam: 'Those whom Allah has favored...' [19:58] and in al-Hajj: 'Do you not see that to Allah prostrates...' [22:18] and in al-Furqan: 'And when it is said to them, prostrate to the Most Merciful...' [25:60]. And what was mentioned in al-Nahr: his statement: (and it is said: it is not obligatory unless he recites most of the verse of sajdah) whether the majority is before the word of sajdah, or after it, or in the middle, and it is a narration from Muhammad and chosen by al-Zayla'i and followed by al-Durr. His statement: (and in Mukhtasar al-Bahr etc.) you have already known that this is one of the sayings. And it is not obligatory by writing, nor by looking without uttering, because he has not recited nor heard. Similarly, spelling does not obligate it upon him nor upon the one who hears him, because it is counting letters, not recitation, and therefore it does not suffice for recitation in prayer, but it does not invalidate the prayer because those letters exist in the Quran—as in al-Bahr. And in al-Khaniyah: A man hears a verse of sajdah from a group, each one of them uttering one letter: no sajdah is required of him because he did not hear it from a single reciter. It is said in al-Durr: This indicates that the unity of the reciter is a condition. Some scholars said: Perhaps the meaning is that it is not recitation. So it follows from the absence of recitation and the absence of a reciter. His statement: (fourteen verses) with fatha on the shin according to the original, and from Tamim with kasrah with the feminine, and sukun is the most eloquent, the language of the Hijaz. His statement: (in al-A'raf) it is a proper noun for the surah, narrated by Sibawayh, and deletion of the part is common without confusion, and there is no dispute that the proper noun is Surat al-A'raf, and by this analogy for the remaining surahs, from al-Qahistani. His statement: (at His statement: 'Indeed those...') it would be better to say: after its end, 'Indeed those...' because the sajdah is after completing it, and likewise for the rest. His statement: (and al-Hajj) i.e., the first one of al-Hajj, not the second. And Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) said: In it there are two sajdahs. Our proof is what is from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar that they said: The sajdah of recitation in al-Hajj is the first one, and the second is a sajdah of prayer [ruku'], and it is supported by its connection to bowing.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues: (1) how much of a sajdah verse must be recited to obligate the sajdah, and (2) the list of fourteen verses of sajdah in the Quran with a dispute about al-Hajj. On the first issue, the base text states that reciting the single word of sajdah (e.g., 'sujud' or 'yasadun') along with one word before or after it from the same verse obligates the sajdah, just like reciting the full verse. However, there are several views: some say reciting most of the verse is required, and this is a narration from Imam Muhammad chosen by al-Zayla'i. The hashia clarifies that writing, looking without uttering, and spelling (tahtiji) do not obligate sajdah because they are not considered recitation. Also, hearing the verse from multiple people each saying one letter does not obligate sajdah; the reciter must be a single person. On the second issue, the text enumerates fourteen verses of sajdah in the following surahs: al-A'raf (7:206), al-Ra'd (13:15), al-Nahl (16:49), al-Isra' (17:107-109), Maryam (19:58), al-Hajj (22:18), and al-Furqan (25:60)—but the list continues? The text cuts off, but the hashia mentions the dispute with al-Shafi'i: The Shafi'i school holds that there are two sajdahs in surah al-Hajj (at verse 18 and verse 77). However, the Hanafi position, based on reports from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar, is that only the first (verse 18) is a sajdah of recitation; the second (verse 77, which says 'submit to Allah') is a sajdah of prayer (i.e., ruku') and not a separate sajdah al-tilawah. The hashia supports the Hanafi view by noting that the second verse is linked to bowing (ruknu).

Key Terms
حرف السجدة (harf al-sajdah): The word(s) indicating prostration in a verse of sajdah, such as 'sujud', 'yasadun', 'asjudu', etc.
آية السجدة (āyat al-sajdah): A verse in the Quran that contains an explicit command or description of prostration, recitation of which obligates sajdah al-tilawah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that reciting the word of sajdah with one word before or after obligates sajdah al-tilawah, and that surah al-Hajj contains only one such sajdah.

The 14 Verses of Prostration and Their Obligation in the Hanafi School
Lists the 14 verses of prostration and discusses rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the fourteen verses of prostration according to the Hanafi school, state that the ruling is wajib, and explain the Hanafi proof and the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding Surah Sad.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds fourteen wajib prostrations in recitation, distinct from other schools.

Prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) is an act of worship that becomes obligatory upon reciting or hearing certain verses of the Quran. This lesson identifies the fourteen verses that trigger this obligation according to the Hanafi school, explains the general ruling, and addresses key differences with the Shafi'i school, particularly regarding Surah Sad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The passage begins with: 'Prostration is (like the verse) that is recited in its entirety.' This means the obligation attaches to reciting a complete verse of prostration. Note that there is a weaker opinion that reciting most of the verse suffices.
The mufta bihi is the obligation upon reciting the entire verse, but reciting the word of prostration with one letter before and one after is considered like the whole verse.
2
Enumerate the Fourteen Verses
The passage lists specific verses from Surahs Al-A'raf, Ar-Ra'd, An-Nahl, Al-Isra', Maryam, Al-Hajj, Al-Furqan, An-Naml, As-Sajdah, and Sad. Write down each surah and the approximate location of the prostration verse.
Refer to the Arabic text for the exact phrases that mark the prostration.
3
Examine the Dispute on Surah An-Naml
The passage discusses two recitations (with shaddah and takhfif) for the verse of prostration in An-Naml. According to al-Farra', the obligation depends on the recitation. However, the correct view (al-asahh) is that prostration is obligatory on both recitations because the verse was written in the 'Uthmanic mushaf.
This shows the Hanafi tendency to unify rulings across valid qira'at.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i Disagreement on Surah Sad
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the prostration in Sad as a prostration of thanksgiving, not an obligatory recitation prostration. The Hanafi position is that it is wajib, supported by hadith of the Prophet prostrating upon reciting it.
This is a key difference; the Hanafi school includes it among the fourteen.
5
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The practical difference: In prayer, a Hanafi must prostrate when reciting the verse of Sad, whereas a Shafi'i does not perform a recitation prostration for it, and if he does, it may invalidate his prayer according to the Shafi'i school.
This highlights why knowing the precise list and ruling is crucial for daily worship.

كتاب الصلاة
السجود (كالآية) المقروءة بتمامها في الصحيح، وقيل: لا يجب إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة، وفي مختصر البحر لو قرأ واسجد ومكث ولم يقرأ واقترب يلزمه السجدة (وآياتها أربع عشرة آية فتجب السجدة (في الأعراف عند قوله تعالى: إن الذين عند ربك لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ويسبحونه وله يسجدون ﴾ [الأعراف/ ۷] (وفي الرعد) والله يسجد من في السموات والأرض طوعاً وكرهاً وظلالهم بالغدو والآصال والنحل) والله يسجد ما في السموات وما في الأرض من دابة والملائكة وهم لا يستكبرون يخافون ربهم من فوقهم ويفعلون ما يؤمرون (والإسراء) إن الذين أوتوا العلم من قبله إذا يتلى عليهم يخرون للأذقان سجداً ويقولون سبحان ربنا إن كان وعد ربنا لمفعولاً ويخرون للأذقان يبكون ويزيدهم خشوعاً (ومريم) أولئك الذين أنعم الله عليهم من النبيين من ذرية آدم وممن حملنا مع نوح ومن ذرية إبراهيم وإسرائيل وممن هدينا واجتبينا إذا تتلى عليهم آيات الرحمن خروا سجداً وبكياً (والحج) ألم تر أن الله يسجد له من في السموات ومن في الأرض، والشمس والقمر والنجوم والجبال والشجر والدواب وكثير من الناس وكثير حق عليه العذاب ومن يهن فما له من مكرم إن الله يفعل ما يشاء والفرقان) وإذا قيل لهم اسجدوا للرحمن قالوا وما الرحمن أنسجد لما تأمرنا وزادهم نفوراً ( والنمل) ألا يسجدوا الله الذي يخرج الخبء في السموات والأرض، ويعلم ما يخفون وما يعلنون الله لا إله إلا هو رب العرش العظيم. وهذا على قراءة العامة بالتشديد وعند قوله تعالى ألا يا اسجدوا، على قراءة الكسائي بالتخفيف وفي المجتبى قال الفراء : إنما تجب السجدة في النمل على قراءة الكسائي أي بالتخفيف وينبغي أن لا تجب بالتشديد لأن معناها زين لهم الشيطان أن لا يسجدوا والأصح هو الوجوب على القراءتين لأنه كتب في مصحف عثمان رضي الله عنه كذا في الدراية (والسجدة) إنما يؤمن بآياتنا الذين إذا ذكروا بها خروا سجداً وسبحوا بحمد ربهم، لا يستكبرون (وص) أخرج البخاري عن العوام بن حوشب قال : سألت مجاهداً عن سجدة ص، فقال: سألت ابن عباس من أين سجدت في ص ، فقال : أو ما تقرأ ومن ذريته داود وسليمان، إلى أولئك الذين هدى الله فبهداهم اقتده فكان داود ممن أمر نبيكم أن يقتدى به، فسجدها داود فسجدها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأخرج الإمام أحمد عن بكر بن عبدالله المزني عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : رأيت رؤيا، وأنا أكتب سورة ص فلما بلغت السجدة رأيت الدواة والقلم، وكل شيء يحضرني انقلب ساجداً فقصصتها على رسول الله ، فلم يزل يسجد بها كذا في البرهان، وفي رواية فقال : نحن أحق بها من الدواة والقلم فأمر أن تكتب في مجلسه وسجدها مع كذا The most correct is obligation on both recitations because it was written in the Mushaf of 'Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him). Likewise in al-Diraya. (And in al-Sajdah): 'Only those believe in Our verses who, when they are reminded by them, fall prostrating and exalt [Allah] with praise of their Lord...' (al-Sajdah 32:15) (and in Sad). And al-Shafi'i said: The prostration in Sad is not from the 'aza'im (i.e., emphatic prostrations); rather it is a prostration of thanksgiving, recommended outside prayer, and forbidden in prayer according to the most correct view of his school. (His statement: 'And Dawud thought...' i.e., he was certain. (His statement: 'Indeed We tried him...' i.e., We placed him in a trial of tribulation through love of that woman. (His statement: 'Obligatory at His statement...' the sentence is a substitute for 'what', and perhaps this is based on one of the previous opinions, which is the opinion that obligation is connected to the entirety of the verse...
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the verses of prostration (ayat al-sajdah). It begins by stating the general rule: prostration is obligatory when one recites a verse of prostration in its entirety. There is a weaker opinion that it is only obligatory if one recites most of the verse. The text then enumerates the fourteen verses where prostration is obligatory, mentioning specific verses from Surat al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Sajdah, and Sad. For al-Hajj, it notes that Imam al-Shafi'i held there are two prostrations, but the Hanafi position is that only the first is a prostration of recitation, while the second is the prostration of prayer (sajdat al-salah). For al-Naml, the passage discusses the difference in qira'ah between the general recitation (with shaddah) and that of al-Kisa'i (with takhfif), and concludes that prostration is obligatory on both readings because the verse was written in the 'Uthmanic mushaf without distinction. For Surah Sad, the text presents evidence from hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated upon reciting it, and cites the disagreement with al-Shafi'i, who considers it a prostration of thanksgiving rather than an obligatory one. The Hanafi position, supported by the actions of the Prophet and his companions, is that it is among the fourteen obligatory prostrations. The commentary also explains the condition that the recitation must be from a reciter, not from writing or looking without reciting, and that the reciter must be one person (not multiple people each reciting a different letter).

Key Terms
آية السجدة (āyat al-sajdah): A verse of the Quran whose recitation or hearing makes prostration obligatory according to the Hanafi school.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran. It is wajib in the Hanafi school.
عزائم السجود (ʿazāʾim al-sujūd): The emphatically obligatory prostrations of recitation, as opposed to recommended ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates fourteen specific verses of prostration, supported by the practice of the Prophet and the Companions.

Hanafi Preference for Delaying Sajdah Tilawah in Surah Fussilat
Explaining Hanafi position on sajdah ayahs and ihtiyat reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi reasoning for delaying sajdah tilawah in Surah Fussilat and apply the principle of ihtiyat in similar inter-madhhab disputes.

Core Idea
In inter-madhhab disputes, Hanafi ihtiyat chooses the safer option to avoid prayer deficiency.

This lesson examines the precise Quranic verse for sajdah tilawah in Surah Fussilat, where the Hanafi school and Shafi'i school differ. Al-Tahtawi explains why Hanafis prefer the later verse based on ihtiyat (legal caution), a hallmark of Hanafi methodology. Understanding this reasoning deepens your fiqh literacy and shows how the school navigates ikhtilaf among the companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ayahs
In Surah Fussilat, two ayahs are candidates for sajdah: earlier "إن كنتم إياه تعبدون" (if it is Him you worship) and later "فإن استكبروا فالذين عند ربك يسبحون..." (then if they are arrogant...). Note the exact wording in Arabic.
The earlier ayah is verse 37, the later is verse 38 in standard numbering.
2
State the Hanafi position and its source
The Hanafi school takes the later ayah (فإن استكبروا...). This is reported from Ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hajar, and it is the zahir al-riwayah position in the Hanafi school.
Zahir al-riwayah refers to the authoritative transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books.
3
State the opposing Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the sajdah is at the earlier ayah (إن كنتم إياه تعبدون), based on reports from Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar.
This is also a valid ikhtilaf among the sahaba.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response using ihtiyat
The Hanafi reasoning: if the sajdah is wajib at the earlier ayah, delaying to the later ayah still fulfills the obligation without harm. But if it is wajib only at the later ayah, performing it earlier would be a deficiency (an extra prostration before its cause). Therefore, to be safe (ihtiyat), delay to the later ayah.
This rational argument is called 'aqli and is a sign of deep fiqh (amarat al-tabahhur fil-fiqh).
5
Apply the same reasoning to other surahs
The same principle applies to Surah Najm (at: أفمن هذا الحديث...), Inshiqaq (at: فما لهم لا يؤمنون...), Alaq (at: كلا لا تطعه واسجد واقترب), and as mentioned in the text, also to Surah Sad.
In each case, ihtiyat dictates choosing the later sajdah ayah to avoid potential deficiency.

The sajdah: 'Then if they are arrogant, those near your Lord glorify Him by night and day and they never tire.' From His saying: 'And of His signs are the night and the day and the sun and the moon. Do not prostrate to the sun nor to the moon, but prostrate to Allah who created them, if it is Him you worship. Then if they are arrogant, those near your Lord glorify Him by night and day and they never tire.' This is according to our school, and it is reported from Ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hajar. According to al-Shafi'i, at His saying: 'if it is Him you worship.' And it is the school of Ali and reported from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Umar. Our imams preferred the first, taking caution when the schools of the companions differ. For if the sajdah were obligatory at His saying 'you worship,' then delaying to His saying 'they never tire' does no harm and fulfills the obligation. And if it were obligatory at His saying 'they never tire,' then the intended sajdah before it would have occurred before its obligation and the existence of its cause, which would necessitate a deficiency in the prayer if it were a prayer prostration. And there is no deficiency in what we say at all. And this is a sign of deep fiqh. Thus in al-Bahr from al-Bada'i. So in what I said before regarding it, likewise; otherwise contradiction would be necessary. And this is the explanation we promised. (And) in (al-Najm) at His saying: 'Do you then wonder at this discourse? And you laugh and do not weep, while you are heedless? So prostrate to Allah and worship.' (And) in (al-Inshiqaq) at His saying: 'Then what is wrong with them that they do not believe, and when the Quran is recited to them, they do not prostrate?' (And) in (Iqra') at His saying: 'Nay, do not obey him, but prostrate and draw near.' And we will mention the benefit of this combination as well. The delaying at His saying: 'and good abode' does no harm and fulfills the obligation. And if it were obligatory at His saying 'and good abode' and he preceded it at His saying 'and returned,' then the prostration would have occurred before its obligation and the existence of its cause, which would necessitate a deficiency in the prayer if it were a prayer prostration. And there is no deficiency in the delay. And you know that this is based on one of the previous statements. (His saying: 'those near your Lord'—'nearness' is one of honor, and this is based on the fact that the sentence before it is one verse. His saying: 'before it' i.e., before His saying 'they never tire.' His saying: 'before its obligation'—it is better to dispense with what comes after it because when the cause of obligation is not present, it is not obligatory. And you know that this is according to one of the statements. His saying 'in what we said' i.e., from delaying. His saying 'and this' i.e., preferring the first to take caution. His saying 'a sign of deep fiqh' i.e., a mark of the wide knowledge of its speaker. His saying 'in Sad' is an extra adverbial related to his saying 'I said.' His saying 'likewise' i.e., like the sajdah of Fussilat. His saying 'otherwise contradiction would be necessary' i.e., if we do not say in Sad as we said in Fussilat that he prostrates at His saying 'and returned,' contradiction would be necessary, for it would require preceding it before its place, causing a deficiency in prayer, and no caution in it. His saying 'and this is the explanation' is an indication to his saying 'for if the sajdah were obligatory etc.,' and the meaning is that it is its parallel. His saying 'we promised with it' by his saying 'we will mention.' His saying 'and we will mention the benefit of this combination' refers to the benefit mentioned at the end of the chapter on sajdah of shukr, and his saying 'also' i.e., as we mentioned its benefit here, the difference that occurred in the place.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah. It discusses the specific verses where sajdah tilawah is wajib in four surahs: Fussilat, Najm, Inshiqaq, and Alaq. The author points out the difference between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the exact ayah in Fussilat. The Hanafi view, reported from Ibn Abbas and Wail ibn Hajar, places the sajdah at the later ayah "فإن استكبروا فالذين عند ربك يسبحون.." while Shafi'i places it at the earlier ayah "إن كنتم إياه تعبدون". Hanafis prefer the later ayah based on ihtiyat (legal caution). The reasoning: if the sajdah were obligatory at the earlier ayah, delaying it to the later one does no harm and still fulfills the obligation. But if it were obligatory only at the later ayah, performing it earlier would cause a deficiency in prayer (as it would be an extra prostration before its obligation). Therefore, to be safe, they delay it. This reasoning is described as a sign of deep fiqh. The same principle applies to other surahs. The commentary then explains various phrases in the original text, including the application to Surah Sad.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilawah): Prostration performed when reciting or hearing specific Quranic verses.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Legal caution; choosing the option that ensures fulfillment of obligation and avoids risk of deficiency.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Sajdah Tilawah: Conditions and Exceptions
Ruling on sajdah tilawah obligation with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who is obligated to perform sajdah tilawah upon hearing a prostration verse, explain the exceptions for menstruating and postpartum women, and apply the specific rules for the imam and follower in congregational prayer.

Core Idea
Sajdah tilawah is wajib upon hearing a prostration verse, but the obligation is lifted for menstruating/postpartum women, and special rules govern the imam and follower during prayer.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah refines the general rule of sajdah tilawah by detailing exceptions and special circumstances. While the general principle is that anyone who hears a prostration verse must prostrate, the Hanafi school exempts women in menstruation or postpartum state, and carefully distinguishes the obligations of an imam and his follower during congregational prayer. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly applying the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the default ruling: sajdah tilawah is wajib upon hearing a verse of sajdah, whether one intended to listen or not, and whether one understood or not.
The rule covers both intentional and unintentional hearing.
2
Examine the first exception
Note that menstruating (ha'id) and postpartum (nufasa') women are not obligated by their own recitation or hearing, but hearing from them obligates others.
The exception is based on their ineligibility for prayer.
3
Consider the effect of the reciter's state
Understand that hearing from a junub, a disbeliever, or a discerning child also obligates sajdah, but hearing from an insane person or a sleeper does not.
Valid recitation requires discernment.
4
Analyze the imam-follower rules
Learn that the imam and his follower are not obligated by hearing from a fellow follower of that imam or another imam; they must prostrate after prayer if hearing from an outsider. Prostrating during prayer is deficient but does not invalidate the prayer.
The rule prevents introducing extraneous acts into the prayer.
5
Refine with a note on non-Arab and jinn
Understand that a pure non-Arab who does not understand is not obliged until he knows it is a sajdah verse; hearing from a jinn or angel likely obligates sajdah.
Knowledge of the obligation is necessary for liability.

منهما لصدور التلاوة الصحيحة منهما (١) . قوله : (كما تجب على الجنب) تلا أو سمع للأهلية، وكافر لأنه مخاطب بالصلاة فهو أهل لها قوله : (وصبي مميز) في الفتح ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنها لا تجب بالسماع من مجنون، أو نائم لأن السبب سماع تلاوة صحيحة، وصحتها بالتمييز ولم يوجد اهـ . قال : وهذا التعليل يفيد التفصيل في الصبي إن كان له تمييز وجب بالسماع منه وإلا فلا، فليكن هو المعتبر اهـ. قوله : (أو بإمام (آخر) هذا خلاف الأصح، والأصح الوجوب على من ليس مشاركاً له في تلك الصلاة مطلقاً سواء كان السامع في جماعة أخرى، أو منفرداً، أو خارجاً بالكلية لأن الحجر ثبت في حق جماعة معينين فلا يعد وهم كذا في الهداية قوله: (لتحقق السبب) وهو التلاوة الصحيحة كذا في السراج قوله : (وزوال المانع أي بفراغ الصلاة، فتقضي خارجها، إذ هي ليست صلاتية. قوله : (من فعلها) بيان للمانع قوله (النقصانها) أي سجدة التلاوة بفعلها في الصلاة لمكان النهي، فيعيدونها لتتأدى بالكامل، كذا في الشرح، وإنما نهي عنها لأنها أجنبية . عن تلك الصلاة حيث لم تكن من قراءتها ولا يدخل في الصلاة ما هو أجنبي منها قال في البحر، ويستثنى من هذا ما إذا قرأ المصلي غير المقتدي تلك السجدة التي سمعها ممن ليس مع في الصلاة، وسجد لها فيها فإنه لا إعادة عليه، ونابت تلك السجدة عنهما جميعاً، وتمامه (1) قوله كما يجب على الجنب الذي في الشرح هنا ومن الجنب فليراجع اهـ.
Prayer section: The Arabic recitation: (Even if they did not intend to listen) understanding or not understanding is reported from the senior companions. (Except that he made an exception:) (the menstruating and the postpartum) so it is not obligatory on them by their recitation or hearing at all, and (it is obligatory by hearing from them and from the junub (impure person) and by hearing from a disbeliever and a discerning child). (And) except (the imam and the follower, so it is not obligatory on them by hearing from a follower of the imam or from another imam). And (it is obligatory on one who is not in their hearing from the follower) according to the most sound opinion. And if they (the followers and the imam) hear it from someone else (i.e., other than the follower), they should prostrate after the prayer because the cause is realized and the impediment from doing it in the prayer is removed. (If they prostrate in it (the prayer), it does not suffice them due to its deficiency, but their prayer is not invalidated because it is of its type) in the manifest transmission. And it is the prostration in some verses. (His saying: 'understanding or not understanding') Ibn Amir Haj said: It is appropriate to exclude from this the pure ajami (non-Arab) and the new convert to Islam, so the prostration is not obligatory on him for recitation of the Quranic text, nor by hearing it, except after knowing that what is recited is a prostration verse, meaning even if he did not understand, because obligation without knowledge is impossible. So if he dies before performing and knowledge of obligation, there is no sin on him, and it is not obligatory on him except at the time of knowledge. And it is determined in al-Fath. If he hears it from a jinn, obligation is apparent, as stated by al-Sayyid; some say the same for an angel. His saying: 'so it is not obligatory on them by their recitation' because the prostration is a pillar of prayer, and they are not fit for it, as in al-Tabyin. His saying: 'and their hearing' meaning it is not obligatory except on one who is fit for prayer in both performance and making up, and they are not fit for it absolutely. His saying: 'and it is obligatory by hearing from them' because the valid recitation emanates from them. His saying: 'as it is obligatory on the junub' whether he recited or heard, due to eligibility; and a disbeliever because he is addressed by prayer, so he is eligible. His saying: 'and a discerning child' - in al-Fath, Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that it is not obligatory by hearing from an insane person or a sleeping one because the cause is hearing a valid recitation, and its validity is by discernment, which is absent. He said: This reasoning indicates a difference in the child: if he has discernment, it is obligatory by hearing from him; otherwise not. So that should be the consideration. His saying: 'or from another imam' - this is contrary to the most sound opinion; the most sound is that it is obligatory on one who is not sharing in that prayer absolutely, whether the listener is in another congregation, alone, or completely outside, because the prohibition is established for specific persons, so it does not extend to others. Thus in al-Hidaya. His saying: 'because the cause is realized' i.e., the valid recitation, as in al-Siraj. His saying: 'and the impediment is removed' i.e., by the completion of the prayer, so they perform it outside, as it is not a prayer prostration. His saying: 'from doing it' is an explanation of the impediment. His saying: 'its deficiency' i.e., the prostration of recitation by doing it in the prayer due to the prohibition, so they repeat it to perform it completely, as in al-Sharh. It is prohibited because it is extraneous to that prayer since it is not from its recitation, and what is extraneous to the prayer is not included in it. He said in al-Bahr: From this is excluded the case where the praying person, other than the follower, recites that prostration which he heard from one who is not with him in the prayer, and prostrated for it in the prayer; then there is no repetition on him, and that prostration suffices for both of them. End. (1) His saying: as it is obligatory on the junub which is in al-Sharh here and from the junub, so let it be reviewed.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies the conditions for the obligation of sajdah tilawah. The general rule is that whoever hears a verse of sajdah must prostrate, whether they intended to listen or not, and whether they understood or not. However, there are exceptions. Firstly, menstruating women (ha'id) and postpartum women (nufasa') are not obligated by their own recitation nor by hearing, because they are not fit for prayer which includes sajdah. However, if others hear from them, it is obligatory because the recitation is valid. Similarly, hearing from a junub (in state of impurity) or from a disbeliever or a discerning child obligates sajdah. Secondly, for an Imam and his follower, if they hear sajdah from a follower of their own imam or another imam during prayer, it is not obligatory on them due to the impediment of being in prayer? Actually the text says they are not obligated by hearing from a follower of the imam they are following. But if they hear from someone else, they must prostrate after prayer. If they prostrate during prayer, it does not suffice and they must repeat, but their prayer is not invalidated. This is the ruling in zahir al-riwayah. The commentary then elaborates on each point, including the case of a non-Arab who doesn't understand, and the case of hearing from a jinn.

Key Terms
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman in her menstrual period.
النفساء (al-nufasa'): A woman in post-childbirth bleeding.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A man in a state of janabah
B) A menstruating woman
C) A discerning child
D) A disbeliever

Key Takeaway
Sajdah tilawah is generally wajib upon hearing a prostration verse, but the obligation is lifted for menstruating and postpartum women, and specific rules apply during congregational prayer for the imam and follower.

Salah — Prayer

Obligation and Exceptions of Sajdat al-Tilawa for the Hearer
Critical refinement of sajdat al-tilawa rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which sajdat al-tilawa is wajib upon hearing and identify the exceptions, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving the imam, follower, menstruating woman, and non-Muslim.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawa is wajib upon hearing even without intention or understanding, but exemptions apply to menstruating women and specific congregational contexts.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on when the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa) becomes obligatory upon hearing a verse of prostration. The general rule is broad—obligation arises regardless of intent or comprehension—but there are important exceptions that protect the integrity of prayer and accommodate those not eligible for prayer. We will trace the reasoning from the text, focusing on the key exemptions and the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf concerning the imam and follower in congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The text opens with the rule that sajdat al-tilawa is obligatory upon hearing a prostration verse even if one did not intend to listen and regardless of understanding. This is based on reports from senior Companions.
The rule emphasizes the objective nature of the cause (hearing valid recitation).
2
Recognize the exemptions
Two groups are exempted: (1) menstruating women and women in postpartum bleeding—they are not obligated by their own recitation or hearing, but others hearing them are obligated. (2) The imam and follower in a specific context: they are not obligated during the prayer when hearing from a fellow follower of the same imam or another imam, according to the most correct view.
The exemption for the imam/follower is due to the restriction (hajr) of being in the same prayer.
3
Analyze the ruling for imam and follower hearing from outside the congregation
If the imam and followers hear a prostration verse from someone not in their prayer (e.g., a visitor), they must prostrate after the prayer. The cause (hearing valid recitation) is established, and the obstacle (being in prayer) is removed after completion.
If they prostrated during the prayer, it would not suffice and they must repeat it after; but the prayer is not invalidated.
4
Understand the effect on the prayer if sajda is performed during it
Performing sajdat al-tilawa during the prayer does not invalidate the prayer, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). However, the prostration itself is defective and must be repeated after prayer. If the follower follows the reciter in prostration during the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid.
The reasoning is that an extra prostration is of the same genre (sajda) and does not break the tahrima, but following the reciter is prohibited.

فسدت ولا تجزيه السجدة عما كما في البحر والنهر، قوله: (لأنها من سمع جنسها وزيادة سجدة واحدة لا تبطل التحريمة. قوله : (وهو الصحيح وقيل : لا تفسد ونسب إلى محمد، وفي غاية البيان الأصح عدم الفساد اتفاقاً
And if he did not intend to hear, whether he understood or not, it is narrated from the great Companions. Except that he exempted the menstruating woman and the woman in postpartum bleeding: the prostration is not obligatory upon them by their own recitation or hearing, but it is obligatory upon hearing from them and from the person in major ritual impurity (junub), and by hearing it from a disbeliever and a discerning child. And except the imam and the follower: it is not obligatory upon them by hearing from a follower of the imam who is listening, or from another imam; but it is obligatory upon one who is not in the hearing of the follower, according to the most correct view. And if they (i.e., the followers and the imam) heard it from someone other than the follower, they should prostrate after the prayer due to the cause being established and the obstacle (of being in prayer) being removed from performing it in the prayer. And if they prostrated during the prayer, it would not suffice them due to its deficiency, and their prayer would not be invalidated because it is of its kind, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). And this is the prostration in some verses. His statement: 'whether he understood or not' – Ibn Amir Haj said: one should exclude from this someone like a pure non-Arab, a new Muslim, so the prostration is not obligatory upon him by recitation of the Qur'anic text nor by hearing it except after knowing that what was recited is a verse of prostration, meaning even if he did not understand, because obligation of what one has no knowledge of is impossible; so if he dies before performing it and before knowing the obligation, there is no sin upon him, and it is not obligatory upon him except at the time of knowledge. This is affirmed in al-Fath. And if he heard it from a jinn, apparently it is obligatory, as the sayyid mentioned, and some said the same for an angel. His statement: 'it is not obligatory upon them by their own recitation' because the prostration is a pillar of prayer, and they are not fit for it, as in al-Tabyin. His statement: 'and their hearing' – it is only obligatory upon one who is fit for prayer in performance and makeup, and they are not fit for it absolutely. His statement: 'and it is obligatory by hearing from them' because valid recitation emanates from them. His statement: 'as it is obligatory upon the junub' whether he recited or heard, due to eligibility, and upon a disbeliever because he is addressed with prayer, so he is fit for it. His statement: 'and a discerning child' – in al-Fath, Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that it is not obligatory by hearing from a madman or a sleeper because the cause is hearing a valid recitation, and its validity requires discernment, which is absent. He said: This reasoning implies detail in the child: if he has discernment, it is obligatory by hearing from him; otherwise, not. So let this be the criterion. His statement: 'or with another imam' – this contradicts the most correct view, and the most correct is that it is obligatory upon one who does not share in that prayer absolutely, whether the listener is in another congregation, alone, or completely outside, because the restriction is established for a specific group, so they are not considered, as in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'due to the cause being established' – i.e., the valid recitation, as in al-Siraj. His statement: 'and the obstacle removed' – i.e., by finishing the prayer, so he performs it outside, since it is not part of the prayer. His statement: 'from performing it' clarifies the obstacle. His statement: 'due to its deficiency' – meaning the prostration of recitation, performing it during the prayer due to the prohibition, so they repeat it to fulfill it completely, as in al-Sharh. It is prohibited because it is extraneous to that prayer, not being from its recitation, and what is extraneous to the prayer cannot enter it. In al-Bahr, an exception is made: if the reciter (not the follower) recites that verse of prostration which the follower heard from someone not in the prayer, and he prostrates for it during the prayer, then there is no repetition upon him, and that prostration suffices for both. And its completion: In his statement: 'and it does not invalidate their prayer' – it is restricted in al-Tajnis and others to when the reciter does not follow the one performing prostration in his prostration; if he follows, it invalidates and the prostration does not suffice him, as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. His statement: 'because it is of its kind' – and an extra prostration does not invalidate the tahrima. His statement: 'this is the correct view, and it was said that it does not invalidate, attributed to Muhammad, and in Ghayat al-Bayan, the most correct is that it does not invalidate unanimously.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement of the rulings on sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation). It begins by stating the general rule: the obligation to prostrate upon hearing a verse of prostration applies even if one did not intend to hear, and regardless of understanding, as reported from senior Companions. However, there are exceptions. The first exception is the menstruating woman and the woman in postpartum bleeding: they are not obligated by their own recitation or hearing because they are not eligible for prayer, which is a prerequisite. But if they recite, others hearing them are obligated because their recitation is valid. The second exception involves the imam and the follower (muqtadi). If the follower hears the verse from another follower of the same imam or from another imam, the imam and follower are not obligated during the prayer. But according to the most correct view, if one hears from a follower, the obligation applies to those not part of that specific congregation. The passage then addresses the case where the imam and followers hear the verse from someone outside the prayer: they should perform the prostration after the prayer, because the cause (hearing valid recitation) is established, and the obstacle (being in prayer) is removed after finishing. If they prostrate during the prayer, it does not suffice and they must repeat, but the prayer is not invalidated because the prostration is of the same genre (sajda) and adding one prostration does not nullify the prayer according to the apparent narration. However, if the follower follows the reciter in prostration during prayer, it becomes invalid. The commentary then elaborates on various points: the condition of understanding for a non-Arab or new Muslim, the ruling for hearing from a jinn or angel, the distinction between a madman and a child, and the exception to the prohibition of prostrating during prayer if the reciter and the listener share the prostration. Overall, the passage provides nuanced guidance on when sajdat al-tilawa is obligatory and how it interacts with prayer.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Qur'an that commands prostration.
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding; she is exempt from the obligation of sajdat al-tilawa whether reciting or hearing, because she is not eligible for prayer.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer; specific rulings apply to him regarding sajdat al-tilawa when hearing from another follower.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the early Hanafi imams, especially from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Used here to indicate the authoritative position that performing sajdat al-tilawa during prayer does not invalidate it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the imam and follower when they hear a sajda verse from a fellow follower of another imam during the prayer?
A) They are obligated to prostrate immediately during the prayer.
B) They are not obligated at all, neither during nor after.
C) They are not obligated during the prayer, but must prostrate after the prayer.
D) They are obligated only if they understood the verse.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawa is wajib upon hearing, but the obligation is suspended for menstruating women and for the imam/follower in specific congregational contexts; if performed during prayer, it does not invalidate the prayer but must be repeated after.

Sajdat al-Tilawa from Persian Recitation and Problematic Cases
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sajdat al-tilawa from Persian recitation and hearing from sleepers, madmen, drunks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for sajdat al-tilawa when hearing Persian recitation and identify which cases (sleeper, madman, drunk) affect the obligation, applying the Hanafi intra-school ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawa from Persian recitation requires understanding the meaning; from a sleeper or madman, it is not obligatory due to invalid recitation.

The obligation of prostration of recitation hinges on the validity of the recitation heard. This lesson examines two edge cases: when the Qur'an is recited in Persian, and when the reciter is in a state of sleep, madness, or intoxication. We will see how Abu Hanifa's initial view differed from that of his two students and why his later retraction shapes the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Sajdat al-tilawa. Determine its hukm level: wajib when conditions are met.
The passage states the correct view that it is obligatory (wajib).
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Persian recitation
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa's earlier view (obligatory even without understanding if informed) versus the view of the two disciples (requires understanding). Note Abu Hanifa's retraction.
The basis is whether Persian is Qur'an from all aspects or only in meaning.
3
Understand the condition of understanding and being informed
According to the relied-upon view, understanding is required. Additionally, if the listener does not know it is a prostration verse, being informed is also necessary (according to the two).
The text says: 'إذا أخبر بأنها آية سجدة أما إذا لم يخبر فلا تجب'.
4
Apply to cases of sleeper, madman, and drunk
For a sleeper or madman: recitation is invalid due to lack of discernment, so no obligation unless the sleeper reports his own recitation. For a drunk: generally obligatory, but if drunkenness from a permissible cause with no awareness, it does not obligate.
The passage reports multiple narrations; the preferred view is non-obligation for sleeper/madman.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is that sajdat al-tilawa from Persian recitation requires understanding; from a sleeper or madman (without report) is not obligatory; from a drunk with discernment is obligatory.
This shows the complexity of Hanafi ijtihad and the importance of tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصحيح (وتجب) السجدة (بسماع) القراءة باللغة الفارسية إن فهمها على المعتمد) وهذا عندهما ويجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة وإن لم يفهم معناها إذا أخبر بأنها آية سجدة، ومبنى الخلاف على أن الفارسية قرآن من كل وجه أو من وجه وإذا فهم تجب احتياطاً واختلف التصحيح في وجوبها على السامع (بالسماع من نائم أو مجنون) ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنه لا يجب لعدم صحة التلاوة وبفقد التمييز، وفي التترخانية سمعها من نائم قيل تجب والصحيح أنها لا تجب، وفي الخانية الصحيح هو الوجوب، وفي الخلاصة سمعها من طير لا تجب هو المختار ومن نائم الصحيح أنها تجب ومثله في قاضيخان، وإذا أخبر أنه قرأها في نومه تجب عليه وهو الأصح وفي الدراية لا يلزمه هو الصحيح وقراءة السكران موجبة عليه، فيه قوله: (وهذا عندهما) وروى رجوعه إليهما وعليه الاعتماد كذا في الجوهرة قوله : ( وتجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة) أي على القول المرجوع عن من جواز الصلاة بها سواء كان يحسن العربية، أو لا فتكون قرآناً من كل وجه فتجب وأما قوله المرجوع إليه فهو كقولهما، فلا تجب السجدة إلا بالفهم لأنها قرآن من وجه، وهو المعنى دون وجه وهو النظم، فإذا فهم كان سامعاً للقرآن من وجه دون وجه، فتجب احتياطاً. قوله : (إذا أخبر بأنها آية سجدة أما إذا لم يخبر فلا تجب لأنه لا تكليف بدون علم، أو دليله، ويفهم منه أنه على قولهما يشترط الفهم والإخبار معاً قوله : (أو مجنون) في الذخيرة ذكر في نوادر الصلاة أن الجنون إذا قصر بأن كان يوماً وليلة أو أقل تلزمه السجدة بالتلاوة، والسماع حال الجنون، فيؤديها بعد الإفاقة لأنه أهل للقضاء قال المحقق ابن أمير حاج : وفيه نظر، بل الوجه أنه لا يجب على المجنون شيء إذا سمع أو تلا في حالة الجنون مطلقاً سواء كان قصيراً أو مطبقاً لأنه ليس بأحسن حالاً من النائم والمغمى عليه، وهما لا تجب عليهما بالأمرين في الحالين فكذا هذا اهـ. قوله : (سمعها من طير لا تجب الأولى تأخير هذه الجملة عند قول المصنف الآتي ولا تجب من سماعها من الطير ويجعلها دليلاً عليه قوله: (وإذا أخبر الخ) هذ مسألة زائدة عما في المصنف قصد بها التنبيه على الحكم في حق النائم إذا تلا. قوله : (وقراءة السكران موجبة عليه قال المحقق ابن أمير :حاج وينبغي أن يقال على ما يظهر هذا التعليل ان الوجوب يختص بسكران من محظور لا من مباح كما لو غص بلقمة، ولم يجد ما يسيغها به إلا الخمر، وخاف هلاك نفسه إن لم يسغها، فشرب منه ما أساغها فقط فسكر من ذلك، أو أكره على الشرب الإكراه الشرعي، وتلا في حالة السكر، أو وليس عنده مسكة يميز بها ما يقول وما يسمع حتى انه لا يتذكر ذلك بعد الصحو، فلا تجب عليه من سمع
The correct view is that the prostration is obligatory by hearing recitation in the Persian language if he understands it, according to the relied-upon view. This is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And it is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa even if he does not understand its meaning, if he is informed that it is a verse of prostration. The basis of the disagreement is whether Persian is Qur'an from all aspects or from one aspect. And if he understands, it is obligatory as a precaution. There is disagreement on the correct view regarding its obligation upon the listener by hearing from a sleeper or a madman. Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that it is not obligatory due to the lack of valid recitation and the absence of discernment. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: he heard it from a sleeper; it was said it is obligatory, but the correct view is that it is not obligatory. In al-Khaniyya, the correct view is that it is obligatory. In al-Khulasa: he heard it from a bird — it is not obligatory, that is the chosen view. And from a sleeper, the correct view is that it is obligatory, and the same is in Qadi Khan. And if he reports that he recited it in his sleep, it is obligatory upon him, and this is the most correct. In al-Diraya: it is not necessary; that is the correct view. And the recitation of a drunk person is obligatory upon him. In it, his statement: 'this is according to the two' – and it is narrated that he (Abu Hanifa) retracted to their view, and upon it reliance, as in al-Jawhara. His statement: 'and it is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa' – i.e., according to the view he retracted from regarding the permissibility of prayer with it, whether he is proficient in Arabic or not, so it is Qur'an from all aspects, so it is obligatory. As for the view he retracted to, it is like their view, so the prostration is not obligatory except with understanding, because it is Qur'an from one aspect (meaning) but not from the other (wording). So if he understood, he is hearing the Qur'an from one aspect, so it is obligatory as a precaution. His statement: 'if he is informed that it is a verse of prostration' – but if he is not informed, it is not obligatory, because there is no obligation without knowledge or its evidence. And it is understood from this that according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), both understanding and being informed are required. His statement: 'or a madman' – in al-Dhakhira, in Nawadir al-Salah, it is mentioned that if the madness is short, i.e., a day and night or less, the prostration is obligatory upon him by recitation and hearing during the state of madness, and he performs it after recovery because he is eligible for makeup. Al-Muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Haj said: There is consideration in this; rather, the correct view is that nothing is obligatory upon the madman if he hears or recites in a state of madness absolutely, whether short or continuous, because he is not in a better state than the sleeper and the unconscious person, and they are not obligated by either action in either state, so this is the same. His statement: 'he heard it from a bird — it is not obligatory' – it is better to delay this sentence to the place of the author's upcoming statement 'and it is not obligatory by hearing it from a bird' and to make it a proof for it. His statement: 'and if he reports, etc.' – this is an additional issue beyond what is in the matn, intended to alert to the ruling regarding the sleeper when he recites. His statement: 'and the recitation of a drunk is obligatory upon him' – Al-Muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Haj said: It should be said, based on what appears from this reasoning, that the obligation is specific to a drunk from a prohibited source, not from a permissible one, such as if he choked on a morsel and found nothing to swallow it except wine, and feared destruction of his life if he did not swallow it, so he drank only enough to swallow it, and became drunk from that, or he was compelled to drink by legal compulsion, and then recited in a state of drunkenness, and he did not have the capacity to distinguish what he says and hears such that he does not remember it after sobriety, then it is not obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya addresses sajdat al-tilawa in cases involving Persian recitation, hearing from a sleeper, madman, bird, or drunkard. The core issue is the status of Persian when reciting the Qur'an: Abu Hanifa initially held that Persian is Qur'an from all aspects (meaning and wording), making sajdat al-tilawa obligatory even without understanding, as long as one is informed it is a verse of prostration. However, he later retracted to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, who consider Persian Qur'an from one aspect (meaning) but not the wording, so obligation depends on understanding. The relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is the later position of Abu Hanifa agreeing with the two, requiring understanding for obligation. For hearing from a sleeper or madman, the text reports multiple narrations: some say obligatory, others not. The preferred view according to Shaykh al-Islam and Al-Tahtawi is that it is not obligatory because the recitation is not valid (due to lack of discernment). However, if a sleeper reports that he recited in his sleep, the most correct view is that it is obligatory upon the listener. For hearing from a bird, it is not obligatory. The drunkard's recitation is generally obligatory, but Al-Tahtawi's commentary qualifies that if the drunkenness resulted from a permissible cause (e.g., necessity) and the person had no awareness, it may not be obligatory. The passage demonstrates the nuanced nature of ijtihad within the Hanafi school, with a clear tarjih towards the later position of Abu Hanifa aligning with his two disciples.

Key Terms
الفارسية (al-farisiyya): The Persian language; used for reciting or translating the Qur'an. The dispute is whether such recitation is considered Qur'an in full or only in meaning.
النوم (al-nawm): Sleep; a state that affects the validity of recitation. Recitation from a sleeper is not considered valid for the purpose of obligating sajdat al-tilawa because there is no discernment.
السكران (al-sakran): A drunk person; his recitation obligates sajdat al-tilawa on the listener unless the drunkenness was from a permissible cause and he had no awareness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in the passage, when is sajdat al-tilawa obligatory upon hearing Persian recitation?
A) Always, regardless of understanding or information.
B) Only if the listener understands the meaning.
C) Only if the reciter is a known pious person.
D) Never, because Persian is not Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: sajdat al-tilawa from Persian recitation requires understanding; from a sleeper or madman, it is not obligatory due to invalid recitation; from a drunk, it is generally obligatory unless the intoxication was from a permissible cause without awareness.

Sajda al-Tilawah upon Hearing Persian Recitation
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sajda al-tilawah upon hearing Persian recitation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Persian recitation obligates sajda only if understood, per the relied-upon position.

The obligation of sajda al-tilawah depends on the nature of the recitation. When the Qur'an is recited in Persian, a dispute arises: is it considered Qur'an in every respect or only in meaning? This affects whether understanding is required. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi internal disagreement and the final relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states that sajda is obligatory upon hearing Persian recitation 'if he understands it' (إن فهمها). This is the relied-upon position.
Note the qualifier 'on the relied-upon' (على المعتمد) – this indicates tarjih.
2
State the opposing view of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa holds that understanding is not required – obligation arises if the listener is merely informed that it is an ayah of sajda.
His view is based on considering Persian as Qur'an in all respects.
3
Understand the basis of the dispute
The dispute hinges on whether Persian is Qur'an 'from every angle' or 'from one angle' (meaning vs. wording).
The Sahibayn consider it Qur'an only in meaning, hence understanding is needed.
4
Note the tarjih
The commentator indicates that Abu Hanifa later retracted (روى رجوعه إليهما) and the relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn.
Thus, the mufta bihi is that understanding is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصحيح (وتجب) السجدة (بسماع) القراءة باللغة الفارسية إن فهمها على المعتمد وهذا عندهما ويجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة وإن لم يفهم معناها إذا أخبر بأنها آية سجدة، ومبنى الخلاف على أن الفارسية قرآن من كل وجه أو من وجه وإذا فهم تجب احتياطاً واختلف التصحيح في وجوبها على السامع بالسماع من نائم أو مجنون ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنه لا يجب لعدم صحة التلاوة وبفقد التمييز، وفي التترخانية سمعها من نائم قيل تجب والصحيح أنها لا تجب، وفي الخانية الصحيح هو الوجوب، وفي الخلاصة سمعها من طير لا تجب هو المختار ومن نائم الصحيح أنها تجب ومثله في قاضيخان، وإذا أخبر أنه قرأها في نومه تجب عليه وهو الأصح وفي الدراية لا يلزمه هو الصحيح وقراءة السكران موجبة عليه
The correct position: the prostration is obligatory upon hearing the recitation in the Persian language if he understands it, according to the relied-upon position. This is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And according to Abu Hanifa, it is obligatory upon him even if he does not understand its meaning, if he is informed that it is a verse of prostration. The basis of the dispute is whether Persian is the Qur'an in every respect or in one respect. If he understands, it is obligatory as a precaution. There is disagreement in correction regarding its obligation upon the listener when hearing from a sleeping or insane person. Shaykh al-Islam stated that it is not obligatory due to the lack of valid recitation and loss of discernment. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: he heard it from a sleeping person; it was said it is obligatory, but the correct view is that it is not obligatory. In al-Khaniyya: the correct view is obligation. In al-Khulasa: he heard it from a bird; it is not obligatory, that is the chosen view; and from a sleeping person, the correct view is that it is obligatory, and similar is in Qadikhan. If he informed that he recited it in his sleep, it is obligatory upon him, and that is the most sound. In al-Diraya: it is not incumbent upon him; that is the correct view. And the recitation of a drunk person makes it obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) when hearing the Qur'an in Persian and also when hearing from a sleeping or insane person, from a bird, or when the reciter is drunk. The author begins by stating the relied-upon position that if one hears the Persian recitation and understands it, the sajda is obligatory. This is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani). However, Abu Hanifa held that even if one does not understand, it becomes obligatory if informed that it is a verse of prostration. The dispute hinges on whether the Persian translation is considered Qur'an in all respects (both meaning and wording) or only in meaning. According to the two (Sahibayn), it is Qur'an only in meaning, hence understanding is required; Abu Hanifa initially considered it Qur'an in all respects, thus obligation even without understanding. The author then notes that if one understands, the obligation is precautionary. The passage then discusses the case of hearing from a sleeping or insane person. There are conflicting reports: some works say it is not obligatory because the recitation is not valid (due to lack of intention or sanity), while others say it is obligatory. The author cites various authorities: in al-Tatarkhaniyya, the correct view is that it is not obligatory; in al-Khaniyya, it is obligatory; in al-Khulasa, hearing from a bird is not obligatory (chosen view), but hearing from a sleeping person is obligatory (according to the correct view). The passage also covers the case where the sleeper himself recited in his sleep: if he is informed, it is obligatory (most sound view), but in al-Diraya it is not incumbent. Finally, the recitation of a drunk person obligates the sajda upon the drunk himself because he has the capacity to intend (unlike a sleeper or insane person). The drunk's recitation is considered valid for obligation.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration that is wajib upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Qur'an that contains a command for prostration.
فارسية (fārisiyyah): The Persian language; here it refers to a translation of the Qur'an into Persian.
آية سجدة (āyat sajdah): A verse of the Qur'an that requires prostration upon recitation or hearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is required for sajda al-tilawah to be wajib upon hearing a Persian recitation?
A) The reciter must be a Muslim.
B) The listener must understand the meaning.
C) The recitation must be loud.
D) The listener must be informed that it is a sajda verse.

Key Takeaway
Sajda al-tilawah upon hearing Persian recitation is wajib only if the listener understands the meaning, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Sajda al-Tilawah from Unconventional Reciters
Collection of rulings on various reciters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the differing rulings on sajda al-tilawah when the recitation comes from a sleeping, insane, bird, or drunk person, and apply the Hanafi tarjih principles to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A valid recitation for sajda requires a sane, awake human reciter; exceptions exist but are contested.

The obligation of sajda al-tilawah depends not only on the language but also on the state of the reciter. Can a sleeping person's recitation obligate? What about an insane person, a bird, or a drunk? The Hanafi texts contain conflicting answers. This lesson navigates the various reports and identifies the relied-upon positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle from Shaykh al-Islam
Shaykh al-Islam states that sajda is not obligatory when hearing from a sleeping or insane person because the recitation is not valid (عدم صحة التلاوة) and discernment is absent (بفقد التمييز).
This suggests a condition: the reciter must be legally capable (mukallaf) and the recitation must be valid.
2
List the conflicting reports
The passage then cites several works: al-Tatarkhaniyya says the correct view is it is not obligatory; al-Khaniyya says it is obligatory; al-Khulasa says from a bird it is not obligatory, but from a sleeping person it is obligatory; Qadikhan agrees.
Note that 'correct' (الصحيح) is used differently in different sources.
3
Analyze the sleeper's own recitation
If a sleeping person recites a sajda verse in his sleep and is informed later, the most sound view (الأصح) is that sajda becomes obligatory upon him. However, al-Diraya states the opposite: it is not incumbent.
This shows a dispute even when the reciter is the same person after waking.
4
Examine the drunk's recitation
The passage ends with a clear rule: the recitation of a drunk person (قراءة السكران) does obligate sajda upon him.
Unlike the sleeper or insane person, the drunk still has some capacity (he is not to the point of losing discernment entirely, according to Hanafi definition).
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi
Despite conflicting reports, the stronger principle is that valid recitation requires a sane, aware reciter. Thus, hearing from a sleeping or insane person does not obligate (following Shaykh al-Islam and al-Tatarkhaniyya), while the drunk's recitation does obligate.
The bird's case is unanimous: no obligation because the bird is not a responsible being.

This is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And according to Abu Hanifa, it is obligatory upon him even if he does not understand its meaning, if he is informed that it is a verse of prostration. Commentary

Key Terms
صحة التلاوة (ṣiḥḥat al-tilāwah): Validity of recitation; the condition that the recitation be performed with intention and awareness.
فقد التمييز (faqd al-tamyīz): Loss of discernment; refers to a state where one lacks the ability to distinguish meaning, e.g., sleep or insanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on sajda al-tilawah when hearing from a drunk person?
A) It is not obligatory because the drunk lacks intention.
B) It is obligatory.

D) It depends on whether the drunk understood what he recited.

Key Takeaway
Hearing a sajda verse from a sleeping or insane person generally does not obligate sajda due to invalid recitation, but from a drunk it does; hearing from a bird never obligates.
