Sajda al-Tilawah: Obligation from Non-Human Sources and Performance in Prayer
Rulings on sajda al-tilawah from non-human sources and performance in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when hearing a sajda verse from a bird or echo does not obligate prostration, and explain how to perform the sajda in prayer using a separate ruku'/sujud or the prayer's own ruku' with intention.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajda verse from a bird or echo does not obligate prostration; the prayer's own ruku' can fulfill the sajda if intended.

This passage continues the discussion of sajda al-tilawah, focusing on two areas: when hearing from non-human sources (bird, echo) triggers obligation, and how to integrate the sajda within the prayer itself. The author clarifies that only valid human recitation with intention obligates, while sounds from birds, parrots, or echoes do not. Then, practical guidance is given: in prayer, one can perform a separate ruku' or sujud, or even use the prayer's own ruku' if intending the sajda, which is recommended for large congregations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exceptions to obligation
From the first part of the passage, list the cases where hearing a sajda verse does not obligate sajda: from a bird (on the correct view), from a trained parrot (similar dispute), and from an echo. Note the reasoning: lack of valid recitation (qira'ah) and hearing (sama').
The phrase 'على الصحيح' indicates the relied-upon view within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the ikhtilaf on bird and parrot
Recognize that some scholars consider hearing from a bird/parrot as obligatory because 'he heard the speech of Allah'. The author sides with the non-obligation view based on the principle that the sound is not actual recitation.
The source mentions 'في الحجة هو الصحيح' which suggests a different strength; but the mufta bihi is non-obligation.
3
Analyze the echo ruling
Echo is defined as the reflection of one's own voice. Since it is not an independent recitation, hearing it does not obligate sajda. This is stated unequivocally.
No ikhtilaf is mentioned for echo.
4
Explore performance options in prayer
The passage explains that sajda al-tilawah in prayer can be performed by either a separate ruku' or sujud, or by the prayer's own ruku' if intended. Separate sujud is better as it combines form and meaning; ruku' alone covers only meaning. Also, if reciting consecutively, it is recommended to recite additional verses before bowing to avoid building ruku' on prostration.
The recommendation for the imam to use the prayer's ruku' is for convenience in large congregations.
5
Grasp the substitution ruling (ruku' of prayer suffices)
Imam Muhammad explicitly stated that the ruku' of the prayer can substitute for sajda al-tilawah if the worshiper intends it, because the essence of both is glorification (ta'zim). This is a qiyas based on the common meaning.
This is a distinctive Hanafi leniency, not found in all schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى السامع والأبكم والأصم وكاتب السجدة لا تجب برؤية من سجد والكتابة لعدم التلاوة والسماع ولا تجب سجدة التلاوة بسماعها من الطير على الصحيح، وقيل: تجب وفي الحجة هو الصحيح لأنه سمع كلام الله وكذا الخلاف بسماعها من القدر المعلم، ولا تجب بسماعها من الصدى وهو ما يجيبك مثل صوتك في الجبال والصحاري، ونحوها وتؤدى بركوع أو سجود كائنين في الصلاة غير ركوع الصلاة و غير سجودها والسجود أفضل لأنه تحصيل قربتين صورة الواجب ومعناه وبالركوع المعنى وهو الخضوع وإذا كانت آخر تلاوته ينبغي أن يقرأ، ولو آيتين من سورة آخرى بعد قيامه منها حتى لا يصير بانياً الركوع على السجود ولو ركع بمجرد قيامه منها كره ويجزى عنها أي عن سجدة التلاوة ركوع الصلاة إن نواها أي نوى أداءها فيه نص عليه محمد لأن معنى التعظيم فيهما واحد، وينبغي ذلك للإمام مع كثرة القوم أو حال المخافتة حتى لا يؤدي إلى التخليط و يجزي السجدة
And upon the listener, the deaf, the mute, and the writer of the sajda, it is not obligatory by seeing one who prostrates or by writing, due to lack of recitation and hearing. And sajda al-tilawah is not obligatory when hearing it from a bird, according to the correct view; and it is said: it is obligatory, and in al-Hujja it is the correct view because he heard the speech of Allah. Similarly, there is dispute regarding hearing it from a trained parrot. And it is not obligatory when hearing it from an echo, which is what responds to you like your voice in mountains and deserts and the like. And it is performed by bowing or prostrating that occur in prayer, other than the bowing and prostration of the prayer itself; and prostration is better because it achieves two closenesses: the form of the obligatory and its meaning, and by bowing only the meaning (which is humility). And if it is the end of his recitation, he should recite, even if two verses from another surah after standing from it, so that he does not become one who builds the bowing upon the prostration. And if he bows immediately upon standing from it, it is disliked. And the bowing of the prayer suffices for it (i.e., for sajda al-tilawah) if he intends it, i.e., he intends to perform it in the bowing; this is explicitly stated by Muhammad, because the meaning of glorification is the same in both. And this is recommended for the imam when there are many people or when reciting quietly, so that it does not lead to confusion. And the prostration also suffices.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of sajda al-tilawah, focusing on its obligation when hearing from non-human sources and its performance in prayer. The author states that the sajda is not obligatory upon a listener who is deaf or mute, nor upon one who sees someone else prostrate or writes the verse, because there is no recitation or hearing. Regarding hearing from a bird, the correct view is that it is not obligatory, though some say it is obligatory because the sound is still the speech of Allah. Similarly, hearing from a trained parrot (القدر المعلم) is disputed. Hearing from an echo does not obligate because it is merely a reflection of one's own voice. The passage then explains how to perform the sajda in prayer: one can perform a ruku' or sujud separate from the prayer's own ruku' and sujud, but prostration is superior because it combines the form and meaning of worship. If one's recitation ends with the sajda verse, it is recommended to recite two additional verses from another surah before bowing to avoid building the ruku' directly on the sajda. If one bows immediately, it is disliked. Importantly, the ruku' of the prayer itself can substitute for the sajda al-tilawah if the worshiper intends it to do so, because both express glorification of Allah. This was explicitly stated by Imam Muhammad. This substitution is recommended for an imam when the congregation is large or when reciting quietly to avoid disorder.

Key Terms
الصدى (as-ṣadā): Echo; reflection of one's own voice.
القدر المعلم (al-qudru al-muʿallam): A trained parrot that imitates human speech.
ركوع الصلاة (rukūʿ aṣ-ṣalāh): The bowing in salah, which can substitute for sajda al-tilawah if intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for hearing a sajda verse from an echo?
A) Obligatory
B) Not obligatory
C) Obligatory only if one repeats the verse
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Sajda al-tilawah is only obligatory from valid human recitation; echoes, birds, and parrots do not trigger obligation, and the prayer's ruku' can substitute if intended.

When Sajdah al-Tilawah Is Not Obligatory – Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Explaining who is not obligated for Sajdah al-Tilawah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on non-obligation of Sajdah al-Tilawah for a listener, mute, deaf, writer, and when hearing from a bird or echo, and apply the qiyas reasoning that imitation does not constitute recitation.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Tilawah is not wajib if the sound is imitation, not genuine recitation.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies the boundaries of obligation for Sajdah al-Tilawah. The matn lists several persons (listener, mute, deaf, writer) and situations (seeing prostration, writing, hearing from a bird or echo) where the sajdah is not required. The commentary provides the rational basis (dalil aqli): the bird's sound is mere imitation (muhakah), lacking discernment and intention, thus not considered legitimate recitation. We will walk through the categories and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of non-obligation
From the matn, note the four persons (listener, mute, deaf, writer) and two actions (seeing prostration, writing). Also note the additional cases: hearing from a bird, from a trained monkey, and from an echo. All these are situations where sajdah is not wajib.
The hashiya explains grammatical connections: 'by seeing' refers to mute and deaf; 'and writing' to the writer.
2
Find the common cause ('illa) for non-obligation
The text explicitly states the cause: 'due to lack of recitation and hearing'. For the bird, echo, and monkey, the commentator explains they are imitation, not actual recitation, because the sound lacks discernment (tamyiz). The effective cause for obligation is hearing the Quran recited with intention and understanding.
The opposing opinion (some say it is obligatory from a bird) is mentioned but rejected because the sound is not true recitation.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas) for the bird case
The bird's sound is compared to an echo: both are mere imitations of the human voice. Since an echo does not obligate sajdah, similarly, the bird's sound does not. The proof is qiyas based on the absence of genuine recitation or hearing.
The hashiya references al-Jawhara and al-Mudmarat for the trained monkey analogy.
4
Locate the Hanafi preferred position
The text states 'upon the correct view (al-mukhtar)' that sajdah is not obligatory from a bird. The author al-Tahtawi endorses this as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. The intra-Hanafi difference (some say it is wajib) is resolved by tarjih.
The authority weight is from the later Hanafi masters (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى السامع والأبكم والأصم وكاتب السجدة لا تجب برؤية من سجد والكتابة لعدم التلاوة والسماع ولا تجب سجدة التلاوة (بسماعها من الطير) على الصحيح، وقيل: تجب وفي الحجة هو الصحيح لأنه سمع كلام الله وكذا الخلاف بسماعها من القدر المعلم، ولا تجب بسماعها من الصدى وهو ما يجيبك مثل صوتك في الجبال والصحاري، ونحوها قوله : ( والأبكم) هو وما عطف عليه مبتدأ وقوله لا تجب خبر، والأولى زيادة عليهم قوله برؤية من سجد) يرجع إلى الأبكم والأصم وقوله : والكتابة بالجر عطف على قوله : برؤية وهو يرجع إلى كاتب السجدة قوله : (لعدم التلاوة والسماع) علة لعدم الوجوب عليهم. قوله : ( على الصحيح) وهو المختار لأنها محاكاة، وليست بقراءة لعدم التمييز وكذا يقال في القرد المعلم كما في الجوهرة والمضمرات قوله من الصدى) بوزن حصى. قوله: (وهو ما يجيبك الخ) الأولى قول بعضهم الصوت الذي يسمعه المصوت عقب صياحه راجعاً إليه من جبل، أو بناء مرتفع اهـ فإنه لا إجابة في الصدى وإنما هو محاكاة.
And upon the listener, the mute, the deaf, and the writer of the prostration, it (the sajdah) is not obligatory by seeing someone who prostrates or by writing, due to lack of recitation and hearing. And the sajdah of recitation is not obligatory (by hearing it from a bird) upon the correct view. And it is said: it is obligatory, and in al-Hujja, the correct view is that it is obligatory because he heard the speech of Allah. And likewise the difference regarding hearing it from a trained monkey. And it is not obligatory by hearing it from an echo, which is what responds to you like your voice in mountains and deserts and the like. His statement: (And the mute) he and what is conjoined to him are a mubtada, and his statement 'it is not obligatory' is the khabar, and it is better to increase upon them his statement 'by seeing someone who prostrates' refers to the mute and the deaf, and his statement 'and writing' in genitive is conjoined to his statement 'by seeing' and it refers to the writer of the sajdah. His statement: (due to lack of recitation and hearing) is the cause for non-obligation upon them. His statement: (upon the correct view) and it is the chosen one because it is imitation, and not recitation due to lack of discernment, and likewise it is said regarding the trained monkey as in al-Jawhara and al-Mudmarat. His statement: 'from the echo' with the weight of hasa. His statement: 'which is what responds to you etc.' The first is the saying of some: the sound that the one who cries hears after his cry returning to him from a mountain or high building, for indeed there is no response in the echo, rather it is imitation.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the obligation of Sajdah al-Tilawah. The matn states that the listener, mute, deaf, and writer of the sajdah are not obligated by seeing someone prostrate or by writing, because they did not recite or hear. The hashiya explains the grammatical structure and clarifies that the obligation is tied to actual recitation or hearing. Regarding hearing from a bird, the correct view (al-mukhtar) is that sajdah is not obligatory because the bird's sound is mere imitation, not considered recitation. The same applies to a trained monkey. Hearing from an echo also does not obligate sajdah for the same reason. The hashiya quotes various sources to support this rational argument (dalil aqli). The commentary also clarifies that the echo is not a real response but an acoustic imitation.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration of recitation performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration.
الصدى (al-sada): The echo that returns the voice as an imitation, not a real response.
محاكاة (muhakah): Imitation; the bird's sound that mimics human speech without understanding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, why is Sajdah al-Tilawah not obligatory when hearing it from an echo?
A) Because the echo is weaker in volume.
B) Because the echo is not a living being.
C) Because the echo is imitation, not genuine recitation.
D) Because the echo does not originate from a human.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Tilawah is only wajib when the sound heard is genuine Quranic recitation; imitation sounds (bird, echo, trained monkey) do not trigger the obligation.
